1601 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Dallas County Flood Control Dist. No. 1 v. Cross


No. 05-90-00582-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


815 S.W.2d 271; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2286



July 15, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 11, 1991. Writ of Error Denied December 11, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 193rd District Court; Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 87-2949-L.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant flood control district sought review of a judgment from the 193rd District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which , upon remand, was in favor of appellee former presiding officer on appellant's conflict-of-interest claim concerning two real estate purchases.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted judgment in favor of appellee former presiding officer, upon remand from the court. The court reversed and rendered a declaratory judgment that appellant flood control district could rescind two permanent easement transactions and recover the purchase prices paid. The court concluded that the purchase of one permanent easement from appellee was voidable because the votes of two of appellant's directors violated the applicable conflict-of-interest statute and the agreement could not have been approved without their affirmative votes. The court concluded that appellant's acquisition of another easement from appellee violated the Texas Open Meetings Act, and rendered the transaction voidable by appellant. The attempt by appellant's board of directors to ratify the transaction was ineffective. The court held that the suit involved the exercise of a governmental function and concluded that appellant was not estopped to deny the enforceability of a settlement agreement approved by its board of directors. The court also concluded that public policy barred appellee from asserting equitable estoppel because he was a knowing beneficiary of the illegal transaction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment granted in favor of appellee former presiding officer and rendered a declaratory judgment for appellant flood control district because the purchases of two easements from appellee were voidable by appellant.

Cardenas v. State


NO. 01-91-00431-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3176



July 11, 1991, Delivered  
July 11, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 180th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 594,706



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 180th District Court, Harris County (Texas), that denied appellant's request to further reduce appellant's bail.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with possession of marijuana in a useable quantity of more than 50 and less than 200 pounds. Appellant's request to further reduce bail was denied. The court reversed and reduced appellant's bail from $ 50,000 to $ 10,000. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 17.151, § 1 provided for the mandatory reduction of bail because appellant was incarcerated for more than 90 days and the state was not ready to proceed to trial. The court considered the $ 50,000 bail excessive because appellant had a low paying job and no assets or property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order denying further bail reduction and reduced appellant's bail from $ 50,000 to $ 10,000 because appellant was incarcerated for more than 90 days and the state was not ready to proceed to trial.

 

1603 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


King v. State


No. 05-86-00461-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


816 S.W.2d 447; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 2516



June 27, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 16, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 1; Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. MB85-42610-A.



DISPOSITION: Reversed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the County Criminal Court No. 1, Dallas County (Texas) for driving while intoxicated (DWI). On original submission, the court sustained appellant's first point of error, reversed the trial court's judgment, and remanded for a new trial. Thereafter, the criminal appellate court ordered reconsideration of all points of error in light of changes in the law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for driving while intoxicated (DWI). He urged that the placement of a roadblock at the target site where he was arrested violated his constitutional rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 9, and that the trial court erred when it overruled his motion to suppress evidence that was seized at the roadblock. The court found that while Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. art. 6687(b), § 13 allowed police to stop and detain a motorist for a driver's license check, it did not validate the stopping an automobile if it was not clear that the reason for the detention was to check licenses. The court determined from the evidence that the purpose of the roadblock was to catch drunk drivers and that appellant was not detained pursuant to a routine driver's license check authorized by the statute. The court held that because Texas did not have a legislatively developed administrative scheme for sobriety checkpoints, the DWI roadblock at issue was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 9. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court sustained appellant's first and second points of error finding that the trial court erred in overruling his motion to suppress evidence seized at the roadblock where he was arrested, reversed the trial court's judgment, and remanded for a new trial holding that the roadblock was unconstitutional in that it violated U.S. Const. amend. IV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 9.

 

1604 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Gutierrez v. Lee


No. 3-90-208-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


812 S.W.2d 388; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1592



June 26, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] Released for Publication August 14, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Overruled August 14, 1991. Writ of Error Denied December 11, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District No. 454,354, Honorable Jerry Dellana, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insolvent savings and loan association and liquidator sought review of the judgment declaring that a federal suit filed by appellee IRA depositors tolled the limitations in the Savings and Loan Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 852a (Supp. 1991), in the suit brought by appellees in the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District (Texas) to obtain priority for their deposits.


OVERVIEW: Seeking priority, appellee IRA depositors timely filed suit in federal court after appellant liquidator determined their accounts in appellant insolvent savings and loan association were not entitled to priority. While that suit was pending, appellees filed under the Savings and Loan Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 852a (Supp. 1991) (Act), asking the same relief. Appellants asked that a class suit be designated and counterclaimed for a decision, under the Declaratory Judgment Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 37.001-37.011 (1986 and Supp. 1991), that the suit was untimely. Reversing the trial court's decision that the federal suit tolled the three-month limitations period, the court noted that § 8.09(f) of the Act established the procedures for appealing claim decisions. Finding § 8.09(f) jurisdictional, and constitutional under Tex. Const. art. I, § 13, the court held that appellees were required to file within three months in the state district court, and the federal suit did not toll the statute. The court noted that § 8.09(f) applied to statutory rights to appeal appellant liquidator's decision.


OUTCOME: Reversing the trial court's decision that a federal suit did not toll the three-month limitations in the Savings and Loan Act, the court remanded the case brought by appellee IRA depositors to have their claims given priority by appellant insolvent savings and loan association and liquidator. The court found that the limitations period was jurisdictional and constitutional.

 

1605 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Edwards v. State


Nos. 05-89-00946-CR, 05-89-00947-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


813 S.W.2d 572; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1977



June 25, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 16, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 292nd Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause Nos. F89-78153-LV; F89-78152-MV.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of their convictions for possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, which were entered after a jury trial in the 292nd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas). Appellants claimed that the evidence was insufficient to link them to the cocaine seized in an apartment, and that the confidential informant should have been identified under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 508.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sought review of their convictions of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver after a jury trial. Appellants claimed that no evidence affirmatively linked them to the cocaine seized in an apartment pursuant to a search warrant obtained on information from a confidential informant. The police found cocaine and weapons in the apartment, but no documents and they did not check for fingerprints. Rejecting appellants' complaints of hearsay under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 801(d), the court ruled that the unobjected-to officers' testimony that the manager said appellants lived in the apartment, together with one appellant's provision of that address when asked after their arrest, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.21 (1979), were sufficient to permit the jury to find both of them exercised control over the apartment. The court emphasized that the drugs were in plain view and were conveniently accessible to appellants, who controlled the apartment where the drugs were found. The court added that Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 508 did not require identification of the confidential informant because it was neither relevant nor helpful.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellants' convictions for possession of cocaine with intent to deliver after a jury trial, explaining that there was sufficient evidence linking appellants to the cocaine in that it was in plain view, conveniently accessible to them, and they controlled the place where the cocaine was found. The court also found that the confidential informant's identity was neither relevant nor helpful.

 

1606 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re S.D.W.


No. 01-89-00238-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


811 S.W.2d 739; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1568



June 20, 1991, Delivered  
June 20, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 1; Brazos County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 141-J-88CC; Claude D. Davis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and remanded in part, affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile contested the determination from the County Court at Law, Brazos County, Texas, that he engaged in delinquent conduct by committing murder and aggravated robbery, and the sentence of nine years' confinement under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 54.04(d)(3) (Supp. 1991) for murder, and an indeterminate period for robbery, under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 54.04(d)(2) (Supp. 1991). Appellant contended the determinate sentence was erroneous.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court reversed appellant juvenile's nine year sentence for murder because the record did not contain anything indicating that prosecution of appellant was affirmatively approved by a grand jury, as required by Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 53.045 (Supp. 1991). Yet it affirmed the indeterminate sentence for aggravated robbery, and remanded the murder allegation for imposition of an indeterminate sentence. The court held that the amended petitions should have been presented to the grand jury, and that a prosecutor's oral representations of approval by a grand jury was not a certification. Without certification, the trial court was without jurisdiction to impose a determinate sentence. Thus, the court reformed the judgment, and remanded. Because appellant and his mother were properly served with the original petition, the trial court had acquired jurisdiction over him. Thus, the state's failure to serve appellant with the second amended petition did not deprive the trial court of jurisdiction. Appellant had not preserved any other alleged errors for review. Thus, the trial court did not err in failing to include jury instructions. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court held that it had jurisdiction over appellant juvenile, and affirmed the determinations as to murder and aggravated robbery. The court affirmed the indeterminate murder sentence, but reversed and remanded for reformation as to the determinate sentence for the robbery, holding that there was no showing that the grand jury had pre-approved the imposition of a determinate sentence, which was statutorily required.

 

1607 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Cotton v. State


No. 01-90-00509-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1573



June 20, 1991, Delivered  
June 20, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused as Untimely Filed October 2, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 184th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 548,504. 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for possession of less than 28 grams of cocaine from the 184th District Court, Harris County (Texas), contending that the trial court committed reversible error by not admonishing him that his plea of guilty would subject him to the possibility of deportation, and that his conviction under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (1977) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for possession of cocaine after entering a guilty plea, on the grounds that reversible error occurred when the trial court failed to admonish him that his plea would subject him to deportation proceedings, and that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.15 (1977) was unconstitutional because he was denied the right to present evidence on his own behalf. On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's conviction because the record was ambiguous and failed to demonstrate that appellant was not a U.S. citizen. Absent that showing, the trial court's failure to address the citizenship issue was not reversible error. The court held that art. 1.15 neither prohibited appellant from offering, or the trial court from receiving and considering, evidence offered by appellant, nor did the article violate due process or equal protection. The court found that there was no requirement, in the state or federal constitutions, for a specific, express waiver of the right to compulsory process.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for possession of cocaine was affirmed because there was nothing in the record that demonstrated failure of required arraignment procedures. Absent a showing by appellant that he was not a U.S. citizen, the trial court's failure to address the citizenship issue in the admonishment was not reversible error. The court found no constitutional requirement for a specific waiver of the right to compulsory process.

PUC OF TEXAS v. GTE-SW


No. 3-90-084-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


833 S.W.2d 153; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1579



June 19, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn April 1, 1992; Substituted Opinion of April 1, 1992, Reported at 1992 Tex. App. LEXIS 1005.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District; No. 406,115, Honorable Joseph H. Hart, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, Reversed and Remanded in Part with Instructions


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Public Utility Commission and other officials, and appellee utility company attacked portions of a decision by appellant commission to order appellee to lower its rates. Parties raised issues regarding the use of double leverage method and diminished-risk adjustment, the determinations of payments to affiliates and federal tax liability in calculation of operating expenses, and the effective date of rate change.


OVERVIEW: The court reviewed a judgment regarding the decision of appellant Public Utility Commission to order appellee utility company to reduce its rates. The court affirmed the portion of the judgment reversing appellant commission's order and reversed the judgment to the extent it affirmed appellant commission's order. The court held that appellant commission did not abuse its discretion in employing the double leverage method in arriving at an opinion of appellee's cost of capital and in making a diminished-risk adjustment. However, the court held that appellant commission erroneously included payments to affiliates in calculating the necessary and reasonable operating expenses without making the required findings under Public Utility Regulatory Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1446c, § 41(c)(1) (Supp. 1991). Additionally, the court held that appellant commission's findings regarding appellee's federal income tax liability did not conform to § 41 (c)(2). Finally, the court held that appellant commission was precluded from making effective date at a date earlier than that of its final order. The court ordered that the action be remanded generally back to appellant commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment to the extent that it reversed appellant commission's order and reversed the judgment to the extent that it affirmed the order. The court approved the use of the double leverage method and diminished-risk but found errors in the calculation of operating expenses with regard to payments to affiliates and federal tax liability and in the setting of effective date. The court ordered action to be remanded.

 

1609 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Guerrero


No. 13-90-490-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


811 S.W.2d 726; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1562



June 18, 1991, Delivered  
June 18, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 103rd District Court of Cameron County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 103rd District Court of Cameron County, Texas, which denied her application for writ of habeas corpus, which was premised on the theory that Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.126 (1991) was void for vagueness because it failed to define "finance," "invest," and "funds."


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted under the Controlled Substances Act for the offense of illegal investment, under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.126 (1991), alleging that she intentionally and knowingly financed and invested funds to further the commission of the offense of aggravated possession of marihuana. Appellant filed an application for writ of habeas corpus, claiming that the indictment was based on a constitutionally invalid statute because it failed to define the terms "finance," "invest," and "funds." The trial court denied relief. Appellant challenged the decision. The court affirmed, holding that by applying common dictionary definitions to the terms "finance," "invest," and "funds," § 481.126 clearly proscribed a person from supplying money which the person knew was intended to further the possession of marihuana. The court found that a person of common intelligence could determine with reasonable precision what conduct was prohibited by the statute and that the statute provided sufficient notice to law enforcement personnel to prevent arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of relief, holding that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague because a person of common intelligence could understand what was meant by "funds," "invest," and "finance" and could determine what conduct was prohibited.

Nash v. State


No. B14-90-01106-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


811 S.W.2d 698; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1488



June 13, 1991, Rendered  
June 13, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled July 11, 1991. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Denied October 16, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 174th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 476732-A; George Goodwin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surety challenged the order of the 174th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which ordered a partial forfeiture of the bail bond in a criminal matter involving the felony offense of manufacture of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Appellee state charged appellant principal with the felony offense of manufacture of a controlled substance. He posted an appearance bond. Appellant surety signed the bond, and principal was released from custody. Appellant principal then failed to appear at the arraignment hearing. An interlocutory judgment of forfeiture was entered, and appellant surety filed an answer and sought a remittitur. Appellant principal was later arrested out-of-state but released from custody because a governor's warrant from Texas had not been issued. The trial court ordered a partial forfeiture of the appearance bond. Appellant surety sought review, arguing that the trial court erred in failing to remit the entire amount of the bond under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 22.16(a). On appeal, the court affirmed because remittitur was at the trial court's discretion at anytime between forfeiture and entry of the final judgment.


OUTCOME: The partial forfeiture of the bail bond against appellant surety was affirmed because remittitur was at the discretion of the trial court at anytime between forfeiture and the entry of the final judgment.

Smith v. State


No. C14-90-00449-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


811 S.W.2d 665; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1425



June 6, 1991, Rendered  
June 6, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled July 11, 1991. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused as Untimely Filed October 2, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 8,903,944; Sherman A. Ross, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of obscenity in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10, Harris County (Texas), arguing that the complaint was defective, that there was insufficient evidence to convict, that the jury charge was improper, and that an incorrect community standard was applied.


OVERVIEW: An undercover officer purchased magazines from appellant in an adult bookstore. Appellant was charged with and convicted of obscenity. Appellant sought review, arguing that the complaint and information were defective since the affiant failed to allege personal knowledge of the criminal conduct, the signatures on the affidavit were illegible, the description of the obscene material was ambiguous, and the alleged criminal acts were not charged to be obscene. Appellant also argued that the evidence at trial was insufficient to show appellant sold the magazines and knew of their content and character, and that the trial court erred in applying an average person community standard. The court affirmed, finding that the complaint and information were not defective, that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction, and that the average person community standard was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction, finding that the complaint and information were not defective, that the evidence was sufficient to conclude that appellant knew the content and character of the obscene material, and that the average person community standard was proper.

 

1612 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Camacho v. Samaniego


No. 08-90-00294-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


825 S.W.2d 467; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 3259



June 5, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 3, 1991. Released for Publication February 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from County Court at Law No. 2 El Paso County, Texas. (TC# 88-679). John L. Fashing, Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bondsmen challenged an order from the County Court at Law No. 2 El Paso County (Texas), where the court granted appellee sheriff and commissioners court's motion for summary judgment and dismissed appellants' complaint for damages and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant bondsmen initiated suit for damages and injunctive relief stemming from appellee sheriff's collection of the pre-conviction bail bond approval fees. The bond amount was set by order of appellee commissioners court. Appellees argued that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the action. The trial court found it had jurisdiction and judgment was entered in appellees' favor. On appeal, the court found that the lower court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. According to the court, subject matter jurisdiction could not be conferred by agreement and could not be waived. The court stated that Tex. Const. art. V, § 8 and Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 24.020 (1988) provided that the district court had appellate jurisdiction and general supervisory control over the commissioners court. However, the court held that because the present suit was a direct attack on the order, it was not an appeal subject to the present concurrent jurisdiction of the district and county courts. The court further held that article 25.0732(t) which attempted to confer jurisdiction on the lower court was unconstitutional because it violated the separation of powers.


OUTCOME: The appeals court dismissed appellant bondsmen's suit because the lower court lacked jurisdiction over the action. The court held that because the present suit was a direct attack on appellee commissioners court's order, it was not an appeal subject to the present concurrent jurisdiction of the district and county courts.

 

1613 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Rountree v. State


No. 01-90-00382-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1402



May 23, 1991, Delivered  
May 23, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINION SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court At Law No. 11; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 8946069.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist challenged his conviction in the County Criminal Court At Law No. 11, Harris County, Texas, for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: A police officer investigated an automobile accident in which appellant motorist's company truck struck another vehicle. Appellant drove to his workplace nearby to get proof of insurance. The officer testified appellant asked to drive there; appellant testified the officer told him to drive there. The officer saw appellant driving erratically. Appellant failed field sobriety tests and was arrested. A jury convicted appellant of driving while intoxicated. On appeal, the court affirmed. Appellant could not claim the defense of entrapment because appellant's testimony indicated only that he was induced to drive, not to drive while intoxicated. In addition, he denied the offense, whereas entrapment assumes the offense was committed. The court also determined that that no warning was required before performing the field sobriety test, that a seven-month delay between arrest and trial was not a constitutional violation, that the state did not admit there was no scientific basis for the field sobriety tests, and that a trial court need not admonish a misdemeanor defendant about the range of punishment before a plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant motorist's conviction for driving while intoxicated. Appellant could not claim entrapment because while he might have been induced to drive by the officer, there was no evidence that the officer knew appellant was intoxicated; thus, appellant was not induced to commit the crime of driving while intoxicated.

Martinez v. State


No. C14-91-00123-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


810 S.W.2d 428; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1178



May 9, 1991, Rendered  
May 9, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted July 3, 1991. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused July 3, 1991. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Dismissed March 25, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 587,768; Ted Poe, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order by the United states District Court for the 228th District, Harris County (Texas), which denied his petition for habeas corpus relief on grounds that appellant was not entitled to release on bail under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 17.151 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought a writ of habeas corpus asserting that he should be released on bail pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 17.151 (1991), which provided for the release of an accused if the state was not prepared to go to trial within 90 days of the accused's detention. Appellant had been initially charged with murder and was later charged with aggravated robbery of the decedent. The court stated that article 17.151 was applicable to the murder charge against appellant but that the 90-day period had not yet elapsed on the subsequent aggravated robbery charge. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, ruling that appellant's request for release on bail had been properly denied.


OUTCOME: The denial of appellant's release on bail was affirmed. The statutory 90-day time limit for the state to hold appellant without bail had not expired for the second of two offenses for which appellant had been charged, and therefore appellant was not entitled to be released.

 

1615 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Work v. Duval


No. A14-90-00055-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


809 S.W.2d 351; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1181



May 9, 1991, Rendered  
May 9, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 295th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 83-65885; Dan Downey, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of summary judgments rendered in favor of appellees, a doctor and hospital, by the 295th District Court, Harris County (Texas). The trial court held that appellant's medical malpractice suit was barred by the statute of limitations set forth in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act of Texas, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (Supp. 1991).


OVERVIEW: Appellees, a doctor and hospital, treated appellant patient for a back condition. After appellant left the hospital, her condition deteriorated, and she became paralyzed. She was informed by other health care providers that her injuries had been caused by appellees. Although appellant conceded that her original petition was not filed within the statute of limitations period set forth in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act of Texas, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (Supp. 1991), she argued that the limitations provision was unconstitutional as applied to the facts of her case. In affirming the trial judge, the court ruled that in order to challenge the constitutionality of § 10.01, appellant had to have alleged that the limitation statute cut off her cause of action before she knew or should have known that a cause of action existed. Appellant conceded that she knew of her cause of action four months prior to the expiration of the two-year period, and the court held that four months provided a reasonable opportunity to consult an attorney and file suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the award of summary judgment in favor of appellees, a doctor and hospital, and against appellant patient. The court ruled that four months provided appellant with a reasonable opportunity to consult an attorney and file suit before her cause of action was time-barred by the limitations period of the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act.

 

1616 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hammond v. Katy Independent School Dist.


No. C14-90-00633-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


821 S.W.2d 174; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1242



May 9, 1991, Rendered  
May 9, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 240th District Court; Fort Bend County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 60,325.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher challenged summary judgments by 240th District Court, Fort Bend County (Texas), entered in favor of appellees school district and supervisor in her constructive discharge claim.


OVERVIEW: Appellant teacher resigned her position and brought a constructive discharge claim against appellees school district and supervisors. Appellees filed motions for summary judgment that addressed all claims asserted by appellant and properly incorporated appellant's deposition testimony. The motions for summary judgment were granted. Appellant challenged the entry of judgments. The court affirmed the judgments on the grounds that general allegations of mere harassment, without more, were insufficient to raise an issue of material as to whether working conditions were so intolerable that a reasonable person would have felt compelled to resign. In addition, the court held that the record was devoid of evidence that indicated that the treatment complained of by appellant was the result of any policy or custom official adopted by appellee school district in violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and did not refute appellee supervisor's defense to the claim of intentional infliction of emotional distress.


OUTCOME: The summary judgments were affirmed because appellant teacher failed to produce summary judgment evidence that raised a genuine issue of material fact. Appellant did not demonstrate the actions alleged against appellees were the result of any policy of custom official adopted by the appellee school district.

Fibreboard Corp. v. Pool


Case Nos. 06-90-00014-CV, 06-90-00022-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, six asbestos manufacturers in a products liability case, sought review from monetary jury verdicts awarded in the 4th Judicial District Court, Rusk County (Texas) to appellees, five asbestos-related injured individuals. OVERVIEW: Beginning in the 1950's to the present, appellees worked as insulators or maintenance mechanics performing insulation repair work. Although the dangers associated with exposure to asbestos were well known by the late 1940's, appellees were never warned of these dangers. A trial jury awarded compensatory damages and punitive damages in favor of the workers and against the manufacturers. The court, upon review, affirmed all the judgments with the exception of an award of future medical for one appellee, whose case was severed and remanded for a new trial unless a voluntary remittitur was made, and the exception of setting aside of exemplary damages against one appellant.


OUTCOME: Monetary judgment against appellant manufacturers in favor of appellee workers exposed to asbestos was, in almost all respects, affirmed on appeal and appellants were held to the knowledge and skill of an expert.

Finley v. State


No. B14-90-00959-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


809 S.W.2d 909; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1025



April 25, 1991, Rendered  
April 25, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 3 Brazoria County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 66,907; James Blackstock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee prosecuted appellant, and appellant sought review of his conviction of the misdemeanor offense of driving while intoxicated, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1 (Vernon Supp. 1991), entered in the County Court at Law No. 3 Brazoria County, Texas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was prosecuted by appellee for driving while intoxicated pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1 (Vernon Supp. 1991). Appellant was convicted and sought review. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that appellee's jury charge was adequate because it was carefully tailored to the charge against appellant and met the requirement for proof of each element beyond a reasonable doubt. Appellee's jury argument was not improper because appellee was responding to an argument made by opposing counsel. The court held that appellee's failure to videotape appellant pursuant to 1983 Tex. Gen. Laws 1568, 1605 did not result in a denial of due process. Appellant waived his right to a blood test under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-5, sec. 3(d) (Vernon Supp. 1990) because he refused to provide a breath test sample. Appellant's refusal to provide a breath test was admissible under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann art. 67011-5, § 3(g) (Vernon Supp. 1990) and could be considered as evidence of guilt. The court held that a police officer could offer opinion testimony of the Horizontal Gaze Nystagmus Test without first being qualified as an expert.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of the misdemeanor of driving while intoxicated. Appellee's charge to jury was adequate because it was carefully tailored and met the requirement for proof of each element of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. Appellee's refusal to provide a breath test sample was admissible and could be considered as evidence of guilt.

Hubbard v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco

April 25, 1991, Filed

DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, principal and sureties on a criminal bail bond, sought review of an order of the County Court, Robertson County (Texas), that entered a default judgment of forfeiture of the bond.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, principal and sureties on a criminal bail bond, objected to a default judgment of forfeiture of the bond, plus attorney's fees and interest. The court reversed. The court held that appellee, the state, was not entitled to any funds. The court held that the citation to appellants failed to notify the parties to appear and show cause why the judgment of forfeiture should not be made final, as required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. § 22.04. The court also held that bond forfeitures were entirely statutory, and there was no provision for the allowance of interest or attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order entering a default judgment of forfeiture of the bond and held that appellee was entitled to nothing because the citation for forfeiture of the criminal bond was defective.

 

1620 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Nail v. Thompson


No. 2-90-145-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


806 S.W.2d 599; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 983



April 24, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled May 28, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 48th District Court of Tarrant County; Hon. William L. Hughes, Jr., Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, adopted family members, sought review of a judgment of the 48th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee heirs and excluded appellants from participating in the distribution of a testamentary trust because they were adopted family members.


OVERVIEW: After the trial court entered summary judgment in favor of appellee heirs and excluded appellants, adopted family members, from participating in decedent's testamentary trust, appellants challenged the judgment. In affirming, the court held that adopted family members were not entitled to participate in the distribution of a testamentary trust. In determining that appellants were not entitled to take under the trust, the court looked to the state's law at the time of decedent's death and the impact of that law on the language of the trust instrument. In emphasizing the instrument's bequest to "lawful heirs" "born of the body" of decedent's siblings, the court held that case law had construed "born of the body" to exclude adopted family members from benefiting under a trust. The court then found that although the law at the time of decedent's death allowed an adopted child to inherit from its adopted parents, the child could not adopt through them. Moreover, the court noted that the question of whether decedent's will, which included the testamentary trust, was ambiguous was a question of law and that both the law and the trust made it clear that adopted parties could not inherit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment entered in favor of appellee heirs because the language of the testamentary trust and the law at the time of decedent's death precluded appellants, adopted family members, from participating in the distribution of decedent's testamentary trust.

Carrollton v. OHBA Corp.


No. 05-90-01505-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


809 S.W.2d 587; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1469



April 23, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 2; Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. cc-90-8938-a/b.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision from the County Court at Law No. 2, Dallas County (Texas), which issued a temporary injunction and a declaratory judgment in favor of appellee condemnee. Appellant contended that the court had no jurisdiction to grant declaratory relief and injunctive relief sought by appellee in relation to condemnation proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city sought review of a county court's grant of a temporary injunction and declaratory judgment on the grounds that the county court had no jurisdiction to grant declaratory relief and injunctive relief sought by appellee condemnee in relation to condemnation proceedings. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and dissolved the injunction because the court found that initiation of the condemnation proceeding invoked only the administrative jurisdiction of the trial court pursuant to Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 21.001 (1984). Appellee could not invoke the court's legal jurisdiction until after an award had been made, and appellee had filed objections to the award. Until the legal jurisdiction of the trial court was invoked, it lacked the authority to grant declaratory or injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court in favor of appellee condemnee, and dissolved the injunction and the amendments to it issued by the trial court, as it lacked jurisdiction in condemnation proceedings until the legal jurisdiction of the trial court was properly invoked.

Burns v. State


No. 13-89-171-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


807 S.W.2d 878; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 943



April 18, 1991, Delivered  
April 18, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled May 16, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 105th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a ruling of the 105th District Court of Nueces County (Texas), which convicted defendant of involuntary manslaughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of involuntary manslaughter after the car he was driving while intoxicated and under the influence of a controlled substance was involved in an accident which resulted in death. Defendant was taken to the police station following the accident and, while en route, questioned a police officer about what charge he would be arrested under. Defendant made certain statements at this time. It was necessary for police to assist hospital personnel in forcibly drawing blood, as required under Tex. Rev. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-5, § 3(i)(1991), when defendant failed to cooperate. Defendant appealed his conviction on multiple grounds and the court affirmed. The court held that the statements which defendant provided police while en route to the station and in custody, which did not implicate defendant, were properly admitted. Where defendant initiated the questioning, this was not a custodial interrogation under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22, § 5(1979). The court found that where only appropriate force was used to obtain defendant's blood sample, there was no violation of defendant's constitutional rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court ruling, which convicted defendant of involuntary manslaughter. The court held that defendant's voluntary statements, which did not implicate defendant, were not the product of custodial interrogation and were properly admitted. The court found that where only appropriate force was used to obtain defendant's blood sample, defendant's rights were not violated.

Martinez v. Harris County


No. 01-90-00723-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


808 S.W.2d 257; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 967



April 18, 1991, Delivered  
April 18, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied September 5, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Dismissed for Want of Jurisdiction October 2, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 269th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 89-43857; Hon. David West.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen challenged the decision of the 269th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee city in an action filed by appellant to recover for injuries he sustained when he fell off a swing at a city park.


OVERVIEW: Appellant citizen brought an action against appellee city for personal injuries, alleging that appellee negligently installed a swing in one of its parks. Appellant was injured when the swing he was on came unlatched from the chain. The trial court, relying on Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 75, which limited the landowner's liability, granted appellee's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that swinging was a recreational activity that was covered under § 75. The court further held that a reasonable meaning of "recreation" would include the activity of swinging on a swing-set provided for public use. The court also overruled appellant's objection that § 75 violated the equal protection clause of Tex. Const. art. I, § 3 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, holding that § 75 bore a rational relationship to a legitimate state interest. Finally, the court held that because appellant could not establish that he had a cognizable cause of action that was restricted by § 75 he failed to show a violation of the open courts provision of the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of appellee city and held that swinging on a swing set was recreational activity, and therefore appellee was not liable and the statute that limited appellee's landowner liability did not violate the equal protection clause of the Texas constitution or the United State's constitution or the open court provision of the constitution.

Port Arthur v. International Ass'n of Fire Fighters, Local 397


No. 09-90-007 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


807 S.W.2d 894; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1328



April 18, 1991, Delivered  
April 18, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 136th Judicial District Court Jefferson County, Texas; Cause No. D-132,838; Honorable Jack King, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of the decision of the 136th Judicial District Court Jefferson County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee firefighters' union declaring Proposition No. 3, which required binding mandatory arbitration of labor disputes between appellant and appellee, valid and directed the issuance of a writ of mandamus requiring appellant to submit to binding arbitration.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city filed an action seeking a resolution in its labor dispute with appellee firefighters' union. The trial court found that Proposition No. 1, which required nonbinding mandatory arbitration in labor disputes, conflicted with Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5154(c)-1, the Fire and Police Employees Relations Act (act), and was unenforceable, and that Proposition No. 3, which required binding mandatory arbitration, did not conflict with the act and was binding. The appellate court affirmed the finding that Proposition No. 3 was valid finding that the act gave authority to resident voters to adopt or repeal its provisions and that by adopting Proposition No. 3, which amended the arbitration provision of the act, the voters had legally exercised their authority. The court rejected a prior holding that the act was unconstitutional because it attempted to delegate a legislative function to the judiciary without sufficient standards to guide the discretion conferred. Rather, the court held that there was no provision in the act that required it to find that the legislature impliedly limited the power of a city to propose an amendment concerning arbitration.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that Proposition No. 3 was valid and that appellant city had to submit to binding arbitration, and held that the applicable statute gave authority to the voters to adopt or repeal its provisions and that the voters had approved Proposition No. 3, which amended the arbitration provisions of the statute, by the appropriate majority vote.

Connor v. State

April 17, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled June 5, 1991. As Corrected June 12, 1991. Released for Publication June 12, 1991. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted September 18, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Llano County, 33rd Judicial District; Nos. 4242, 4343, and 4244, Honorable Clayton E. Evans, Judge.

Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-29(C)(1) (1991) and Tex. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-4(F) (1964).


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to three counts of fraudulent sale of securities in violation of the Texas Securities Act, Tex. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 581-29(C)(1) (1991) and 581-4(F) (1964). Punishment was assessed in each case at 10 years confinement, probated, and the court ordered restitution. Beyer v. Employees Retirement System


No. 3-90-168-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


808 S.W.2d 622; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 979



April 17, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled June 5, 1991. Released for Publication June 12, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Denied September 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 167th Judicial District; No. 416,188, Honorable Paul R. Davis, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant widow sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 167th Judicial District (Texas), which affirmed an order issued by the trustees of co-appellee Employees Retirement System of Texas that awarded appellant life insurance proceeds but denied her request for interest, attorney's fees, and a penalty.


OVERVIEW: Appellant widow and co-appellee stepsons filed competing claims for life insurance proceeds with co-appellee Employees Retirement System of Texas. The board of trustees for co-appellee retirement system awarded the proceeds to appellant, but denied her request for interest, attorney's fees, and a 12 percent penalty due to the delay in payment. Appellant filed suit in district court seeking to recover the additional amounts, and the district court affirmed the board's order. On appeal, appellant contended that the board erred in failing to award her the additional sums and that the district court erred in failing to file findings of fact and conclusions of law. Affirming the board's order, the court held that pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-13a, § 4(B), the board's authority was limited to deciding questions related to the payment of claims and it had no authority to award the additional sums. The court further held that § 4(B), provided for substantial evidence review; therefore, it would be fruitless for the district court to make findings of fact, and there was no necessity for it to file conclusions of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order issued by the board of trustees for co-appellee Employees Retirement System of Texas denying appellant widow interest, attorney's fees, and a 12 percent penalty because the board's statutory authority was limited to making payment on claims.

Commercial Life Ins. Co. v. Texas State Bd. of Ins.


No. 3-90-148-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


808 S.W.2d 552; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 863



April 10, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled June 5, 1991. Released for Publication June 12, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Denied September 18, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Overruled October 16, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 331st Judicial District; No. 377,085, Honorable Pete Lowry, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 331st Judicial District (Texas), which refused appellant's application for a trial de novo, and sustained appellee Texas State Board of Insurance's final order denying appellant's desired name reservation on the ground that it was supported by substantial evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurer applied to reserve a name in connection with its intention to obtain a corporate charter issued by appellee Texas State Board of Insurance. Appellee denied appellant's name reservation on the ground that the name was likely to mislead the public. A trial court held that the proper method of review for appellee's order was substantial evidence review. Appellant sought review of the trial court's judgment. The court reversed the trial court's judgment because Tex. Ins. Code art. 1.04(f) (1981) was constitutional as applied to the case, and the trial court erred in determining the cause based on a substantial evidence scope of review. The court concluded that appellee's action in denying appellant's name reservation was quasi-judicial and not legislative in nature. The court found that appellee's only function was to determine whether appellant's name reservation met the standards prescribed by Tex. Ins. Code art. 3.02, § 1(2) (1991). The court held, therefore, that the trial court erred in determining the cause based on a substantial evidence scope of review, as it denied appellant a trial de novo. The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded a trial court's judgment refusing appellant insurer's application for a trial de novo because the trial court erred in determining the case based upon a substantial evidence scope of review. The court found that a provision of the Texas insurance code was constitutional as applied to the case, and that appellee Texas State Board of Insurance's denial of appellant's name reservation was quasi-judicial nature.

 

1629 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


David v. State


No. 05-90-00477-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


808 S.W.2d 239; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1336



April 10, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Criminal District Court #5; Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. F89-79719-TL.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions from the Criminal District Court #5, Dallas County (Texas), for aggravated sexual assault of a child, contending that his conviction and sentence unconstitutionally placed him twice in jeopardy for the same offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions for aggravated sexual assault of a child, contending that his conviction and sentence unconstitutionally placed him twice in jeopardy for the same offense by charging the same offense committed by different methods. The court noted that the sentences ran concurrently. Logically such sentences did not twice jeopardize or put defendant in danger of either additional or increased punishment. Defendant committed two acts performed with his sexual organ, vaginal penetration and oral penetration. The evidence revealed that both acts occurred in a motel room on the same day. The record, however, was silent about when each act occurred in relation to the other. They reasonably could not have occurred simultaneously. One act must have been completed before the other began. Although there was some overlap of proof, such as same victim, date, and place, each conviction required the allegation and proof of an entirely separate element that the other did not. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, because each of defendant's convictions required the allegation and proof of an entirely separate element that the other did not. The acts were consecutive and, according to statute, the sentences ran concurrently.

OVERVIEW: Appellee insurers represented appellant insured in a medical malpractice action against appellant's former patient. Appellant was held liable and a non-execution agreement was executed, which provided that the patient would only execute against appellant's insurance policy proceeds. Appellant contended that appellees failed to properly settle, defendant, and provide him with coverage in the action. The lower court awarded judgment in favor of appellant, pursuant to Tex. Ins. Code Ann. art. 21.21 § 16(b)(1) (1990). The court determined that the non-execution agreement was merely a covenant not a release, and therefore, such agreement did not affect appellees' liability. The court held that appellees' duty toward appellant extended beyond reasonable settlement attempts to investigation, preparation, and defense of the lawsuit. The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court with a damages modification.

The court held that appellees were not entitled to contribution or indemnity from other parties for their statutory violations. Ortiz v. State


No. A14-90-00241-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 758



March 28, 1991, Rendered  
March 28, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 315th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 63795.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the ruling of the 315th District Court for Harris County (Texas), which found that appellant had engaged in delinquent conduct and assessed a determinate sentence of 20 years. The trial court ordered appellant transferred to the Department of Criminal Justice prior to his 18th birthday to complete his sentence, and appellant contended the trial court was without jurisdiction to order a determinate sentence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the juvenile appellant had engaged in delinquent conduct by committing aggravated kidnapping and assessed a determinate sentence of 20 years. Appellant challenged the trial court's jurisdiction to order a determinate sentence because the grand jury did not approve the original petition and that he was not served with the petition. The court disagreed and affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that the state filed a petition that met all the requirements of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 53.04 (1986), and properly sought the grand jury's approval of the petition. The court also held that the trial court read the petition into the record in appellant's presence and that appellant's counsel then stipulated that appellant had been served with the petition. Therefore the trial court had jurisdiction. The court rejected appellant's claim that the determinate sentencing statutes were unconstitutional because appellant made no objection at the hearing and thus failed to preserve the claim for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which found appellant had engaged in delinquent conduct and assessed a determinate sentence of 20 years because the state filed a petition that met all the requirements of the statute and properly sought the grand jury's approval of the petition, and the trial court had jurisdiction because appellant was properly served with the petition.

General Electric Credit Corp. v. Midland Cent. Appraisal Dist.


No. 08-90-00164-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


808 S.W.2d 169; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 728



March 27, 1991

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 142nd District Court of Midland County, Texas. TC No. A-36,748; Pat M. Baskin, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged a decision from the 142nd District Court of Midland County, (Texas) that granted summary judgment to appellees counties and appraisal districts on their counterclaim for delinquent ad valorem taxes, penalties, interest and attorney's fees against appellant on its aircraft. The aircraft in question was taxed in some manner by multiple appellee counties and their appraisal districts.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted summary judgment to appellees counties and appraisal districts on their counterclaim for delinquent ad valorem taxes, penalties, interest and attorney's fees against appellant corporation on their aircraft. The trial court granted summary judgment to the appellees denying appellant's petition for relief from double taxation. Appellant failed to exhaust prerequisite administrative remedies to challenge the assessed taxes. Appellant, taxed by two appellee counties on the aircraft, challenged the trial court judgment on appeal. The court noted that appellant resorted to direct suit to obtain determination of situs to avoid double taxation because neither the statutes nor the administrative procedures outlined a process to determine the aircraft's situs. The court, however, found appellant's argument regarding lack of due process and violation of the state constitutional open courts doctrine in his contest of the tax assessments unsupported by law. The court affirmed the lower court judgment because appellant, as the taxpayer, had not exhausted the administrative procedures to contest assessment. Appellant was also assessed damages for filing a frivolous appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment and damages assessed against appellant corporation in this case. The court found that appellant failed to exhaust procedures set forth in the statutes for taxpayers to resolve issues with taxing authorities. The court also assessed damages against appellant after finding their appeal was brought for the purpose of delay and without sufficient cause.

Morgan v. State


No. 01-89-00522-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 710



March 21, 1991, Delivered  
March 21, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 11; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 8839200.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the County Court at Law No. 11, Harris County (Texas), which found him guilty of misdemeanor assault, and assessed his punishment at 180 days confinement, probated for one year, and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his wife were involved in an altercation, wherein defendant raised his leg to ward off a kick from his wife. A jury found defendant guilty of misdemeanor assault. On appeal, defendant argued that by not recognizing "passive self-defense," Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 9.31 (1974) was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend V and U.S. Const. amend XIV. The court found that the statute enjoyed a presumption of constitutionality that defendant failed to refute. Defendant also argued that by raising his leg to ward off a kick was a form of "passive self-defense," and required the trial court to give a jury instruction on self-defense. However, the court found that defendant's "passive self-defense" theory was a theory that negated an element of the offense and was not a self-defense issue for the jury. Finally, defendant argued that he was subjected to ineffective assistance of counsel because his lawyer failed to request a jury instruction on self-defense. However, because there was no evidence to merit an instruction on self-defense, counsel's performance in not requesting one was not deficient. The decision of the trial court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision finding defendant guilty of misdemeanor assault was affirmed because defendant was not entitled to a jury instruction on "passive self-defense" where the statute did not provide such a defense.

 

1636 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Dillard v. Austin Independent School Dist.


No. 3-88-241-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


806 S.W.2d 589; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 692



March 20, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 25, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Denied October 2, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District; No. 399,939-A, Honorable Joe B. Dibrell, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of December 19, 1990, Reported at 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 3011.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a decision by the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District (Texas), which granted a motion for summary judgment in favor of appellee school district based on governmental immunity and the absence of a taking under Tex. Const. art. I, § 17.


OVERVIEW: Appellants owned a 24 acre property which appellee school district's board of trustees had voted to negotiate to purchase for a new high school. After appellants allegedly spent $ 151,000 to obtain the permits necessary to develop the property, appellee purchased a different tract of land. Appellants sued for damages, alleging breach of contract, promissory estoppel, breach of the duty of good faith negotiation, fraud, gross negligence, and a taking under Tex. Const. art. I, § 17. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that an independent school district carries out only governmental functions, and, consequently in entitled to governmental immunity. The court held that estoppel can apply only to governmental units that exercise proprietary functions. In addition, the court held that the mere initiation of condemnation proceedings was but an incidental damage that was not compensable as a taking or damage even though it may interfere with the marketability of the property. Finally, the court held that permitting a suit directly against a governmental unit that has acted illegally would effectively gut the provisions of the Texas Tort Claims Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which granted a motion for summary judgment against appellant owners of property based on governmental immunity and the absence of a taking. The court held that appellee was entitled to governmental immunity, that estoppel did not apply, and that mere initiation of condemnation proceedings was not compensable as a taking.

 

1637 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Shidaker v. Winsett


No. 07-90-0095-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


805 S.W.2d 941; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 653



 March 15, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled April 8, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Denied June 19, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 47th Judicial District Court of Potter County; No. 72,067-A; Honorable David L. Gleason, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, individually and as executor of the estate of the deceased, and others, appealed from the 47th Judicial District Court of Potter County (Texas) after a take-nothing summary judgment. The judgment was rendered on the ground that limitations barred appellants' action to hold appellee doctor liable for the death of the deceased, alleged to be directly and proximately caused by appellee's negligent diagnosis and medical treatment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, individually and as executor of the estate of the deceased, and others, appealed from a take-nothing summary judgment. The judgment was rendered on the ground that limitations barred appellants' action to hold appellee doctor liable for the death of the deceased. Appellants alleged that the death was directly and proximately caused by appellee's negligent diagnosis and medical treatment. The reviewing court affirmed. The court held that in an action founded on a health care liability claim of misdiagnosis or mistreatment, the operative limitation period for redress was Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1991), regardless of the alleged extent of the health care injury. The court rejected appellants' argument that the application of § 10.01 placed an impossible burden on them by cutting off the wrongful death action before it accrued. The court concluded that application of § 10.01 had not denied appellants access to the court; the statute merely limited the time in which they could file suit. Appellants had more than one year to file their health care liability claim after they knew appellee could have been guilty of medical malpractice.


OUTCOME: The take-nothing summary judgment in favor of appellee doctor was affirmed. Appellants had more than one year to file their health care liability claim after knowledge that appellee could have been guilty of medical malpractice; therefore, the limitation period was not unconstitutionally applied.

Smith v. State


No. B14-90-00110-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 652



March 14, 1991, Rendered  
March 14, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 19, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 515,775.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the 176th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of aggravated assault of a peace officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated assault of a peace officer. Defendant challenged the trial court's decision; however the appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision convicting defendant. The appellate court held that the trial court did not err by not sustaining defendant's objection to state's argument, wherein state asked jurors to place themselves in the position of the complainant because the record reflected that the trial court did admonish state for making the argument. The appellate court further overruled defendant's objection that state's argument was so inflammatory and prejudicial during the punishment stage that in the interest of justice his cause should be reversed even though defendant's counsel failed to object at trial because state's argument was not improper at this stage. Moreover, appellate court held that defendant was not denied the effective assistance of counsel on the ground that his counsel failed to object to the "in their shoes" argument because it has already been determined that such comments were not objectionable.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated assault of a peace officer was affirmed because state's argument requesting that jurors to place themselves in the shoes of the complainant was not improper or impermissible. Moreover, the appellate court found that given that state's comments were not improper, defendant's counsel could not have been ineffective for failing to object to those statements.

Bullock v. Regular Veterans Assn., Post No. 76


No. 3-90-142-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


806 S.W.2d 311; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 593



March 13, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 17, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District; No. 468,215, Honorable F. Scott McCown, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state comptroller and alcoholic beverage commission, sought review of a decision of the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District (Texas), which entered a judgment declaring § 2(4)(A)(iv) of the Bingo Enabling Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 179d (Supp. 1991), to be unconstitutional and awarding attorney's fees to appellee veterans' organization.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, state comptroller and alcoholic beverage commission, denied a bingo license to appellee veterans' organization, on the ground that it met neither the definition of a fraternal organization under § 2(4)(A)(iv) of the Bingo Enabling Act (the Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 179d (Supp. 1991), which excluded groups composed predominantly of veterans, nor that of a veterans' organization under the Act. Appellee brought suit seeking a declaratory judgment that the Act unconstitutionally discriminated against it, and an injunction. The trial court declared § 2(4)(A)(iv) unconstitutional, enjoined appellants from enforcing the provision, and awarded appellee attorney's fees. Appellants sought review of the decision. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that § 2(4)A)(iv) unconstitutionally made a distinction without a rational basis. The court held that appellants' failure to specially except and raise affirmative defenses waived both sovereign immunity from suit and any complaint of appellee's failure to allege specific statutory authority for the attorney's fees award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting a declaratory judgment, an injunction, and attorney's fees to appellee veterans' organization, in its suit against appellants, state comptroller and alcoholic beverage commission, to declare a portion of the Bingo Enabling Act unconstitutional, because the statute irrationally discriminated against appellee and appellants had waived sovereign immunity.

Porter v. State


Appeal Nos. 04-90-00036-CR, 04-90-00098-CR

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 216th District Court of Gillespie County (Texas), which convicted him of manufacturing and possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, amphetamine, in an amount greater than 28 grams but less than 400 grams.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of manufacturing and possession with intent to deliver a controlled substance, amphetamine, in an amount greater than 28 grams but less than 400 grams. On appeal the court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court rejected appellant's argument that the law was void for vagueness, holding that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague simply because appellant did not know in advance within what range of penalties appellant would actually be charged because the statute sufficiently described the offense, giving a person of ordinary intelligence fair notice that the contemplated conduct was forbidden. The court held that appellant's argument concerning the doctrine of in pari materia was misplaced because two conflicting statutes were not involved. The court further held that the evidence was sufficient to establish appellant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. The court rejected appellant's final point of error, holding that the state's questioning regarding appellant's silence was not reversible error because the issue was not properly preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for manufacturing and possession with intent to distribute amphetamines because the statute under which appellant was convicted was not vague, evidence was sufficient to establish appellant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt, and the state's questioning regarding appellant's silence was not reversible error because the issue was not preserved for appeal.
