Jackson v. State


No. B14-90-00023-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


807 S.W.2d 387; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 515



March 7, 1991, Rendered  
March 7, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused July 3, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 522,433; Robert Mont, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought reversal of the judgment of the 177th District Court, Harris County (Texas), convicting him of possession of cocaine and sentencing him to 30 years confinement on grounds that the evidence was insufficient to show that he knowingly possessed cocaine, and that his conviction violated his rights to due process and equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of possession of cocaine under Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §§ 481.102(3)(D), 481.115(a),(b) (1991) and sentenced to 30 years in prison. He appealed his conviction and alleged that the evidence was insufficient to show that he knowingly possessed cocaine; that his conviction for possession of an unusable amount of cocaine violated his rights to due process, due course, and equal protection of the law; that his due process rights were violated because there was no reasonable basis to prohibit the possession of an unusable quantity of cocaine; and that punishment for possession of an unusable amount of cocaine was cruel and unusual. The court affirmed the conviction and found that a rational fact finder could conclude that appellant knowingly possessed cocaine. The court also determined that the § 481.115 did not violate due process because it had a rational relation to the legitimate legislative purpose of deterring distribution and use of cocaine. Likewise, appellant's equal protection rights were not violated because there was no class discrimination. The law was directed at the conduct of possessing a controlled substance and not a class of people.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because it found that a rational finder of fact could have concluded that appellant knowingly possessed cocaine. The court also found that appellant's conviction for possession of cocaine did not violate due process or equal protection as there was a rational relation to the legitimate legislative purpose of deterring distribution and use of cocaine, and there was no class discrimination.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the order of the 298th Judicial District Court of Dallas County (Texas) which dismissed its appeal of the appraised value of its property assessed by appellees, the appraisal district and review board. Appellant argued that the dismissal was improper and that the statutory scheme was unconstitutional under the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art I, § 13.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property brought an appeal of the assessed tax liability owed on its property. Appellees, the appraisal district and review board, argued that the appeal should be dismissed as the statutorily required prerequisite taxes had not been paid. The court found that appellant had paid no taxes due prior to the statutory delinquency date found in Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08 (1991). The court concluded that appellant violated the provisions of § 42.08, and affirmed, holding that the trial court's dismissal of appellant's suit was proper. The court found that appellant did not claim a cognizable common law cause of action, but challenged a statutory scheme.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which dismissed appellant property owner's appeal of the valuation of its property as set by appellees, the appraisal district and review board. The court found that appellant had not satisfied the statutory prerequisites to bringing such a challenge.

Shaw v. State


Nos. 2-90-134-CV, 2-90-135-CV, 2-90-136-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


804 S.W.2d 672; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 460



February 27, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled March 26, 1991. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused July 3, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 213th District Court of Tarrant County; Honorable George S. Kredell.



DISPOSITION: Judgment is affirmed in part and reformed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surety sought review of the order of the 213th District Court, Tarrant County (Texas), which entered judgment against appellant in three separate bond forfeiture proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Appellant surety sought review of the trial court's judgments against him in three separate bond forfeitures. Appellant challenged the assessment of prejudgment interest against him, contending that the assessment was a violation of his due process rights. The court overruled this point of error, holding that the assessment against appellant was not prejudgment interest but interest that accrued from the date of the forfeiture. The reference to prejudgment interest in Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.16 referred only to the rate at which the interest accrued. Furthermore, that statute was no longer in conflict with Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 2372p-3, § 13(b), because the latter statute had been declared unconstitutional by the criminal court of appeals. The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court, reforming the judgments in two of the cases to assess interest from the date of the judgment nisi only until the case disposition date, after which appellant had no liability.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments against appellant surety were affirmed as reformed to adjust the period of interest accrual. The statute at issue did not assess prejudgment interest, but rather interest from the date of the judgment at the same rate as prejudgment interest. The statute was no longer in conflict with another statute because the other statute had been ruled unconstitutional.

Nisbet v. State


No. 01-89-00782-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 421

NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the trial court (Texas) for intentionally selling obscene materials, knowing their content.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for intentionally selling obscene materials, knowing their content. His motion to quash the complaint was denied, and he was found guilty after a plea of nolo contendere. The trial court assessed punishment at three days confinement and a $ 500 fine. On appeal, the court affirmed. Based on prior case law upholding the constitutionality of the Texas obscenity statutes, the court overruled defendant's argument that the statutes were overbroad. Finally, the court overruled defendant's contention that the trial court erred in denying his motion to quash the complaint because there was not a timely and proper determination of obscenity. The court found that by his plea of nolo contendere, defendant admitted every element of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because the Texas obscenity statutes was neither overbroad nor indefinite, vague, and uncertain. The court also concluded that defendant, by his plea of nolo contendere, admitted every element of the offense.

Chumney v. Craig

PRIOR HISTORY: From 220th Judicial District Court; Hamilton County, Texas; Trial Court No. H-51-90.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant election contestant sought review of a decision by the 220th Judicial District Court, Harris County (Texas), which denied appellant relief in his action against appellee hospital district.


OVERVIEW: Appellant election contestant filed an action against appellee county hospital district. The trial court denied appellant relief and appellant filed an appeal. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment against appellant. The court noted that appellant had standing to bring the suit under Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 233.02 (1986). The court found that, at the time of the election, appellee's directors were properly serving and had the authority to call the election. The court considered appellant's contention that appellee failed to comply with the statute in conducting the election. In considering appellant's challenge to the qualifications of the voters, the court explained that, in order to prevail, appellant had to prove not only that voting irregularities occurred, but also that they materially affected the results of the election. The court concluded that the record did not reflect that votes by unqualified persons affected the outcome of the election.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment denying relief to appellant election contestant, because appellee county hospital district substantially complied with the statute and appellant election contestant failed to satisfy his burden of overcoming the presumption that the officials properly discharged their duties in conducting the election.

Burton v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas

 February 20, 1991, Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his convictions from the 194th Judicial District Court of Dallas County (Texas) for aggravated robbery and aggravated kidnapping following a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for aggravated robbery. Eleven months later, appellant failed to appear for trial. Six years later, appellant was extradited from Nevada and returned to Texas. Appellant was indicted for aggravated kidnapping. Appellant executed a number of speedy trial waivers. Following a jury trial, appellant was convicted for aggravated robbery and aggravated kidnapping and this appeal followed. The court affirmed appellant's convictions. The court held that appellant's constitutional right to a speedy trial was not violated because appellant made no showing that the state's delay was prejudicial. The court held that the Interstate Agreement on Detainers, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 51.14 was inapplicable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for aggravated robbery and aggravate kidnapping because the lower court properly granted the state's challenges for cause for two veniremen and properly denied appellant's motion to dismiss the indictments for violations of the statute of limitations, violations of his constitutional right to a speedy trial, and violations of the Interstate Agreement on Detainers.

State v. Durham


No. 3-90-071-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


804 S.W.2d 312; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 346; 119 Oil & Gas Rep. 549



February 13, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled March 13, 1991. Released for Publication March 13, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Granted September 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 345th Judicial District; No. 438,554, Honorable Pete Lowry, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County (Texas) which granted summary judgment for appellees, the successors of a Relinquishment Act landowner and his colleagues, in appellant's suit for the profits obtained from an oil and gas transaction.


OVERVIEW: In 1934, a surface owner of land governed by the Relinquishment Act (Act), 1919 Tex. Gen. Laws, ch. 81, negotiated an oil and gas lease. Pursuant to the Act, the owner and appellant state shared the consideration paid by the lessee. Subsequently, the owner acquired a larger interest in the mineral estate. Fifty-six years later, appellant sued appellees, the successors of the landowner and his colleagues, for a share of that mineral interest and of the owner's profits. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court concluded that a 1934 Relinquishment Act landowner owed appellant only those duties expressly set forth in the Act and not a fiduciary duty. Even if a 1934 surface owner did owe appellant a fiduciary duty, the court held, the owner in this case did not owe that duty to appellant at the time of the mineral transactions because his representation had terminated. The court noted that this termination resulted from the failure to offset drainage, from the imposition of a receivership, and from the execution of a subsequent lease.


OUTCOME: Holding that the 1934 surface owner of Relinquishment Act land did not owe appellant state a fiduciary duty, the court affirmed summary judgment against appellant in its suit to recover a share of mineral interests and profits.

Jamail v. State


No. B14-85-00019-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 316



February 7, 1991, Rendered  
February 7, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied October 30, 1991. State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied October 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Court at Law No. 6; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 775449.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from County Court at Law No. 6, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of driving while intoxicated under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1(b) after it overruled appellant's motion to quash an indictment.


OVERVIEW: When the trial court overruled appellant's motion to quash an indictment and convicted him of driving while intoxicated under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-1(b), appellant sought review. On appeal, the court stated that appellant's consent was not vitiated by appellant's requests for his own doctor. The court affirmed because appellant's blood sample was not the product of an unreasonable seizure. The trial court properly instructed the jury that, if they had a reasonable doubt as to whether appellant received statutory warnings prior to any statement made on videotape, they could disregard the evidence. The trial court also properly instructed the jury that, if they had a reasonable doubt as to whether appellant knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily consented to the taking of the blood specimen, they could disregard that evidence. The court added that the legality of the stop and arrest were questions of law for the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence for driving while intoxicated because appellant's blood sample was not product of unreasonable seizure. The court further held that the trial court properly instructed the jury that if it had reasonable doubt as to whether appellant received statutory warnings prior to statement, it could disregard this evidence.

Mays v. State


No. 01-90-00611-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 266



January 31, 1991, Delivered  
January 31, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 3; Harris County, Texas; Appellate Cause No. 4732.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 3 of Harris County (Texas) affirming his conviction and fine after a bench trial before a municipal court of the City of Houston, for failure to complete repairs on a moved-in building within 150 days, a misdemeanor under Houston, Tex. Ordinances § 10-49 (1985). Defendant asserted that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and, therefore, voided.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and fined after bench trial for failure to complete repairs on a moved-in building within 150 days, a misdemeanor under Houston, Tex. Ordinances § 10-49 (1985). He appealed to the county criminal court, which affirmed the judgment. On appeal, defendant contended the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and, therefore, voided. He also contended the trial court erred in assessing a fine because the only penalty provided under the ordinance was demolition of the building at the owner's expense. The court affirmed. The court held defendant failed to challenge the constitutionality of the ordinance in his motion for new trial. Tex. Gov't Code 30.269(c) stated that the motion for new trial must set forth the points of error of which defendant complained and, for the purpose of appeal, a point not distinctly set forth in the motion was waived. There was no objection to the vagueness of the ordinance; therefore, the constitutional complaint was waived by the terms of the statute. The court further held no authority was cited, nor was the ordinance included in the brief on appeal. Thus, the court could not address defendant's second point of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's misdemeanor conviction and fine for failure to complete repairs on a moved-in building within 150 days. The court held that there was no objection to the vagueness of the ordinance; therefore, the constitutional complaint was waived by the terms of the statute.

 

1652 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. One 1988 Nissan Pickup


No. 12-90-00100-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


804 S.W.2d 957; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 291



January 31, 1991, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 145th Judicial District Court of Nacogdoches County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the 145th Judicial District Court of Nacogdoches County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee, the owner of an automobile that the state sought to forfeit as a result of appellee's alleged illegal activities.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a forfeiture action against appellee automobile owner as a result of appellee's alleged illegal activities. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellee, finding that the state had failed to comply with the requirements of former Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 § 5.07(a), requiring a forfeiture case to be set for trial within 30 days of the filing of an answer. The state appealed and the reviewing court reversed. The court held that the language in former art. 4476-15 § 5.07(a) was directory and not mandatory. Therefore, the trial court erred in granting appellee's motion for summary judgment on the basis that no hearing was set within 30 days of the date appellee filed his answer. Because the court was persuaded that the legislature never intended for the time period to be mandatory, the court held that the summary judgment was in error and the court remanded the case for a trial on the merits.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for appellee automobile owner was reversed and remanded for a trial on the merits. The language in the former statute requiring a forfeiture case to be set for trial within 30 days of the filing of an answer was directory and not mandatory. Therefore, the trial court erred in granting appellee's motion for summary judgment on the basis that no hearing was set within 30 days of the date appellee filed his answer.

 

1653 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re S.B.C.


No. 12-88-00305-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


805 S.W.2d 1; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 292



 January 31, 1991, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 4, 1991. Rehearing Denied April 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 321st Judicial District Court of Smith County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the 321st Judicial District Court of Smith County, Texas, which adjudicated and disposed of a juvenile court action alleging appellant committed delinquent conduct, namely aggravated sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the adjudication and disposition of a juvenile court alleging appellant committed delinquent conduct. The state's petition complied fully with every element of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 53.04 (1986). The state's determinate sentencing statutes, including Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 53.045, 54.04, under which appellant was sentenced did not violate his federal constitutional rights to equal protection and due process. The determinate sentencing statutes furthered a compelling state interest by striking a balance between the state's interest in providing for the care of its children and its interest in providing security for citizens in general. Appellant's argument that the potential of impropriety existed in the prosecutor's exercise of the determinate sentencing statutes presented nothing for review. Appellant was not twice placed in jeopardy for the same offense. The state's motion to dismiss a previous delinquency petition for the same conduct meant there was no adjudication on the merits. Appellant's failure to obtain a ruling on his objection to the prosecutor's inappropriate terminology meant the error was not preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's adjudication and disposition of a juvenile court action alleging appellant committed delinquent conduct. The state's determinate sentencing statutes, under which appellant was sentenced, did not violate his equal protection and due process rights. Appellant was not twice placed in jeopardy when the state brought a second petition on the same conduct that a first petition was based on that was later dismissed.

Burleson v. State


No. 2-88-301-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


802 S.W.2d 429; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 229



January 25, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From Criminal District Court No. 1 of Tarrant County; Hon. John Bradshaw.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the Criminal District Court No. 1 of Tarrant County (Texas) of the offense of harmful access to a computer in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.03 (1985). Defendant challenged the admissibility of the computer generated records and the constitutionality of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.03.


OVERVIEW: Shortly after defendant was fired, someone accessed his computer terminal using his password and security clearance. Computer logs indicated that actions taken during the unauthorized access triggered malevolent software responsible for destroying payroll data. A jury convicted defendant of harmful access to a computer in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.03, sentenced him to seven years probation, and ordered him to pay restitution. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that defendant's objection to testimony about the computer search was properly overruled because the witness need not be qualified as an expert or present printouts in order to testify as to the results of the computer search. The court also held that computer printouts were the results of an automatic recording device. Because there was no reliance upon human input, the determination that such computer self-generated data was not hearsay was in accord with Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 801. The court further held that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 33.03 was constitutional as applied to defendant because it was not too vague to inform him that his conduct was criminal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of the offense of harmful access to a computer. The court held that the payroll record was not hearsay because it was not activated automatically; it was not the result of the observations entered into the device by the declarant. The court also held that statute under which defendant was charged was not unconstitutional because it was not too vague to inform defendant that his conduct was criminal.

First Bank of Deer Park v. Harris County


No. 01-88-00501-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


804 S.W.2d 588; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 199



January 24, 1991, Delivered  
January 24, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 270th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 83-72985A; Hon. Ann Tyrell Cochran.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of March 8, 1990, Reported at 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 492.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank sought review of a decision of the 270th District Court, Harris County, Texas, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, county and tax assessor-collector, in appellant's suit seeking refund of taxes paid under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.02(d) (1982).


OVERVIEW: Appellant bank brought suit against appellees, county and tax-assessor-collector, for a refund of taxes it paid on bank stock under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.02(d) (1982). The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellees, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that appellant's protest under Tex. Tax Code Ann.§ 31.11 (1982) did not preserve its right to contest the ownership of the stock under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 41.41 (1982), and that because appellant's denial of ownership was unrelated to the constitutionality of the tax, appellant had not exhausted its administrative remedies so as to be eligible for judicial relief. The court found that under § 41.41, appellant was required to file a notice protesting ownership no later than the 30th day after the date the notice of taxes was delivered to it, and that its notice was therefore untimely. The court also held that appellant's pleadings of fraud, duress, and mutual mistake were affirmative defenses rather than claims for affirmative relief, and that appellant had failed to raise fact issues in its summary judgment proof on these questions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment to appellees, county and tax assessor-collector, in appellant bank's suit for a refund of taxes paid on bank stock, because appellant had not preserved the question of ownership of the property on appeal, and because appellant had failed to raise fact issues in its summary judgment proof.

Olson v. Central Power & Light Co.


No. 13-90-166-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


803 S.W.2d 808; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 213



January 24, 1991, Delivered  
January 24, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled February 21, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Denied September 5, 1991. Rehearing Overruled December 11, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 117th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of a decision of the 117th District Court of Nueces County, Texas, which granted summary judgment to appellee utility in appellee's suit for statutory indemnity under the Texas Public Utility Act art. 1436c, § 7(b), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 1436c, § 7(b) (1980).


OVERVIEW: An employee of appellant employer sustained personal injuries from an electrical overhead power line owned by appellee utility. The employee filed suit against appellee and others for his injuries. Appellant's workers' compensation carrier provided benefits to the employee. Appellee filed a third party suit against appellant for statutory indemnity under the Texas Public Utilities Act. Appellee and appellant filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court granted appellee's motion, except as to attorney's fees, and denied appellant's motion. Both parties sought review. The court affirmed in part, and reversed and rendered in part, the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the Texas Public Utilities Act took precedence over the immunity provision of the Texas Workers' Compensation Act. The court declined to expand the doctrine of express negligence to instances of statutory indemnity, and found that the indemnity provision was not void for vagueness. The court held that the indemnification provided for under the Texas Public Utilities Act included attorney's fees, and that appellee's proof had established its entitlement to attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of appellee utility, in its indemnity suit against appellant employer, because the statute providing indemnity took precedence over appellant's claim of immunity. The court reversed and rendered that part of the judgment denying appellee attorney's fees, because the statute authorized attorney's fees and appellee had established its entitlement to fees.

Smith v. State


No. 05-90-00104-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


801 S.W.2d 629; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 231



January 23, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 8; Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. MA88-48928-J.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED and ABATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of County Criminal Court No. 8, Dallas County, Texas, which convicted him of the offense of promotion of obscene material and assessed a fine of $ 2,000. The transcript contained an order signed by the trial judge granting defendant's pretrial motion to declare Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§43.21-43.23 (1989) unconstitutional and to dismiss the cause against him.


OVERVIEW: The court abated defendant's appeal and ordered the trial court on remand to determine the circumstances underlying the trial court's action with respect to defendant's pretrial motion to declare Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§43.21-43.23 (1989) unconstitutional and dismiss the case against him. The trial judge signed an order granting defendant's motion. The statement of facts showed that the trial judge orally denied the motion, but signed an order granting it. Because dismissal of a case was a jurisdictional matter and could not be waived, the court held that defendant did not waive his point of error by failing to object to the continuation of the trial and participating in it. The court suggested that, if the order was signed as the result of clerical error, it could be corrected. The court held that the decision regarding the clerical or judicial nature of any error was a question of law. However, because the court could not make fact determinations, it remanded the case to the trial court for a factual determination either that the written order truthfully reflected what actually occurred or that it was inaccurate for certain specified reasons.


OUTCOME: The court abated defendant's appeal and ordered the trial court on remand to determine the circumstances surrounding the signing of the dismissal order, because the court could not make the findings of fact necessary for it to determine whether the order was signed as the result of clerical or judicial error. The trial court was to correct the order, if needed, and forward the hearing record, fact findings, and any corrections to the court.

Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001 (Supp. 1991), arguing abuse of discretion and violation of his constitutional rights.

Williams v. State


No. B14-90-00206-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 87



January 10, 1991, Rendered  
January 10, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 178th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 520,170. 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction of the felony offense of possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, weighing less than 28 grams after a jury trial in the 178th District Court, Harris County (Texas). Appellant presented 23 points of error in a pro se brief, including errors under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.01 § 1 (1989) and delay contrary to Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.01 and 32A.02.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction of the offense of possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, weighing less than 28 grams. The court held that pretrial hearings were discretionary under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.01 § 1 (1989). The court added that mere allegations not supported by evidence could not have considered on appeal, and failures to object at trial left nothing to review, including the admission of an open blue warrant. There was no pre-trial procedure to test the sufficiency of the evidence. Noting that the Speedy Trial Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32A.01 and 32.02, was declared unconstitutional, the court also decided that appellant was not prejudiced by any delays. The court found he failed to meet the requirements of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 24.13 (1989) to obtain witnesses in the custody of the state. The court decided the state could have used hypotheticals to assure prospective jurors were able to consider the full range of punishment. The court found no prosecutorial misconduct and noted that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 3(a) (1991) permitted admission of appellant's record at the punishment phase.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of the felony offense of possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, weighing less than 28 grams after a jury trial. Appellant raised 23 points of error in his pro se brief, but the court found no error in the pre-trial phase, the trial, or the punishment phase, noting that in a number of instances appellant either failed to object to the trial court or failed to substantiate his allegations.

Ford v. State


No. 01-89-01185-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 103



January 10, 1991, Delivered  
January 10, 1991, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused as Untimely Filed March 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 272nd District Court; Brazos County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 18,453-272.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 272nd District Court, Brazos County (Texas), after he was convicted of capital murder, on the grounds that the trial court erred in overruling his motion for a change of venue due to pretrial publicity and that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 8.07(d) (1991) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant hit the victim in the head with a shotgun several times. Thereafter, appellant and his co-defendant stole the victim's truck and wallet, drove to the mall, and used the victim's credit card to buy three cassette tapes. The case was extensively covered in the news, both on television and in print. During his trial for murder, appellant filed a motion for a change of venue due to the publicity surrounding the case. The trial court denied appellant's motion, and he was convicted of capital murder. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to change venue and that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 8.07 (d) (1991) was unconstitutional because juveniles convicted of capital murder only had one possible punishment, life in prison. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motion for a change of venue, as only two of appellant's five witnesses indicated that appellant could not get a fair trial in Brazos County (Texas) and coverage of the case had been reduced prior to trial. Appellant's position that § 8.07 was unconstitutional was overruled, as he cited no authority to support his position.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellant's motion for a change of venue in his trial for capital murder, as only two of appellant's five witnesses indicated that appellant could not get a fair trial in the county and the coverage of the case in the news had been reduced prior to trial.

Serrano v. State


No. C14-90-00498-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


804 S.W.2d 543; 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 12



January 3, 1991, Rendered  
January 3, 1991, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled February 7, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 451276-A; Mary Bacon, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a surety and the principal on a bail bond, challenged a summary judgment of the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which forfeited the bail bond for appellant principal's failure to appear for trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a surety and the principal on a bail bond, contended that they had never received notice of a change of the trial setting. The court determined that the state, in moving for summary judgment on the bond forfeiture, had the burden of showing there were no genuine issues of material fact as to whether appellant surety had executed a valid and binding bond, whether appellant principal's name had been called at the courthouse door, whether appellant principal had failed to appear, and whether appellant principal had a valid reason for not appearing. The court found that appellants had sufficient notice of the trial setting and that appellants had not presented a valid reason for not appearing. In addition, the court found that appellant principal had not appeared on the former trial setting date and had not appeared any time in the 20 months between judgment nisi and final judgment. Because appellants had not rebutted the essential elements of the state's cause of action, the court affirmed the summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment forfeiting the bond of appellants, a surety and the principal on a bail bond, because the record showed that appellants had sufficient notice of the trial setting and because appellants had not presented adequate proof of a reason for failing to appear.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant executor challenged the order of the 281st District Court of Harris County, Texas, which granted appellee widow's and appellee corporation's motions for summary judgment in appellant's suit to recover damages for wrongful disinterment of decedent's body.


OVERVIEW: Appellee widow had her husband's body moved from one section of appellee corporation's cemetery to another section of the cemetery. Steigerwald v. Rodeheaver


No. B14-90-00020-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 49



January 3, 1991, Rendered

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn March 7, 1991; Substituted Opinion Reported at 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 549. Rehearing Granted March 7, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 295th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 87-31986; Dan Downey, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a judgment from the 295th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted appellant interest on a condemnation award fund and also granted appellant attorney's fees. Appellant challenged the amount of attorney's fees as inadequate. Appellees, county and county officials, cross-appealed the award of interest on the award fund and the award of attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowner deposited money into the registry of the trial court to challenge appellee county's right to condemn his land. Appellee county officials held the money for over two years until appellant withdrew it. When appellee county retained the interest earned on the money, appellant filed a declaratory judgment action asking the trial court to declare the owner of the interest. The trial court determined that appellant was entitled to the interest and attorney's fees. Both appellant and appellees sought review of the judgment. Appellant argued that the jury awarded an inadequate amount as attorney's fees. Concluding that the evidence was factually insufficient to support the amount of attorney's fees, the court reversed the portion of the judgment that awarded attorney's fees and remanded for a new trial on that issue alone. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment, rejecting appellees' challenge to the interest award. Although appellee county was permitted to show the amount it was due for accounting and administrative expenses, it failed to do so and thus waived any right it had to any portion of the interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of a judgment that awarded attorney's fees to appellant landowner in an action to recover interest on a condemnation award fund. The court remanded for a new trial on attorney's fees because the evidence was factually insufficient to support the attorney's fee award. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment, holding that appellant was entitled to recover the interest on the award fund.

General Land Office v. Rutherford Oil Corp.


No. 3-90-037-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


802 S.W.2d 65; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 3008; 118 Oil & Gas Rep. 98



December 19, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 6, 1991. Rehearing Overruled February 6, 1991. As Corrected. Second Amendment. Second Rehearing Overruled March 13, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Granted May 1, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District; No. 433,969, Honorable Joseph H. Hart, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state land office and state oil and gas lessor sought review of an order of the District Court of Travis County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellee oil and gas lessees in a declaratory judgment action brought by appellees to declare that Tex. Nat. Res. Code §§ 52.135 and 52.137 conferred no authority upon appellant to adjudicate the parties' rights under a state mineral lease.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state land office and state oil and gas lessor and appellee oil and gas lessees entered into a mineral lease contract. A dispute arose when appellant asserted a royalty deficiency on appellees' lease. Appellees filed a declaratory judgment action seeking to declare that Tex. Nat. Res. Code §§ 52.135, 52.137 did not confer authority on appellant to adjudicate their rights under the lease contract and requested a temporary injunction prohibiting an agency hearing. The district court granted and later dissolved the injunction. In an interlocutory appeal from the order dissolving the injunction, the court determined that it was probable that appellant did not have power to adjudicate the dispute. Both appellant and appellees filed motions for summary judgment. The district court granted summary judgment to appellees with respect to appellant's right to adjudicate the dispute. The court affirmed, holding that only courts were empowered to determine controverted property rights. The statute at issue allowed appellant to examine accounting-type errors resulting in royalty deficiencies, not make royalty deficiency assessments based upon disputed lease provisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment to appellee oil and gas lessees in a declaratory judgment suit brought by appellees to declare that appellant state land office and state oil and gas lessor did not have statutory power to adjudicate a mineral lease dispute because the statute conferred on appellants powers to audit appellees' books in search of royalty deficiencies, not make deficiency assessments in a disputed lease.

Carrion v. State


No. 3-88-162-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


802 S.W.2d 83; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 3014



December 19, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 23, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Bell County, 264th Judicial District; No. 36,269-K, Honorable Jack W. Prescott, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 264th Judicial District, District Court of Bell County (Texas), which convicted appellant of conspiracy with the intent to commit the offense of aggravated delivery of cocaine over 400 grams.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of conspiracy with the intent to commit the offense of aggravated delivery of cocaine over 400 grams based on jury verdict. Appellant presented five points of error on appeal, including that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss that some of the prosecution's peremptory challenges were based impermissibly on race, and that the trial court erred in its charges to the jury. Appellant, who was of Hispanic origin, objected to the prosecution's challenges directed at three African-American veniremembers. The appellate court noted that the appeals court had, in applying the Batson factors, held that a defendant could not complain unless the excluded veniremembers were of the same race as the defendant. Appellant contended that Tex. Code Crim. P. art. 35.261 had different requirements than Batson and therefore permitted cross-racial strikes. The appellate court held, after an examination of the legislative history, that appellant's contentions were not well founded. The court also rejected appellant's claims that the trial court had incorrectly charged the jury. As such, the court affirmed the lower court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision. The court held that appellant had no standing to object to the peremptory challenge of jury veniremembers that were of a different race than appellant himself.

McBride v. State


Nos. 05-89-01338-CR, 05-89-01339-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


803 S.W.2d 741; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 3207



December 18, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review as to Document Number 05-89-01339-CR Granted April 3, 1991. State's Petition for Discretionary Review as to Document Number 05-89-01338-CR Refused April 3, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 219th District Court Collin County, Texas; Trial Court Cause Nos. 219-80404-89, 219-80446-89.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 219th District Court Collin County, Texas, convicting appellant for burglary of a habitation and engaging in organized criminal activity. On each count, the trial court admitted appellant's confessions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of burglary of a habitation, with a sentence of 15 years in prison, and engaging in organized criminal activity, with a sentence of 60 years in prison. Appellant challenged both convictions, and the court reversed each. As to burglary, the court found that appellant's own description of the location of the burglary was vague, no exact dates were mentioned, no property taken in the burglary was found in appellant's possession, and no other evidence supported the conviction. Therefore, the court found it was not supported by sufficient evidence, and rendered a judgment of acquittal. As to organized criminal activity, the court found that the state had not shown that appellant's confession was voluntary, where appellant claimed he was beaten and the arresting officers did not testify at the suppression hearing to contradict this. In addition, the arresting officers did testify at trial, placing appellant in a dilemma under the Fifth Amendment, because he would be required to give up his right to refuse to testify in order to debate the voluntariness of his confession. Consequently, the court reversed and remanded this charge.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and remanded in part. Appellant was acquitted of burglary of a habitation, because there was insufficient evidence to support a conviction. Appellant's written confessions were improperly admitted on the trial for engaging in organized criminal activity, because the state failed to demonstrate that the confessions were voluntary.

Makeig v. State


No. 07-89-0353-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


802 S.W.2d 59; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 3002



December 14, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 14, 1991. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted March 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 69th Judicial District Court of Moore County; No. 2233; Honorable Bill Sheehan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Court of Appeals Affirmed June 17, 1992.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bondsman challenged an order of the 69th District Court, Moore County (Texas), which entered a judgment of forfeiture on a $ 50,000 bond and, in response to appellant's motion for remittitur after forfeiture, granted a remittitur of $ 25,000 less costs of suit.


OVERVIEW: Appellant bondsman issued an appearance bond. The principal failed to appear and the trial court entered a judgment of forfeiture. Law enforcement officials eventually apprehended the principal. Appellant filed a motion for remittitur after forfeiture in the amount of the bond less costs and interest. The trial court granted partial remittitur in the amount of 50 percent of the bond less costs. Appellant sought review and the court affirmed. The court first determined that the bond was valid because its language provided sufficient identification of the court and the nature of the bonded offense. The court also determined that the trial court did not err when it refused to apply a waiting period specified by statute because that portion of the statute had previously been declared unconstitutional. Finally, the court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion, when it ordered only a 50 percent remittitur, because there was no showing of sufficient cause for the principal's absence, the principal was not apprehended through the efforts of appellant, and appellant had received compensation for the risk appellant endured under the bond.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Partial remittitur on forfeited bail bond was proper when bondsman failed to show sufficient cause for principal's absence, principal was not apprehended through efforts of bondsman, and bondsman was compensated for risk assumed under bond.

State v. McKinney


Nos. C14-90-00453-CR, C14-90-00456-CR, C14-90-00459-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


803 S.W.2d 374; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2968



December 13, 1990, Rendered  
December 13, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 2; Fort Bend County, Texas; Trial Court Cause Nos. 43,231, 43,232, 43,233; Walter S. McMeans, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from three orders of the County Court at Law No. 2 (Texas) granting motions to quash three misdemeanor complaints charging appellee with disorderly conduct. The state argued that the trial court abused its discretion in finding Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 42.01(a)(2) (1989) unconstitutionally overboard as applied to appellee in the absence of facts to support such findings.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was charged with disorderly conduct in three separate but identical complaints. Appellee pled no contest, then perfected appeals to the trial court. In the trial court, appellee filed identical motions to quash the complaints. The trial court granted all three motions to quash. On appeal, the state argued that the trial court abused its discretion in finding Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 42.01(a)(2) (1989) unconstitutionally overboard as applied to appellee in the absence of facts to support such findings. The appeals court dismissed the state's appeals. The court reasoned that the appeals were filed 16 days after the trial court signed and entered the orders. Because the state had no legal power to appeal the cases once the 15-day limit set out in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 44.01(d) had expired, the court erred in granting the state's motion to extend time for filing the notices of appeal.


OUTCOME: The appeals court dismissed the state's appeal because the state's notice of appeal was filed 16 days after the trial court signed and entered the orders. The court ruled that the state's substantive authority to appeal was limited after its 15-day deadline expired.

Kendrick v. Lynaugh


No. A14-89-00966-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


804 S.W.2d 153; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2990



December 13, 1990, Rendered  
December 13, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication January 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 278th District Court; Walker County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 16,689-C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a judgment of the 278th District Court (Texas) dismissing his pro se in forma pauperis action against appellee corrections department, director, and other officials as frivolous. Appellant argued that the trial court abused its discretion in dismissing his application for an injunction without a hearing upon an unverified pleading.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate sued appellee corrections department, director, and other officials under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 106.001 and entitled his complaint "Tort Claims." Upon the motion of appellees, the trial court dismissed the complaint with prejudice as frivolous. Appellant argued that the trial court abused its discretion in dismissing appellant's application for an injunction without a hearing upon an unverified pleading. Appellant urged that because appellee director's pleadings were unverified, Tex. R. Civ. P. 690 required that a final hearing be conducted before appellant's petition was dismissed. The appeals court affirmed. The court ruled that the "final hearing" required by Tex. R. Civ. P. 690 was necessary only where the defendant was seeking to have a temporary injunction abated on the basis of allegations contained in his or her non-verified answer, thereby preventing a defendant from dissolving a temporary injunction already in place without proof verified by the oath of the defendant. Because appellant never obtained a temporary injunction, rule 690 was not applicable in this case.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court judgment dismissing appellant's pro se in forma pauperis action against appellee corrections department, director, and other officials as frivolous. The court ruled that no final hearing was required because appellees were not seeking to have a temporary injunction abated on the basis of allegations contained in the non-verified answer.

All Valley Acceptance Co. v. Durfey


No. 3-88-248-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


800 S.W.2d 672; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2961; 13 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 1376



December 12, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled January 16, 1991. Released for Publication January 16, 1991. Application for Writ of Error Denied March 27, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 200th Judicial District; No. 424-412-A, Honorable Paul R. Davis, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant secured party challenged a judgment of the District Court of Travis County (Texas) in favor of appellee debtors in a breach of contract action, based on appellant's failure to give notice of sale of the collateral upon appellees' default. Appellant contended the court erred because appellees renounced or modified their right to notice of the resale.


OVERVIEW: Appellee debtors suffered allergic reactions to formaldehyde used in constructing their manufactured home. Appellees' attorney sent a letter to appellant secured party seeking to settle the matter. Appellant later repossessed the home with appellees' consent. Appellant sent a notice of sale to appellees, then four days later entered into a contract with a third party. Appellees filed suit for breach of the installment purchase contract. The trial court entered judgment for appellees. On appeal, appellant contended the trial court erred because appellees renounced or modified their right to notice of the resale. The appeals court affirmed. The court ruled that the attorney's letter did not constitute a modification or renunciation under Tex. Bus. & Com. Code § 9.504 (1991) because it was not signed by appellees and did not mention a waiver of their right to notice. Moreover, because the notice sent by appellant contained a different date than the actual date of sale, there was no genuine issue of material fact as to whether appellees received reasonable notice. Thus, because damages were specifically provided for in the statute, appellees were not required to prove actual damages.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court judgment in favor of appellee debtors because there was no genuine issue of material fact as to whether appellees received reasonable notice. The court also ruled that a letter from appellees' attorney to appellant secured party did not constitute a modification or renunciation because it was not signed by appellees and did not mention a waiver of their right to notice.

Yohey v. State


Appeal Nos. 04-88-00215-CR, 04-88-00216-CR

December 12, 1990, Delivered  
December 12, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 227th District Court of Bexar County; Trial Court Nos. 85-CR-3303 and 85-CR-3304; Honorable Mike M. Machado, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought relief from his conviction in the 227th District Court of Bexar County (Texas) for the murder of his estranged wife and her friend. Appellant was separately indicted for the offenses. The indictments were consolidated for trial. The jury assessed punishment in each cause at life imprisonment and a fine of $ 10,000.00.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his wife had separated and were in the process of getting a divorce. In the early morning hours, appellant entered his estranged wife's apartment with a key, and had with him a loaded nine-millimeter pistol. When his wife and a friend entered the apartment, they were shot and killed. Appellant was indicted separately for the offenses, which were consolidated for trial, and he was convicted of murder. The court affirmed conviction, finding no error by the trial court in consolidating the two causes for trial, in overruling the motion to quash the indictments for failure to give notice which particular gun was used in the deaths of the victims, and in not declaring mistrial when insurance was mentioned. The court held that the trial court did not err in requiring appellant to turn over his statement of the case to state after it had been used by his psychiatrist expert witness, on not appointing a psychiatrist until eleven days before trial, and in allowing state to call rebuttal witnesses. The court held it was not improper to permit a police officer to testify regarding how long he believed the alleged victims had been dead at the time he arrived at the scene.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's murder convictions, finding that the court did not err by consolidating the two causes, by not quashing indictments, and by not granting appellant a mistrial. The court found no error by the way the trial court handled issues concerning appellant's psychiatrist expert witness. The court also found no error by the trial court in permitting police officer to express his opinion as to how long victims had been dead.

Central Power & Light Co. v. Caballero


Appeal No. 04-90-00112-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


804 S.W.2d 534; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 3213; 2 Am. Disabilities Cas. (BNA) 857



December 12, 1990, Delivered  
December 12, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 293rd District Court of Maverick County; Trial Court No. 9313; Honorable Eugene D. Stewart, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of the decision of the 293rd District Court of Maverick County (Texas) that entered judgment in favor of appellee employee in his action alleging employment discrimination based on a handicap under the Commission on Human Rights Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5221k.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employer sought review after a jury returned a verdict in favor of appellee employee in his action for employment discrimination that was filed pursuant to the Commission on Human Rights Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 5221k. The appellate court reversed the judgment because appellee failed to comply with the act. The court found that appellee's failure to follow the mandates of the act resulted in reversible error because appellant was deprived of a hearing to determine whether the lower court would enjoin any unlawful employment practice, deprived of a hearing to determine whether it had failed to comply with an order of a court, deprived of the equitable principles with which a court, but not a jury, was familiar, and deprived of any consideration of the credits to which it was entitled for payments made. The court also determined that there was nothing in the act that provided for recovery of loss of future earning capacity, and because appellee based his case entirely on the act, he was limited to those damages it authorized.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment in favor of appellee employee, finding that he did not follow the dictates of the Commission on Human Rights Act and that, as a result, appellant employer was deprived of hearings mandated under the act, a review of the applicable equitable principals involved, and any consideration of the monetary credits to which it might have been entitled.

Lara v. State


No 13-89-275-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


800 S.W.2d 387; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2871



November 29, 1990, Delivered  
November 29, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled December 13, 1990. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused March 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 275th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 275th District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas), which convicted him of involuntary manslaughter by using a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Appellant went to his bedroom and, in the dark, emptied the bullets out of the barrel of his gun. He then returned with the gun to show his friends. While walking back to his bedroom pulling the gun's trigger, one friend stepped in front of him and appellant accidentally shot and killed him. Appellant was unaware that his gun was still loaded. Appellant and convicted of involuntary manslaughter. Appellant challenged his conviction, arguing error in denying his pretrial motion to halt the felony prosecution and his post-trial motion to set aside his conviction because the legislature's attempt to distinguish between culpable mental states for recklessness and for criminal negligence were distinctions without difference. Appellant argued that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.05(a)(1), was unconstitutional as applied. The court affirmed the conviction, holding Tex. Penal Code § 6.03(c), and Tex. Penal Code § 6.03(d), did not define the same culpable mental states, nor did one definition include any portion of the other. The court held that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.05(a)(1), and Tex. Penal Code § 19.07 (1989), did not penalize the same conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment convicting appellant of involuntary manslaughter because the mental states of recklessness and criminal negligence were sufficiently different so as to not define the same culpable mental states, and neither definition included any portion of the other.

Willis v. State


No. 05-85-00569-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


802 S.W.2d 337; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 3133



November 29, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled January 9, 1991. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 282nd District Court; Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. F-85-97073-JS.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was convicted of theft. Originally, the court reversed the conviction, holding that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(a), was constitutional as applied to appellant's case and that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on his good faith purchase defense. The Criminal Court of Appeals (Texas), affirmed the court's holding as to the constitutionality of § 31.03(a), but reversed and remanded as to the jury instruction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant jeweler was convicted of theft by purchasing stolen property. The court originally reversed his conviction, holding that the trial court erred in refusing to give his requested jury instruction as to his good faith purchase defense. The criminal court of appeals reversed and remanded this judgment for the court to determine whether appellant's requested instruction was sufficient to inform the trial court that a proper instruction on mistake of fact was to be given. The court held that the requested instruction was sufficient to put the trial court on notice, but that the charge was sufficient and the error in omitting the statutory definition of mistake of fact set forth in Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 8.02(a) (1974), was harmless. The court held that it was not error to submit a charge on the law of parties because it limited the application of the presumption of knowledge to appellant and his mental state and not to appellant's son. The court held that court granted appellant's requested instruction on the law of accomplice testimony, it was not powerless to amend the charge. The court held that there was no fatal variance between the indictment and the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of theft by purchasing stolen property because the trial court's instruction to the jury on mistake of fact was adequate without a statutory definition. The instructions on the law of parties and accomplice testimony were also sufficient.

Ross v. State


No. 05-89-01352-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


802 S.W.2d 308; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 3125



November 26, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from County Criminal Court of Appeals No. 1; Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. MC89-R0007-D.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convicted of disorderly conduct sought review of judgment from County Criminal Court of Appeals No. 1, Dallas County, Texas that affirmed the trial court decision. Appellant contended that her trial counsel rendered ineffective assistance, that the municipal court should have quashed her complaint, that the statute under which she was charged was unconstitutionally vague, and that the words she used were not fighting words.


OVERVIEW: Appellant convicted of disorderly conduct contended on review that her trial counsel rendered ineffective assistance, that the municipal court should have quashed her complaint, that the statute under which she was charged was unconstitutionally vague, and that the words she used were not fighting words. The court held that appellant failed to show a deficiency in her counsel's actions and that she was prejudiced. The court concluded that counsel's acts or omissions were not outside the range of professional competent assistance and that a different outcome would not have occurred but for his actions. The court also found that the municipal court correctly overruled appellant's motion to quash. The court reasoned that the statute under which appellant was charged was not too vague. The court held that the statute provided explicit standards. The court found that the state introduced sufficient evidence to show that appellant's words not only tended to incite a breach of the peace, but that she actually did incite a breach of the peace. The court also held that a review of the record showed that the state met its burden of proof. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellant of disorderly conduct was affirmed because the court held that counsel's acts or omissions were not outside the range of professional competent assistance, the complaint used to charge appellant fully met the requirements of the statute, and the state provided sufficient evidence that appellant's conduct incited a breach of the peace in an area accessible to a substantial group of the public.

Puckett v. State

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 12th District Court, Walker County (Texas), which revoked his probation and sentenced him to five years confinement for failure to comply with terms of his probation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested for retaliation. An officer testified that appellant on several occasions was verbally abusive toward him and threatened him. Appellant was convicted of retaliation under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 36.061 (1990). Appellant was placed on felony probation for five years. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the case finding that appellant's sufficiency of the evidence argument was without merit, that the statute he was convicted under was not facially unconstitutional, and that his threats were not constitutionally protected because he intended to make threatening statements to the officer and they were in fact threatening in nature.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmates sought review of the decision from the 278th District Court, Walker County (Texas) that dismissed their pro se in forma pauperis action, pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001, which appellants had brought against appellees, the department of criminal justice director and unit warden, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmates sued appellees, the department of criminal justice director and unit warden, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claiming unconstitutional conditions of confinement and seeking monetary and injunctive relief. Specifically, appellants complained of physical injury from excessive television noise emanating from five televisions located adjacent to their living cells but beyond their view. Since one appellant had initiated such suit and it was not brought to the trial court's attention, the court could not consider it. The court found that appellants failed to allege the deprivation of a valid constitutional right. A noise-free prison environment was not a fundamental right and appellants were clearly not members of a suspect class. The judgment was affirmed.

Valenzuela v. Aquino

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


800 S.W.2d 301; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2752



November 15, 1990, Delivered  
November 15, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing overruled December 13, 1990. Application for writ of error granted May 1, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 94th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant picketers challenged a decision from the 94th District Court of Nueces County (Texas), in favor of appellee doctor and his family awarding appellees actual and punitive damages, and issuing a permanent injunction prohibiting appellants from the further picketing of appellees' residence.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted an injunction, and actual and punitive fees to appellee doctor and his family, in an action for negligent infliction of emotional distress arising from appellants' picketing of appellees' residence. On appeal, appellants challenged the injunction's constitutionality. They argued that the injunction violated U.S. Const. amend. I and Tex. Const. art. I, § 8.The court found that the injunction constituted a content-neutral, narrowly tailored limitation on the place and manner of appellants' expressive activities and ample alternative avenues of communication existed. The court overruled this point of error. Appellants further challenged the constitutionality of the award of actual and punitive damages. The court found that appellees were not public figures and thus might not recover damages for emotional harm negligently caused by the exercise of expressive activity protected by U.S. Const. amend. I. The court reversed the award of damages. Appellants contended that an award of attorney fees was inadequate. The court found appellees were not state actors and thus could not be held liable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The court reversed the award.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the permanent injunction in favor of appellee doctor and his family and against appellant picketers. The court reversed and rendered the trial court's judgment awarding damages on the grounds that appellees were not public figures and thus not entitled to damages. The court reversed and rendered the trial court's judgment regarding the award of attorney fees against appellees because they were not state actors.

 

1679 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Lone Star Gas Co. v. Railroad Comm'n


No. 3-88-012-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


798 S.W.2d 888; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2728; 117 Oil & Gas Rep. 152



November 14, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]  Released for Publication December 19, 1990. Application for Writ of Error Granted March 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 299th Judicial District, No. 414,537, Honorable Joe B. Dibrell, Judge Presiding.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of December 13, 1989, Reported at 1989 Tex. App. LEXIS 3255.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the court had reversed the trial court's order dismissing appellant companies' suit seeking a declaration as to the validity and applicability of certain rules promulgated by appellee state railroad commission, the Supreme Court (Texas) reversed the court's decision and remanded the cause to the court to render an opinion on whether the rules were valid despite the posture of the case.


OVERVIEW: Appellee state railroad commission promulgated rules governing the natural gas industry in response to the creation of special marketing programs. Appellant companies filed suit in the trial court seeking a declaration as to the validity and applicability of the ratable take and proration rules promulgated by appellee. After a trial on the merits, the trial court rendered judgment that appellee did not exceed its authority by enacting the rules, but dismissed the cause for lack of ripeness. The court initially reversed the trial court's dismissal, but following an appeal the court was directed to rule on whether appellee's rules were valid. Appellants argued that federal law preempted the challenged rules. The court agreed and held that the rules were invalid. The rules in question came within the limits of the comprehensive Natural Gas Policy Act of 1978, 15 U.S.C.S. §§ 3301-3432, scheme, and they conflicted with the federal interest in low gas prices. The rules sought to regulate federally regulated purchasers of natural gas. Thus, the rules were preempted by federal law and invalid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and declared the challenged rules invalid because federal law, the Natural Gas Policy Act of 1978, preempted the challenged rules.

 

1680 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State Com. on Judicial Conduct v. Gist


No. 3-88-252-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2729



November 14, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn by Order of the Court December 12, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District; No. 401,177, Honorable Joseph H. Hart, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Texas Commission on Judicial Conduct challenged the order of the District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District (Texas), which declared that appellant's public reprimand of appellee judge for appellee's sentencing practice was void.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Texas Commission on Judicial Conduct publicly reprimanded appellee judge for appellee's sentencing practices. Appellee sought a declaration that the reprimand was void, and the trial court held that it was void. The court affirmed and held that appellant violated Tex. Const. art. II, § 1, and art. V, § 1 by acting in a judicial rather than an administrative capacity. The court held that appellant interpreted the law rather than applied the facts to determine the law, which appellant was not empowered to do. The court concluded that a judge could not be held to have "willfully" violated the Texas Code of Judicial Conduct for erroneous legal rulings unless the judge acted with bad faith, and the preponderance of the evidence did not show bad faith. The court also held that appellee was entitled to attorney's fees pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 104.001.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that the public reprimand of appellee judge was void, because appellant Texas Commission on Judicial Conduct violated the state constitution by acting in a judicial capacity and the preponderance of the evidence did not show that appellee acted in bad faith.
