Fox v. State


No. B14-89-00692-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


801 S.W.2d 173; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2701



November 8, 1990, Rendered  
November 8, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled December 6, 1990. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law Number Nine; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 8842454; Neil McKay, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of a judgment from the Criminal Court at Law, Harris County (Texas) which convicted him under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.05(a)(2) (1989) of hindering the apprehension of his client.


OVERVIEW: When appellant attorney appeared in court with his client, a court coordinator advised that the client was going to be arrested pursuant to two open warrants. The court coordinator agreed to reset the case on the condition that appellant tell his client to remain in the courtroom. After the court coordinator signed the reset form, appellant, using a hand signal, motioned for the client to exit the courtroom with him. Appellant was subsequently tried and convicted for hindering apprehension, a violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 38.05(a)(2) (1989). On appeal, the court held that § 38.05(a)(2) was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad. The court also rejected appellant's contentions that the statute infringed on his constitutionally protected right of freedom of speech and interfered with his right to counsel his client. The court affirmed the conviction, finding that appellant engaged in a continuing course of conduct which aided his client in evading arrest after he was advised by the court coordinator that there were two open arrest warrants for his client.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant attorney's conviction for hindering apprehension, because he engaged in a continuing course of conduct that aided his client in evading arrest after he was advised by the court coordinator that there were two open arrest warrants for his client.

 

1682 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Evans v. Henry Industrial Park, Inc.


No. 01-90-00150-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2710



November 8, 1990, Rendered  
November 8, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 269th District Court of Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 81-34350.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged an interlocutory order, from the 269th District Court, Harris County (Texas), directing a receiver to obtain funds owed to appellants by a casualty company in order to satisfy a judgment owed to appellees, arguing that the turnover order was in error because a reversal and remand required a new trial on the merits.


OVERVIEW: Appellants sought review from an interlocutory order that appointed a receiver, and directed the receiver to obtain money from a casualty company that purportedly owed money to appellants, in order to satisfy a judgment owed to appellees, contending that the lower court erred by entering a turnover order because a reversal and remand by the appellate court contemplated a new trial on the merits. On appeal, the lower court judgment was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court held that it could find no authority that provided that when an appellate court reversed and remanded a specific order, a new trial of the entire case was necessary. The court further explained that such a result would violate logic, judicial economy, and the rights of the parties. The court, thus, found that it seemed clear that such a reversal and remand was limited to specific fact issues did not reopen the case in its entirely. The court added that appellants had failed to request a new trial.


OUTCOME: The lower court judgment was affirmed because the court found that a new trial on the merits was not indicated when the reversal and remand was limited to specific fact issues.

 

1683 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. Windham


No. B14-89-01052-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


803 S.W.2d 340; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2629



November 1, 1990, Rendered  
November 1, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled November 29, 1990. Application for Writ of Error Granted April 3, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 2; Brazos County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 208-CC; J. D. Langley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the judgment of the County Court at Law No. 2 of Brazos County (Texas) in a condemnation proceeding against appellee landowners, based on the trial court's grant of appellee's motion in limine relating to the determination of the value of the property condemned, and the trial court's rejection of appellant's tenders of proof regarding the value of the property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state condemned a portion of appellees landowners' property in order to widen a state highway. All matters, aside from the issue of adequate consideration, were determined before trial. The trial court granted appellees' motion in limine to consider only a portion of the entire tract owned by appellees in considering the value of the land taken. The trial court also denied appellant's judgment of proof as to value, and the jury returned a verdict, assessing the value of the condemned land. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court ruled that, based on Tex. Const. art. 1, § 17, the land taken from the state was to be valued without consideration of surrounding land. Moreover, the court held that Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 21.042(e), which provided for considering any benefit that arose from the highway improvement in considering the value of condemned land, was unconstitutional and inapplicable because the Tex. Const. art. 1, § 17 could not be changed without constitutional amendment or a finding by the Texas Supreme Court that such a change was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because the trial court did not err in granting appellees landowners' motion in limine regarding the consideration of the value of condemned property, nor did it err in denying appellant state's judgment of proof as to the property's value.

 

1684 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Baker v. Howard


No. 10-89-164-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


799 S.W.2d 450; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2736



October 25, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From 170th Judicial District Court; McLennan County, Texas; Trial Court No. 88-1601-4.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the District Court of McLennan County (Texas), awarding appellant the balance due on the defaulted note and loan agreement between appellant and appellee less the penalty for usurious interest set forth in Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 5069.


OVERVIEW: Appellant loaned appellee four advances of funds. Appellant agreed to finance the loan over a period of seven years, at fifteen percent interest per annum. The loan agreement between the parties was oral. Appellant testified that they decided the monthly payment amount based on an amortization book. Appellee did not execute a promissory note or any other instrument evidencing the loan. After the terms of the loan had been agreed upon, appellant gave appellee a printed amortization schedule setting forth the amount of the loan, the rate of interest, and the required payment amount under the original agreement. After appellee made eight payments, he quit paying on the loan. Appellant filed suit against appellee. The trial court awarded appellant the balance due on the note less the penalty for usurious interest set forth in Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 5069. The trial court concluded that the interest charged on the loan was usurious as a matter of law. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision because the oral agreement exceeded the maximum legal rate of interest that the parties could have agreed upon orally for the loan which was ten percent per annum.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the decision awarding appellant the balance due on the defaulted note and loan agreement between appellant and appellee less the statutory penalty for usurious interest because the trial court was justified in determining that the parties merely intended and used the amortization schedule as evidence of the prior completed oral contract of the loan transaction, thus the fifteen percent loan rate was usurious.

Marshall v. State


Nos. 2-89-201-CV, 2-89-202-CV, 2-89-203-CV, 2-89-204-CV, 2-89-205-CV, 2-89-206-CV, 2-89-207-CV, 2-89-208-CV, 2-89-209-CV, 2-89-210-CV, 2-89-211-CV, 2-89-212-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


797 S.W.2d 698; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2674



October 16, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 213th District Court of Tarrant County, Hon. George Kredell.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bondsman sought review of the decision by the 213th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) to charge appellant interest calculated from the date of judgment nisi to the entry of a final judgment remitting bonds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant bondsman entered into 12 separate bail bonds conditioned on the appearance of defendants in each case. After the defendants failed to appear a judgment nisi was entered against appellant and the defendants. The state mailed appellant a bill directing him to pay interest calculated from the judgment nisi date to the entry of the final judgment remitting the bond. Appellant contested the assessment of interest. Appellant argued that it was improper to assess prejudgment interest prior to the final judgment because there was no ascertainable sum due until that point. The appellate court disagreed and concluded that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.16(e) (1989) did not actually provide for prejudgment interest, but rather required payment of interest on the bond amount. The court also stated that the date of forfeiture was the date the defendants failed to appear and not the final judgment date. The court did remand two of the bail bonds to the trial court because those bonds were not subject to the new version of art. 22.16 and the old version did not permit interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's determination that appellant bondsman owed interest on bonds from the judgment nisi date to the date of final judgment because the most recent statute permitted recovery of the interest.

Tai Tien Lam v. State


No. 01-89-00401-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2504



October 11, 1990, Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 89-02446.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant offender challenged a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County, Texas, which convicted him of selling obscene material based on entry of his plea of nolo contendere.


OVERVIEW: Appellant offender sought relief from his conviction of selling obscene material, which was based on his nolo contendere plea. The court found that it had previously ruled that the Texas obscenity law was not unconstitutionally overbroad in violation of Tex. Const. art. I, § 8, and that the inclusion of the phrase "on any subject" in art. I, § 8 did not provide any greater protection than U. S. Const. amend. I. The court pointed out that it had already ruled against appellant's argument that the Texas obscenity statute was indefinite, uncertain, and vague. The court found that there was timely and proper determination of obscenity and that appellant admitted to every element of the offense in his nolo contendere plea and his conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant offender's conviction for selling obscene material because it had already ruled that the Texas obscenity law was not overbroad, indefinite, uncertain, and vague. Further, appellant admitted to each element of the offense in his nolo contendere plea.

Ex parte Benavides


No. 01-89-00935-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


801 S.W.2d 535; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2518



October 11, 1990, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Dismissed for Want of Jurisdiction October 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 12th District Court; Walker County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 16,326.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the order of the 12th District Court, Walker County, Texas, which dismissed his pro se application for writ of habeas corpus as frivolous under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001(a)(2) (1990).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought relief from the dismissal of his pro se application for writ of habeas corpus by the trial court, pursuant to Tex. Civ. Prac. &b Rem. Code Ann. § 13.001 (1990), on the grounds that it was frivolous. Appellant claimed the statute under which the trial court dismissed his complaint was unconstitutional, but the court held that ruling on the constitutionality of the statute was not necessary to decide the case and therefore declined to rule on it. The court found that appellant did not challenge the legality of his confinement but only complained of the terms and conditions of his imprisonment and certain management acts and that the record showed no illegal restraint for which habeas corpus relief could be granted. The court ruled that the trial court did not err in dismissing appellant's application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment denying appellant inmate's application for habeas corpus because ruling on the constitutionality of the statute permitting a finding of frivolity was not necessary to decide the case, and appellant challenged the conditions of his confinement rather than its legality, making habeas corpus action inappropriate.

Shannon v. State


Appeal No. 04-89-00320-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


800 S.W.2d 896; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 3149



October 10, 1990, Delivered  
October 10, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 7 of Bexar County; Trial Court No. 404,007; Honorable Tony Jimenez, III, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of County Court at Law No. 7 of Bexar County (Texas), which found defendant guilty of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: In defendant's trial for driving while intoxicated, the arresting officer testified concerning defendant's appearance and physical condition. Defendant's vehicle was impounded and searched. The court held that defendant's motion to suppress evidence found in the search of his vehicle was properly denied because it was incident to defendant's arrest. A certified breath test operator testified that he performed an intoxilyzer test that showed an alcohol concentration of 0.18 percent. The breath test technical supervisor testified that the machine upon which defendant was tested was approved and certified, that the intoxilyzer operated on generally accepted scientific principles, and was regarded as accurate by the scientific community. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701l-5, § 3(a)(b), and the Texas Breath Alcohol Testing Regulations. The court found that the provisions ensured accuracy and did not violate due process. The court held that the jury was free to disregard testimony from defendant's experts and that evidence presented by the state was sufficient for the admissibility of the test results.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated was affirmed because the statutes provided for the admissibility of intoxilyzer results and the rulemaking authority given to the Department of Public Safety was not an unconstitutional delegation of authority and the regulations promulgated ensured the accuracy of the tests and did not violate due process.

Bexar County Appraisal Review Bd. v. First Baptist Church


Appeal No. 04-89-00543-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


800 S.W.2d 892; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 3155



October 10, 1990, Delivered  
October 10, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Granted April 17, 1991. Withdrawn and Replaced by Order of the Court January 20, 1993, Reported at 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 538. Appellants' Motion for Rehearing Denied January 20, 1993, Reported at 1993 Tex. App. LEXIS 538.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 224th District Court of Bexar County; Trial Court No. 84-CI-20348; Honorable Carolyn H. Spears, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county review board and county appraisal district, challenged the judgement of the 224th District Court of Bexar County, Texas, which found that appellee church'ss property was exempt from property taxes as being used primarily for religious purposes under Tex. Prop. Tax Code Ann. § 11.20.


OVERVIEW: Appellee church owned property that was leased to a company as a parking lot during work hours. Appellee, sought a property tax exemption on the property, which was denied by appellants, county review board and county appraisal district. Appellee challenged appellants' ruling. The lower court found that under Tex. Prop. Tax Code Ann. § 11.20 the property was primarily used for religious purposes. Appellants challenged the finding. The court reversed the finding and rendered judgment finding that the property was not exempt property under the statute. The court found that the proper inquiry was not the primary reason that appellee owned the property or how much use and enjoyment appellee got from the property, but what the actual use of the property was. The court found that the record contained no evidence that the property was used primarily for religious purposes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and rendered judgment in favor of appellants, county review board and county appraisal district, holding that the lots in question were not exempt from taxation because their actual use was not primarily for religious purposes.

Ortega v. State


No. B14-89-00791-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2406



October 4, 1990, Rendered  
October 4, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Overruled November 1, 1990. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 177th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 520,440.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 177th Judicial District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of felony driving while intoxicated and sentenced him to four years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant drove his vehicle into the rear of a school bus that was unloading children. He was convicted of felony driving while intoxicated. On appeal, the court held that, absent a showing of bad faith, state's failure to preserve a blood sample so that he could have an ethanol concentration test performed did not constitute a denial of due process. The court held that appellant was not entitled to an instruction on voluntariness under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.22, § 7, because appellant was not under custodial interrogation when he admitted drinking before the collision. The court held that appellant failed to preserve error on several issues because he failed to provide any supporting authority, failed to object at trial, or it concerned evidence admitted without objection by another source. The court held that state could comment on the failure of appellant to call witnesses who were available to testify, could answer opposing counsel's arguments, and could summarize the evidence presented. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to support appellant's conviction based on eyewitness testimony, medical records, and appellant's own admission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for felony driving while intoxicated because there was sufficient evidence to support the verdict. Appellant failed to demonstrate bad faith in connection with state's failure to preserve appellant's blood sample. Appellant's statement that he had been drinking before the collision was admissible and did not require a voluntariness instruction because he was not in custody when he made the statement.

Fed. Deposit Ins. Corp. v. F & A Equip. Leasing


No. 05-89-00487-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


800 S.W.2d 231; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2895



September 24, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 14th District Court, Dallas County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 86-13750-A.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: As successor in interest to an insolvent bank, appellant federal deposit insurance corporation, in its corporate capacity, challenged the judgment of the 14th District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which was rendered in favor of appellee leasing corporation on its claims against the insolvent bank for deceptive trade practices, negligence, fraud, impairment of collateral, and breach of fiduciary duty.


OVERVIEW: A bank sued appellee leasing corporation for the collection of three promissory notes, originally executed by appellee and later assumed by two individuals. The notes were collateralized by certain equipment. Based on the bank's advice, appellee delivered the equipment to the two individuals after they assumed the notes. No additional financing statements were filed. Thereafter, the equipment disappeared. Appellee countersued for, among other things, fraud and breach of fiduciary duty. The jury found in appellee's favor. The bank was declared insolvent while the appeal was pending. Appellant federal deposit insurance corporation was appointed receiver and was substituted as a party to the appeal. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case so that appellant could seek collection on the notes. Appellee's claims failed as a matter of federal law. Appellant's appointment as receiver, while the appeal was pending, caused all evidence introduced at trial of matters extraneous to banking records to have been erroneously admitted, and appellee could not rely on any defenses arising out of representations which were not evidenced in the official loan documents.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment rendered in appellee leasing corporation's favor on its claims against an insolvent bank and remanded the case so that appellant federal deposit insurance corporation could seek collection of the promissory notes executed by appellee. Because appellant was appointed receiver while the judgment was on appeal, appellee's claims against the insolvent bank were no longer viable.

Ex Parte Palomo


No. 01-90-00536-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2356



September 20, 1990, Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 209th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 558264.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his extradition to face charges of grand theft before the 209th District Court, Harris County (Texas), arguing that the supporting affidavit for the governor's warrant was void and did not substantially charge him with a crime in California.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was to be extradited to answer to charges of grand theft. He argued that the supporting affidavit for the governor's warrant was void and did not substantially charge him with a crime in California because no court seal or stamp was affixed to the jurat in the affidavit. The court held that the jurat was sufficient because it was dated and it showed the official capacity of the officer taking it. The supporting affidavit was not void or fundamentally defective. Appellant also asserted that the information failed to give him proper notice of whether the charged offense was a felony or a misdemeanor. The court held that appellant had been put on notice of the offense with which he was charged and the precise punishment range. The judgment denying appellant habeas corpus relief and remanding him to custody for extradition to California was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellant habeas corpus relief and remanded him to custody for extradition to California. The court held that the jurat was sufficient because it was dated and it showed the official capacity of the officer taking it.

Bullock v. Marathon Oil Co.


Nos. 3-89-216-CV, 3-89-217-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


798 S.W.2d 353; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2476; 115 Oil & Gas Rep. 209



September 19, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication November 28, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 261st Judicial District, Nos. 420,254 and 420,255, Honorable Joseph H. Hart, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, comptroller, attorney general and state treasurer, sought review of the judgment from the District Court of Travis County, 261st Judicial District (Texas) which granted appellees, oil companies, summary judgment in their action to recover franchise taxes paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, oil companies, filed suit to recover franchise taxes that they paid under protest. Appellants, comptroller, attorney general and state treasurer, challenged the trial court's grant of summary judgment. Appellees reported "barter exchange agreements" as gross receipts and were taxed by appellants. Appellees contended that the exchanges of oil for oil should have been excluded because appellee comptroller's long-standing interpretation of Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 171.103 and 171.105 (1982 and 1989). Appellants contended that appellee comptroller merely corrected his interpretation of the statutes. The court noted that that legislature had amended the law without having made any substantial change before appellee comptroller changed its interpretation. The court stated that if an agency interpretation was in effect at the time the legislature amended the law without making any substantial change in the statute, the legislature was deemed to have accepted the agency's interpretation. The court concluded that appellee comptroller could not change his long-standing statutory interpretation unless there was clear legislative authorization to do so.


OUTCOME: The trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellants, oil companies, was affirmed because appellee comptroller could not change his long-standing statutory interpretation of an ambiguous statute unless there was clear legislative authority to have done so.

 

1694 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


747, Inc. v. 2618, Inc.


No. 01-89-01248-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2311



September 13, 1990, Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Application for Writ of Error Denied February 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 295th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 86-52952-B.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a city and a corporation, sought review of a 295th District Court, Harris County (Texas), decision that entered a declaratory judgment in favor of appellee corporation that decided the competing claims of appellant corporation and appellee to a permit for the operation of a sexually-oriented business. Appellants contended that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to grant the declaratory relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a city and a corporation, challenged the trial court's entry of declaratory judgment in favor of appellee corporation deciding the competing claims of appellant corporation and appellee regarding a permit for the operation of a sexually-oriented business. Appellants argued that the trial court did not have jurisdiction to grant the declaratory relief. The court reversed the trial court's declaratory judgment and remanded with instructions to dismiss appellee's counterclaim for declaratory relief. The trial court lacked jurisdiction to construe the sexually-oriented business ordinance because appellee's allegation that the ordinance was wrongfully interpreted did not confer jurisdiction upon the trial court to render declaratory relief. Appellee did not plead that the ordinance was unconstitutional or that its enforcement would result in irreparable harm to a vested properly right. The trial court did not have jurisdiction to review appellant city's administrative decision that denied appellee's permit application. The ordinance was enacted pursuant to Tex. Local Gov't Code Ann. § 243.003 (1990), and no appeal of appellee city's decision was statutorily permitted.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's declaratory judgment in sexually-oriented business permit dispute and remanded for dismissal of appellee corporation's declaratory relief request. Appellee's allegation that the penal ordinance was wrongfully interrupted, without allegations that the ordinance was unconstitutional or violated vested property rights, did not give the trial court jurisdiction to review appellant city's administrative decision.

 

1695 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Graham v. Lakewood Village


No. 2-89-276-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


796 S.W.2d 800; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2628



September 5, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled October 30, 1990. Application for Writ of Error Denied March 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 211th District Court of Denton County; R. C. Vaughan, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of a judgment of the 211th District Court of Denton County (Texas) that held them responsible for monthly charges imposed by appellee city on their vacant lots because of the availability of water service.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owners brought suit seeking a declaratory judgment that an ordinance enacted by appellee city that established a standby fee for all vacant lots that had water and sewer service immediately available was unconstitutional. Appellants also sought an injunction against the enforcement of the ordinance. After the trial court denied the relief requested and held appellants responsible for the monthly fees, appellants sought review and contended that the trial court erred in declaring the fee against a non-user was a legal fee, not an illegal tax, within the meaning of Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 51.032 and 402.001 et seq. The court found that the monthly charge to owners of vacant lots adjacent to the water and sewer system, but not hooked on to the system, constituted an illegal tax to the owners. Appellants also argued that the trial court abused its discretion in awarding appellee attorney's fees. The court held that the trial court had discretion in the award of attorney's fees. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court holding appellants responsible for monthly charges on their vacant lots because of the availability of water service because it found that the fees were an illegal tax. The court remanded the cause to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1696 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Bailout Bonding Co. v. State


No. 05-90-00439-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


797 S.W.2d 275; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2651



September 5, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court No. 3, Dallas County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. F88-80915-PJ.



DISPOSITION: Modified in part, affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a bond forfeiture case, appellant bail bond filed a writ of error challenging the decision of the Criminal District Court No. 3, Dallas County (Texas), which entered judgment in favor of appellee state for the full amount of the bond and also awarded appellee prejudgment and postjudgment interest.


OVERVIEW: Appellant bail bond company sought review of the judgment of the trial court in a bond forfeiture case by filing a writ of error. The judgment against appellant included the full amount of the bond plus prejudgment and postjudgment interest. In point of error one, appellant contended that the trial court erred by entering judgment before the expiration of 18 months, as required by Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann art. 22.16(c)(2). Appellant also argued that the trial court improperly awarded prejudgment and postjudgment interest. The appellate court modified the judgment to delete the award of prejudgment and postjudgment interest and affirmed the judgment in all other respects. The appellate court noted that it had previously held art. 22.16(c)(2) to be unconstitutional and declined to reconsider that holding. Further, the appellate court noted that postjudgment interest was prohibited in bond forfeiture proceedings. Also, it was error to award prejudgment interest under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 22.16(a), (d) in the absence of a remittitur.


OUTCOME: The appellate court deleted the prejudgment and postjudgment interest from the judgment in favor of appellee state, but otherwise affirmed the judgment, in a bond forfeiture case. The trial court erred in awarding postjudgment interest against appellant bail bond company. Also, because there was no remittitur in the instant case, the trial court erred in awarding prejudgment interest.

Perez v. Lear Siegler, Inc.


No. 13-89-348-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


797 S.W.2d 222; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2215; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,704; 13 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 154



August 31, 1990, Delivered  
August 31, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled October 11, 1990. Application for Writ of Error Granted February 27, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 139th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: The trial court's judgment is affirmed with regard to Dallas Lite, affirmed in part with regard to appellants' breach of warranty claim against Lear and reversed and remanded in part with regard to appellants' negligence and strict liability claims against Lear.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant relatives of the deceased sought review of the judgment of the 139th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas, which granted a take-nothing judgment in favor of appellee companies in appellants' negligence suit. Appellants contended issues of fact remained regarding their claims which precluded summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, relatives of the deceased, sought review of the take-nothing summary judgment granted in favor of appellee companies in appellants' suit for negligence that resulted in an accident and death. Appellants asserted the trial court erred in granting appellees' motion for summary judgment because fact questions remained on many of appellants' claims. Appellants also asserted that Tex. Bus. & Com. Code Ann. § 2.275 violated the open courts provision. The court concluded that § 2.275 did not bar appellants' breach of warranty claim until 18 months after decedent's death. The court held that at the time appellants asserted their breach of warranty claim they were barred by law from doing so. The court held that the trial court improperly granted summary judgment to one of the appellees in the negligence and strict liability claim because a fact issue remained regarding the operability of the signboard that was involved in the accident when the board was in motion on a roadway. The court affirmed the judgment in part and reversed and remanded in part.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part summary judgment for appellee companies in appellant relatives' suit for damages due to deceased's death in an accident. An issue of fact remained regarding the operability of a signboard at the time of the accident, and appellants' breach of warranty claims were not barred until 18 months after the decedent's death.

 

1698 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Reyna v. State


Nos. 13-88-341-CR, 13-88-342-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


797 S.W.2d 189; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2223



August 31, 1990, Delivered  
August 31, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled September 27, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 206th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 206th District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas, that convicted him of aggravated sexual assault and indecency with a child and sentenced him to 55 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Following his conviction of aggravated sexual assault and indecency with a child, appellant sought review and asserted that the trial court erred in overruling his objection to the testimony of a four-year-old victim because she did not demonstrate that she was competent to testify under the standard set forth in Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 601. The court held that the competence of a child witness was generally a question for the trial court and its ruling would not be disturbed on appeal unless an abuse of discretion was shown. After examining the record, the court concluded that there was sufficient evidence to support the trial court's decision that the child witness was competent. Appellant also contended that the trial court erred in conducting the competency hearing in the presence of the jury on the ground that Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 104(a) required a competency hearing to be held outside the presence of the jury. The court disagreed and held that because appellant never objected during the competency hearing, the issue was not preserved for appellate review. The court found no merit to appellant's remaining assertions of error and affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment because it found that there was sufficient evidence in the record to support the trial court's ruling that a child witness was competent to testify and that the trial court did not err in conducting the competency hearing in the presence of the jury.

 

1699 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Strong v. State


No. 12-88-00053-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Twelfth District, Tyler


805 S.W.2d 478; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2273



August 31, 1990, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 21, 1990. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied January 30, 1991. Rehearing Denied January 30, 1991. Released for Publication April 9, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 188th Judicial District Court of Gregg County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the trial court is affirmed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for organized crime participation claiming that the 188th Judicial District Court of Gregg County (Texas) erred in convicting him under the activity organized crime statute, Tex. Penal Ann. Code § 71.01(a) (1989), contending the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it did not define the word collaborate. Defendant also claimed various errors amounting to insufficiency of evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for his participation in organized criminal activities. He claimed that the conviction should be set aside because the statute on which it was based was unconstitutionally vague, he was entitled to a separate trial, and because voir dire was improperly conducted. The court in affirming held that Tex. Penal Code § 71.01(a)(1989) was not unconstitutionally vague because persons of ordinary intelligence could understand its meaning. It also held that severance was not required when defendant failed to show that he would be prejudiced by a shared trial. In addition, the court said that voir dire was not improper because the trial court had discretion over how to conduct it, and prosecutor's comments were not unfairly prejudicial during cross-examination and closing arguments. The court also held that demonstrative evidence used but not admitted at trial was not subject to error, and that when defendant failed to object about evidence at trial, he waived any right to appeal that error. Finally, the court held that any comment made by judge was cured by instruction to jury by trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's racketeering conviction. It held that no reversible error occurred when the trial court failed to sever trial, refused to find the statute was unconstitutional, allowed demonstrative evidence to be used at trial, and when it overruled objections regarding voir dire, witness statements, and statements by prosecutor and judge.

 

1700 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Perryman v. State


No. 05-89-00882-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


798 S.W.2d 326; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2719



August 31, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 219th District Court, Collin County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 219-81085-88.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the 219th District Court, Collin County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated sexual assault pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (1989), after a trial in which expert testimony regarding the psychological profile of the victim's assailant was admitted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (1989). The court held that expert testimony regarding the psychological profile of the assailant was inadmissible under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 702, because it did not assist the jury in determining the only issues of what crime was committed or who committed the crime. The court could not say that the error was harmless under Tex. R. App. P. 81(b)(2), where the testimony portrayed the assailant, identified as defendant, as a repeat offender, and defendant was sentenced to 99-years imprisonment even though he had no prior convictions. The evidence was sufficient to show that the assault was aggravated where defendant forced his way into victim's apartment, repeatedly pushed her to the floor, and put a dishtowel on her face to impair her breathing. Tex. Penal Code § 22.021 (1989), was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant because the victim's state of mind was not the only determinative factor. Defendant was not entitled to a lesser included offense instruction of sexual assault because there was no evidence that raised only that offense. DNA evidence was reliable and had gained acceptance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction of aggravated sexual assault. The expert testimony presenting the psychological profile of the victim's assailant was inadmissible because it did not aid jury in understanding the evidence and its prejudicial and inflammatory effect outweighed its probative value. The court could not say that the admission of this testimony did not contribute to defendant's conviction or punishment.

 

1701 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. 1985 Chevy PU


No. 2-89-290-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


797 S.W.2d 682; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2731



August 31, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled November 13, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: From 213th District Court of Tarrant County, John Bradshaw, Trial Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the order of the 213th Judicial District Court, Tarrant County (Texas), which dismissed its forfeiture action against appellant property owner under § 5.07(a) of the Texas Controlled Substances Act because the cause had not been set for trial within 30 days of the answer date.


OVERVIEW: State brought a forfeiture action against appellee property owner under the Texas Controlled Substances Act. However, state failed to secure a setting for the forfeiture proceeding within 30 days of the answer date as was required by § 5.07(a) of the act. The trial court granted appellee's motion to dismiss. The court reversed the judgment, holding that the 30-day requirement of § 5.07(a), was directory rather than mandatory. The court noted that its decision did not affect the date of the hearing itself, but only the setting of the date for trial. To avoid further automatic dismissals of forfeiture actions, the court overruled State v. $ 4097 in U.S. Currency, 773 S.W.2d 674 (Tex. App. 1989), which had held that § 5.07(a), was mandatory. The court held that if § 5.07(a), were mandatory, it violated the separation of powers doctrine set forth in Tex. Const. art. II, § 1, because it was a legislative interference with the prosecutor's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, which had dismissed state's forfeiture action against appellee property owner, because the statutory provision requiring that the cause be set for trial within 30 days of the answer date was discretionary. The court overruled its prior decision, which had held that the provision was mandatory, because that holding rendered the statute unconstitutional.

Warner v. Sunkavalli


No. 11-89-230-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eleventh District, Eastland


795 S.W.2d 326; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2171



August 30, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

Appeal from Jones County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of the decision of the trial court of Jones County (Texas) that granted summary judgment based upon limitations in favor of hospital and two doctors in appellant's suit for medical malpractice.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed suit against appellees hospital and two doctors after he discovered that his gallbladder operation performed by appellees was incomplete since stones were left in his gallbladder. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of appellees based on the limitations period. The court affirmed as to appellee hospital, but reversed and remanded as to appellee doctors. The trial court had permitted appellant to amend his pleadings to allege fraudulent concealment and so that issue was raised for appellate review pursuant to Tex. R. Civ. P. 166a. Because a jury could believe appellee doctors fraudulently concealed the fact that there were still gallstones in appellant's body, the issue of fraudulent concealment was sufficiently raised and summary judgment was not appropriate.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of appellee hospital was affirmed, but summary judgment in favor of appellee doctors was reversed and remanded. The court reversed as to the doctors because the issue of fraudulent concealment was sufficiently raised so that a jury could find the limitations period had not expired.

Paley v. State


No. 01-88-00791-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2173



August 30, 1990, Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Withdrawn June 6, 1991; Substituted Opinion Reported at 1991 Tex. App. LEXIS 1426. Rehearing Overruled June 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trail Court Cause No. 503279.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the 176th District Court, Harris County, Texas, of aggravated kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Appellant stopped the vehicle in which the victim was a passenger, pointed a gun at the car, forced the victim out of the car and into his truck and drove away. A short time later, appellant ran his truck off the road. Both appellant and the victim had gunshot wounds. The victim died. The driver of the other car testified for the state. The court held that the trial court did not err in prohibiting cross-examination as to prior crimes of the witness because adjudication of the offense had been deferred. The court held that the trial court did err in not permitting evidence of prior crimes of the witness to indicate a motive for testifying, but that the error was not harmful because there was other direct testimony to prove the kidnapping. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to find that appellant had used deadly force sufficient to sustain a conviction for aggravated kidnapping. The court held that the state's closing argument was not improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and held that there was sufficient evidence to substantiate the charge of aggravated kidnapping.

 

1704 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Fredericks v. State


No. B14-90-00035-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2209



August 30, 1990, Rendered  
August 30, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 540,502.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 228th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellant of the offense of aggravated robbery pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.02.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.02. He filed an appeal and argued that the evidence was insufficient because the state failed to prove the property was taken without the effective consent of the owner. The court found that consent did not become a disputed fact issue where it was alleged, proven, and found that the owner was threatened or placed in fear of imminent bodily injury, intentionally or knowingly, by an accused in the course of the taking. The complainant testified appellant threatened her with a knife and physically removed the money from a cash drawer. When reviewing the sufficiency of the evidence to support the conviction, the evidence must be viewed in the light most favorable to the verdict. The testimony was sufficient to support the inference that the complainant was in fear of bodily harm at the time of the taking. A rational trier of fact could reasonably find lack of consent on the part of the complainant by proof beyond a reasonable doubt. The court overruled appellant's point of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court which convicted appellant of the offense of aggravated robbery because when reviewing the sufficiency of the evidence to support the conviction, the evidence must be viewed in the light most favorable to the verdict.

 

1705 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Jack v. Jack


No. 05-89-01454-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


796 S.W.2d 543; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2575



August 28, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 256th District Court, Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 89-4886-Z.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant son challenged a judgment from the 256th District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which dismissed appellant's suit against appellee father to rebut the presumption that appellee was the father of a child born during appellee's marriage to the child's mother.


OVERVIEW: Appellant son challenged the trial court's order dismissing his suit to rebut the presumption that appellee father was the father of a child born during appellee's marriage to the child's mother, as determined in their divorce degree. The court affirmed because Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 12.06 (1990) allowed only a mother or presumed father to rebut the presumption; thus, appellant lacked any statutory means to challenge it. The court found that appellant failed to show a constitutional right to make such a challenge under due process or the Equal Protection Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex. Const. art. 1, § 3. The court found that appellant had no constitutionally protected interest that enabled him to challenge the presumption. The court held that appellant had no fundamental interest in a relationship with the child, and the purpose of protecting children was rationally related to limiting the right to challenge paternity to the mother or presumed father. The court found that, as § 12.06 precluded a man other than the mother's husband from rebutting the presumption, the classification was marriage-based and was rationally related to protecting the child.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that dismissed appellant son's suit against appellee father to rebut the presumption that appellee was the father of a child born during appellee's marriage to the child's mother was affirmed, as appellant lacked statutory or constitutional means to make such a challenge where no fundamental interest or suspect classification existed, and statutory restriction was rationally related to protecting the child.

 

1706 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. Muller


No. 01-89-00306-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


798 S.W.2d 315; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2158



August 23, 1990, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted April 24, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 8832565, Hon. J.R. Musselwhite, Judge.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of May 10, 1990, Reported at 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1089.



DISPOSITION: We reverse, order the information reinstated, and remand for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state of Texas, sought review from a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6, Harris County (Texas), which granted an order striking a paragraph in an information that charged appellee criminal with operating a motor vehicle in a public place while intoxicated and alleged a 0.10 alcohol concentration.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the state of Texas, challenged an order striking a paragraph in an information as unconstitutional that charged appellee criminal with operating a motor vehicle in a public place while intoxicated and alleged a 0.10 alcohol concentration. First, the court addressed the notice of appeal, which the district attorney did not personally sign and found it was proper as amended. The state argued that the trial court erred in declaring the statute and regulations unconstitutional. The court held that the statute and regulations were not unconstitutional under any ground. The state asserted that the trial court erred in granting the motion to suppress the evidence of the intoxilyzer test because the statute and regulations were constitutional. Appellee stipulated that the test was done according to the regulations and rules and that the trial court had this stipulation when it ruled. Therefore, the trial court erred in suppressing the evidence. The state argued that the trial court should have awarded them attorney fees. The court held that attorney fees are only allowed in declaratory judgment cases not criminal cases. The court reversed the order and remanded for trial.


OUTCOME: The court remanded and reversed the order striking a paragraph in an information that charged appellee criminal with operating a motor vehicle in a public place while intoxicated in favor of appellant, the state of Texas. The court held that the statute and regulations were constitutional, that the notice of appeal was proper as amended, that the trial court erred in suppressing the intoxilyzer test, and that attorney fees were not allowed.

 

1707 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Space Master Int'l, Inc. v. Porta-Kamp Mfg. Co.


No. 01-90-00020-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


794 S.W.2d 944; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2084



August 16, 1990, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 125th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 89-009452.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the order nunc pro tunc of the 125th District court, Harris County (Texas), which had dismissed its suit for declaratory judgment against appellee manufacturer. Appellant contended that the trial court erred because the mere pendency of two other federal and state actions was not a sufficient basis for dismissal.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, a Texas corporation, had filed a breach of contract action against appellant corporation. The parties had entered into two construction contracts for projects in New Jersey and Massachusetts in which appellee had respectively its claims. Appellant then filed the declaratory judgment action in Texas alleging that appellee had violated the Texas usury statute. Appellee filed a motion to dismiss and a plea in abatement urging the Texas court to either decline to exercise its jurisdiction or abate the cause of action, in order to avoid interference with litigation involving the same parties and issues in Massachusetts. Appellant challenged the authority of the trial court to dismiss a suit for declaratory judgment in this case. The court affirmed because it was within the discretion of the trial court to refuse to enter a declaratory judgment if it would not terminate the uncertainty or controversy which gave rise to the proceeding and as a matter of comity.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed because appellant had conceded that the suit for declaratory judgment involved the same parties and issues as the proceedings pending in the other courts. Appellant could not be allowed to use declaratory relief as a forum-shopping device.

Houston Independent School Dist. v. Houston Chronicle Pub. Co.


No. 01-90-00116-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


798 S.W.2d 580; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2042



August 9, 1990, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied February 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 295th District Court, Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89-15172, Hon. Dan Downey, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants school district and superintendent sought review of a judgment from the 295th District Court, Harris County, Texas, granting appellee newspaper's petition for a writ of mandamus that required appellants to release certain portions of the college transcripts of their administrative personnel to appellee pursuant to the Texas Open Records Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-17a (1990).


OVERVIEW: Appellants, school district and superintendent, denied appellee newspaper's request for the college transcripts of its administrative personnel pursuant to the Texas Open Records Act (Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6252-17a (1990). Appellee sought a writ of mandamus to compel release. The Act was subsequently amended to prohibit disclosure of such transcripts, after which, the trial court granted the writ. Appellants challenged the judgment claiming that the trial court erred in applying the pre-amendment law. The court reversed the trial court judgment, holding that appellee did not obtain a vested right to information contained in the transcripts until final judgment, which was after the Act was amended, and that the trial court erred in finding that the application of the amended Act would be an unconstitutional retroactive application of law. The trial court further erred as a matter of law in denying appellant's motion to vacate mandamus, because it did not correctly apply the applicable law. The case was remanded to the trial court to order appellant to release only that information as required by the amended Act and for further proceedings as to costs and fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment that granted appellee newspaper's petition for a writ of mandamus, holding that appellee did not obtain a vested right to information in the transcripts until after the Texas Open Records Act (Act) was amended. The court held that the trial court erred in applying the pre-amendment Act and in finding that application of the amended Act would be an unconstitutional retroactive application of law.

 

1709 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Boyd v. Fuel Distributors, Inc.


No. 3-89-184-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


795 S.W.2d 266; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1957



August 8, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1]

Released for Publication October 17, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Overruled October 17, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Bell County, 146th Judicial District; No. 121,792-B, Honorable Rick Morris, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, personal representatives and injured minor, sought review of the summary judgment entered by the District Court of Bell County, 146th Judicial District (Texas), in favor of appellee store. Appellants sought recovery on, inter alia, an alleged violation by appellee of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. §§ 2.01-2.03 (1990).


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of appellee store in an action brought by appellants, personal representatives and injured minor, seeking damages for appellee's alleged violation of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. §§ 2.01-2.03 (1990), and Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 106.03(a) (1990). Appellants sought review. Section 2.02 required proof that the recipient's intoxication was a proximate cause of damages, otherwise the provider could not be held liable. The court affirmed, on grounds, inter alia, that appellants had not proven that appellant minor's intoxication was a cause-in-fact of their damages. The court found that the decedent minor driver's intoxication was the cause-in-fact for the accident and the resulting injuries. Appellant minor's intoxication played no part in bringing about the wreck. The court further found that Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 2.03 (1990) set forth the exclusive cause of action for providing alcohol to a minor and summary judgment on appellants' claim of violation of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 106.03(a) (1990) was not error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment entered by the lower court in favor of appellee store in an action brought seeking damages for injuries resulting from the sale of alcoholic beverages to a minor. The court held that appellant minor's intoxication could not have been a cause-in-fact of the automobile accident and resulting damages, thus appellee was not liable under statute making sellers responsible for the actions of their customers.

 

1710 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Bullock v. House of Lloyd, Inc.


No. 3-89-129-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


797 S.W.2d 133; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1968



August 8, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 12, 1990. Rehearing Overruled September 12, 1990. Application for Writ of Error Granted February 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Travis County, 353rd Judicial District, No. 424,393, Honorable F. Scott McCown, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Comptroller of Public Accounts, challenged the judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 353rd Judicial District (Texas), that determined that appellee corporation was not subject to a franchise tax under the Texas Franchise Tax Act, Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 171.001 et seq., and was entitled to a refund.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the Comptroller of Public Accounts, changed the rule defining when a corporation was "doing business in Texas" and decided that appellee corporation had conducted business in Texas within the meaning of the Texas Franchise Tax Act, Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 171.001 et seq., and was subject to the corporate franchise tax. The district court disagreed, ruling that appellee was entitled to a refund. The issue on appeal was whether appellant could impose a franchise tax upon appellee pursuant to Tex. Admin. Code Ann. § 3.406 (1983). Appellee contended that the language "doing business in Texas" was ambiguous. Considering that prior to 1983 appellant did not seek to impose the tax on corporations such as appellee, and that the franchise tax statute language had remained virtually unchanged since 1941, the court agreed. Additionally, because appellant's construction of the franchise tax law and that of appellant's predecessors was of long-standing duration, it should not have been changed absent clear statutory authorization. The court held that appellant lacked authority to impose the franchise tax upon appellee pursuant to the 1983 rule change. The judgment below was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the district court finding that appellee was not subject to a franchise tax and was entitled to a refund was affirmed because the court found that appellant had no authority to impose such a tax pursuant to a rule change.

 

1711 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


May v. Appraisal Review Bd.


Nos. 2-89-262-CV, 2-89-263-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


794 S.W.2d 906; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2327



August 8, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled September 19, 1990 for Case No. 2-89-262-CV. Rehearing Overruled September 17, 1990 for Case No. 2-89-263-CV. Application for Writ of Error Denied November 21, 1990. Motion for Rehearing of Application for Writ of Error Overruled January 9, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 352nd District Court of Tarrant County; Hon. Bruce Auld, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a judgment from the 352nd District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which refused to award them attorney's fees upon their successful appeal of appellee taxing authorities' denial of an open-space land valuation of their real property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers challenged the trial court's refusal to award them attorney's fees upon their successful appeal of appellee taxing authorities' denial of an open-space land valuation of their real property. The court noted that attorney's fees could not be recovered unless provided for by statute or by contract between parties, and any statutory provisions allowing recovery of attorney's fees had to be subjected to strict construction. The only statutory authority permitting recovery of attorney's fees by taxpayers was Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.29 (1990). It was clear to the court that appellants were complaining of excessive appraisal value placed upon their properties as referred to in Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.25 (1982). Therefore, their successful protest entitled them to an award of attorney's fees under § 42.29. The court also noted that to interpret the Tex. Tax Code Ann. §§ 42.24 and 42.25 not to include appeals of this kind would leave the court without statutory instruction of what to do with this type of appeal. Such a result would undermine the system of judicial review of board orders and appeals of appraisal district decisions. The judgment below was reversed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court refusing to award appellant taxpayers attorney's fees was reversed because their successful protest of the denial of open-space land valuation of their real property entitled them to an award of attorney's fees under the Tax Code.

Pittman v. State

Gonzales v. State


No. A14-90-00091-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1913



August 2, 1990, Rendered  
August 2, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 183rd District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 460,121-A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 183rd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which entered a final judgment against him and his surety on a bail bond. That trial court also previously overruled appellant's motion to pass setting (or motion for continuance), and appellant's prior motion for a new trial was overruled by operation of law.


OVERVIEW: After appellant's bail bond was issued, a judgment nisi was entered when he failed to appear. Final judgment was entered against appellant and his surety for their failure to show sufficient cause for appellant's failure to appear. Appellant presented an unsworn motion to pass setting, which was overruled, and his subsequent motion for a new trial was overruled by operation of law. Appellant then challenged the entry of the final judgment, contending that it was premature, as Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 22.16(c)(2) required that final judgment be entered no less than 18 months after bond forfeiture in a felony case; appellant argued that art. 22.16 retroactively applied to bonds issued prior to that article's enactment. The court found that there was nothing in the language of art. 22.16 indicating that the legislature intended retroactive application. Moreover, retroactive application of the statute would have impaired the vested contractual rights of the state, under the bond agreement, and thus would have violated Tex. Const. art. 1, § 16, which forbade retroactive application of any law impairing the obligation of contracts. The order below was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Final judgment against appellant and his surety on bail bond was affirmed. As to a statute requiring a final judgment to be entered no less than 18 months after bond forfeiture, the court found that nothing in the statute's language indicated retroactive application, and such retroactive application would have unconstitutionally impaired the vested contractual rights of the state, under its bond agreement with appellant.

 

1714 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Russell v. Ingersoll-Rand Co.


No. 01-89-00397-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


795 S.W.2d 243; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1923; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P12,626



August 2, 1990, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Granted January 23, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 61st District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 82-62965.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs challenged a judgment from the District Court of Harris County (Texas) that dismissed their wrongful death and survival actions as barred by the statutes of limitations. Plaintiffs filed the actions and added defendants after the death of decedent. Plaintiffs asserted that decedent's death revived the causes of action against defendants, even though the statutes of limitations had run against decedent.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed a judgment that dismissed plaintiffs' survival and wrongful death suits, filed three months after decedent's death, because they were barred by statutes of limitations. Prior to his death, decedent developed silicosis as a result of his employment as a sandblaster and filed suit against several corporations that manufactured or distributed the products his employer used. After his death, plaintiff wife, as executrix of the estate, added additional plaintiffs, survival and wrongful death causes of action, and named additional defendants. The court held that a survival action was purely derivative and that when decedent's statute of limitations had run against defendants at the time of his death, the limitations period also barred the survival action. The court harmonized Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 16.003(b) and 71.003(a) by finding that one applied to the right to file a wrongful death action and one governed the time period for that suit The court held that a wrongful death action related back to an original suit filed by a decedent, so that here, where there was no original suit, there was no right to file the wrongful death action.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the actions as barred by the statute of limitations. The court held that survival action was purely derivative and that when the statute of limitations had run against decedent, the survival action was also barred. The court reconciled two statutes referencing wrongful death and found that wrongful death action must relate back to original suit, thus plaintiffs never had a right to file the suit.

In the Interest of George

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 273RD Judicial District Court of Shelby County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: The cause is reversed. The judgment of the trial court is vacated and the cause is dismissed. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner widow, by writ of error, sought review of the judgment of the 273rd Judicial District Court, Shelby County, Texas that declared child to be the biological child of petitioner's deceased husband in paternity action brought by child's mother.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner widow filed a writ of error for review of trial court's order declaring a child to be the biological child of petitioner's deceased husband. The court reversed, as a paternity suit could not be brought under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. ch. 13 after the death of the putative father. The court found that the writ was brought within six months of the date of judgment by a party to the suit who did not participate in the trial, and it was apparent on the face of the record that the trial court erred in entering an order designating decedent as the child's father when it was clear that he was dead before the suit was filed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that declared child to be the biological child of petitioner widow's deceased husband in paternity action brought child's mother was vacated and the cause was dismissed, as the paternity suit could not be brought after the death of the putative father.

Ackenback v. State


Nos. 01-89-00430-CR, 01-89-00431-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


794 S.W.2d 567; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1814



July 26, 1990, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused December 12, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 228th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause Nos. 502904, 502905; Hon. C.V. Milburn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We affirm the judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his 228th District Court for Harris County, (Texas) conviction for aggravated robbery and attempted capital murder of a peace officer.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery and attempted capital murder of a peace officer. Contrary to appellant's assertions, the trial court did not commit error in connection with the admission into evidence of items seized during two warrantless searches. Officers pursued appellant following a robbery and came across a vehicle they believed belonged to appellant. The officers searched the vehicle and found papers with appellant's address. They went to the address and found a gun in the common area of the apartment complex. The vehicle search came within the vehicle exception of the warrant requirement because it was readily capable for use on the highways and was found in a place not regularly used for residential purposes. Additionally, the gun was found just outside appellant's patio gate in a common area of the apartments and, therefore, the gun was not seized as a result of a warrantless search of appellant's residence.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery and attempted capital murder was affirmed because the trial court did not err in admitting into evidence items seized during two warrantless searches.

Bledsoe v. State


No. 01-89-00776-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1841



July 26, 1990, Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused November 21, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 263rd District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 500287.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of less than 28 grams of cocaine and sentence to 40 years punishment enhanced by two prior convictions from the 263rd District Court, Harris County, Texas, following a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty in a jury trial of possession of less than 28 grams of cocaine and sentenced to 40 years punishment enhanced by two prior convictions. The appellate court affirmed. The court rejected defendant's contention that the state's request at punishment for a 45 year enhancement violated the ban against cruel and unusual punishment. First, defendant did not object to the request and thus the issue was waived. Also, the state's request was a proper plea for law enforcement which is allowed in closing argument, and finally, state had the discretion of choosing what charges to bring absent a finding of vindictiveness. The trial court's discussion of parole law with a juror was not an error because the jury had no power to affect parole eligibility, and defendant did not object to the discussion anyway thus waiving the issue. Defendant was not placed in double jeopardy for being twice convicted of indecency with a child. The habitual offender statute, Tex. Code Penal Ann. § 12.42(d)(1990), did not constitute a double jeopardy punishment. It merely classified a more severe punishment for defendant's persistence in crime.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of less than 28 grams of cocaine and sentence of 45 years punishment based upon a repeat offender enhancement. The state's request for the enhancement was a proper form of closing argument. The trial court's discussion of parole law with a juror was not an error because the jury had no authority to affect parole, and the repeat offender statute was not a form of double jeopardy.
