Garza-Vale v. Kwiecien


Appeal No. 04-89-00296-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


796 S.W.2d 500; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2567



July 25, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 10, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 73rd District Court of Bexar County; Trial Court No. 86-CI-05504; Honorable Rose Spector, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, doctor and his wife, who were lessors, sought review of a judgment of the 73rd District Court of Bexar County (Texas), entered on a jury verdict in a wrongful death and survival action brought by appellees, mother and as personal representative and heir of her adult son, with respect to his death by smoke inhalation during a fire at appellants' apartment duplex. Common law negligence was claimed.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, mother and as personal representative and heir of her adult son, brought a suit alleging common law negligence in a wrongful death and survival action, with respect to her son's death by smoke inhalation during a fire at the apartment duplex of appellants, doctor and his wife, who were owners and lessors. A judgment was entered on a jury verdict for common law negligence damages favoring appellees where negligence in failing to install a smoke detector and in failing to repair a floor furnace was claimed. The appellate court reversed the judgment of the trial court, holding that the Texas Smoke Detectors Statute provided the exclusive remedy for the absence of a smoke detector, hence the jury's negligence finding, which did not embrace the statutory scheme, was legally insufficient to support the judgment. The court held further that absent any notice by a tenant to appellants of the specified unsafe condition at the rental premises in need of repair, appellants, as landlords, were under no duty to make such repairs, and that the Texas Smoke Detectors Statute was constitutional, contending substantive due process, including equal protection, violations.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and rendered appellees take nothing in a wrongful death and survival action where appellees, mother and as personal representative and heir of her adult son, filed suit after the adult son died from smoke inhalation from a fire in an apartment owned and leased by appellants, doctor and his wife. The constitutional state smoke detectors statute preempted common law negligence, and no landlord liability existed.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston

The court also held that the demonstrative evidence supported the trial court's denial of appellant's request for a jury view of the crime scene.

He alleged error in the denial of his pretrial motions to quash the informations. The statute on which the prosecution was based was unconstitutionally overbroad, indefinite, uncertain and vague and that there was no timely and proper definition of obscenity.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who pled nolo contendere to three charges of obscenity pursuant to Tex. Defendant had filed pre-trial motions to quash, but the trial court did not rule on any of them and to preserve a matter for review required that the objection or motion be brought to the trial court's attention and that the trial court rule on it adversely.

Goheen v. Koester


No. 05-89-01474-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


794 S.W.2d 830; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2361



July 10, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied November 28, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 304th Judicial District Court; Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 89-361-W.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the judgment from 304th Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, which established appellant father's parental rights and required that appellant pay appellee's attorney fees in appellant's suit for voluntary legitimation of a child. Appellee sought review of the portion of the judgment that failed to grant child support retroactive to the date of the child's birth.


OVERVIEW: Appellant father sued appellee mother for legitimation of child, and for appointment as conservator with visitation rights. Appellee sought termination of appellant's parental rights and adoption by husband. The trial court established appellant's parental rights, granted visitation, made appellee sole conservator, awarded appellee child support retroactive to original petition and attorney fees. On appeal, the court could not say that the trial court abused its discretion in awarding appellee attorney fees when the trial court found that the award was in the best interests of child. The court reversed attorneys' fees in part and remanded because trial court abused discretion in awarding attorneys' fees to appellee that were properly allocable to her attorneys' representation of her husband. The court reversed judgment which did not child support retroactive to birth because, upon a finding of paternity, temporary orders for child support could include prenatal and postnatal health care expenses of mother and child and, upon final judgment, trial court could award child support retroactive to birth. The court affirmed in all other respects.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the trial court judgment that failed to grant appellee child support retroactive to the date of birth because, upon finding paternity, temporary child support orders could include prenatal and postnatal health care expenses of mother and child and, upon final judgment, trial court could award child support retroactive to birth. The court affirmed in all other respects.

Trahan v. State


Nos. 01-89-0553-CR, 01-89-0554-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1635



July 5, 1990, Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause Nos. 8902961 & 8902962.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 8, Harris County (Texas), which found him guilty of two separate misdemeanor offenses of promotion of obscene material, Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 43.21 (1989), claiming that the statute was unconstitutional for indefiniteness, uncertainty and vagueness, and that there was not a timely and proper judicial determination of obscenity prior to his arrest.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled nolo contendere to two separate misdemeanor offenses of promotion of obscene material, Tex. Penal Code Ann. art. 43.21 (1989), and challenged his conviction, claiming that the statute was unconstitutional and that there was no finding of guilt. The court held that based upon prior precedent, the state's obscenity statute was not unconstitutional for indefiniteness, uncertainty, and vagueness. The court also determined that a prior judicial determination of obscenity was not an element of the offense. The court further stated that no evidence was necessary to support a finding of guilt because appellant had entered a nolo contendere plea in his two misdemeanor convictions. Finally, the court concluded that there was no statement of facts in the record before it, and thus the court did not have a record of what evidence the state may have presented. The court overruled appellant's points of errors and affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, and held that appellant was properly convicted on two counts of obscenity; the state statute was not unconstitutional; and that evidence was necessary to support a finding of guilt, because appellant pled nolo contendere in the misdemeanor charges.

 

1727 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Texas Nat'l Bank v. Lewis


No. 13-90-096-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


793 S.W.2d 83; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1600



June 29, 1990, Delivered  
June 29, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Petition for Writ of Mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Relator's petition for writ of mandamus is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator bank sought a writ of mandamus to compel respondent lower court (Texas) to rescind an order denying its motion for protection of customer bank records pursuant to Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 342-705, § 1 (1990).


OVERVIEW: Relator bank sought a writ to compel respondent court to rescind an order denying its motion for protection of customer bank records. The court denied the writ and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the discovery of the bank records, and therefore, mandamus was not an appropriate remedy. The statute relating to the disclosure of information concerning borrowers, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 342-705, § 1 (1990), was unclear and there was no clear case law to guide the trial court in the manner in which it should interpret the statute. Thus, there was no clear duty of the trial court to compel protection under the statute. The trial court fashioned an order allowing the discovery, but provided some protection of confidentiality for the bank's customers. The court held that the balancing of interests under an ambiguous statute was a proper exercise of the trial court's discretion, and mandamus was not proper.


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of mandamus because there was no abuse of discretion by respondent court in denying relator's motion for protection of customer bank records. The statute relating to the disclosure of information concerning borrowers was unclear and there was no case law to guide the trial court. As such, the trial court's order allowing discovery, but providing some protection to bank customers, was a proper exercise of discretion.

 

1728 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


McKinney v. State


No. 01-89-00535-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1547



June 28, 1990, Delivered


NOTICE:  [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 506805.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged decision of the 185th District Court, Harris County, (Texas) convicting him of injury to a child. Appellant contended, inter alia, that the prosecution failed to prove the culpable mental state of intentionally or knowingly causing serious bodily injury. Appellant also complained that certain testimony of a physician who treated complainant should not have been admitted and that there was fundamental error in the jury charge.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of a decision convicting appellant of injury to a child, the court rejected appellant's contention that the prosecution failed to prove the culpable mental state of intentionally or knowingly causing serious bodily injury. The court held that because the injury to child statute focused on the result of defendant's conduct, the allegation in the indictment that defendant did "intentionally and knowingly engage in conduct that caused serious bodily injury" to a child was sufficient to allege that it was defendant's conscious objective or desire to cause serious bodily injury. The court also rejected arguments that testimony of a physician, who treated the complainant, should not have been admitted. The court held that failure to object to the doctor's qualifications at trial precluded raising the issue on appeal. The court held that, under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 702 and 704, it was permissible for the doctor to give an opinion on the ultimate issue of whether complainant's injuries were sustained accidentally, or were inflicted intentionally. As to assertions of error in the jury charge, the court held that there was no fundamental error.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court convicting appellant of injury to a child was sustained. The appellate court found that the language of the indictment was sufficient to allege the culpable mental state of intentionally or knowingly causing serious bodily injury and that testimony of a physician who treated the complainant was admissible. Any error in the jury charge was not so harmful that appellant was denied a fair and impartial trial.

Reed v. State


Nos. C14-89-00828-CR, A14-89-00829-CR, B14-89-00830-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


794 S.W.2d 806; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1558



June 28, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled September 6, 1990. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 10, 1991. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 16, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court At Law No. 5; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause Nos. 8916760; 8916761; 8916763.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 5, Harris County (Texas), which convicted appellants of obstructing a passageway leading to an abortion clinic in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.03.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected the argument of appellants, convicted of obstructing an abortion clinic passageway, that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.03 was unconstitutionally overbroad and void for vagueness. The statute regulated conduct, not speech, and was not overbroad; the court noted also that appellants cited no authority as to vagueness and, thus, nothing was presented for review. A police videotape of appellants' offenses was properly admitted because the predicate for its admission was established; a "predicate" objection was general and did not preserve error on appeal. When appellants offered a defense upon being denied a directed verdict after the state rested, any error in the denial of their motion was waived. Further, the defenses of necessity and defense of a third person were properly denied, because a fetus was not a legal "person" for purposes of the third person defense and because the harm sought to be prevented was not a legal harm so as to justify necessity. Absent an adverse ruling as to appellants' objection to the prosecutor's jury argument, nothing was preserved for review. Jail sentences falling within the statutory range of punishment were not cruel or unusual.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting appellants of obstructing an abortion clinic passageway was affirmed because the underlying statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad or void for vagueness. The defenses of necessity and defense of a third person were properly denied, absent a legal "person" or legal harm, and error was not preserved for review concerning the admission into evidence of a police videotape of the offenses.

State v. One (1) 1986 Nissan Auto.


No. 08-89-00324-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


792 S.W.2d 577; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1533



June 27, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 142nd District Court of Midland County, Texas; TC# A-37,598; Pat M. Baskin, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from an order of the 142nd District Court of Midland County (Texas) dismissing a forfeiture proceeding commenced under the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15 (1976).


OVERVIEW: The state appealed from an order of dismissal in a forfeiture proceeding commenced under the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4476-15, § 5.07(a) (1976). The reviewing court affirmed. The state contended that it was error for the court to treat the 30 day requirement of § 5.07(a) as mandatory rather than directory. The court disagreed. The court determined that the requirement was not an unconstitutional legislative encroachment on prosecutorial discretion under the separation of powers doctrine. The state relied on the fact that several appellate courts had interpreted § 5.07(a) to be merely directory, not mandatory. However, the court failed to see how the state would have been harmed or prejudiced by the requirement that a setting be obtained within the 30 day period. The court found no merit to the state's argument that appellee waived the 30 day setting requirement and was estopped from asserting it. Because the state had not requested or obtained a setting for the forfeiture hearing within the 30 day period, the trial court was correct in dismissing the suit and its judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing a forfeiture proceeding was affirmed. The state did not request or obtain a setting for the forfeiture hearing within the 30 day period required by the statute, therefore, the trial court was correct in dismissing the suit and its judgment was affirmed.

MJR'S Fare v. Dallas


No. 05-89-00765-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


792 S.W.2d 569; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1866



June 21, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 12, 1990. Motion for Rehearing of Application for Writ of Error Overruled November 28, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 68th Judicial District Court; Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 86-15601-C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of the declaratory judgment from the 68th Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, that found appellee city's zoning ordinance that regulated sexually oriented businesses did not violate Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 3a, 19, and held that appellant's claims against appellee were barred by res judicata and collateral estoppel.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation challenged in federal court, pursuant to the Federal Declaratory Judgment Act, 28 U.S.C.S. §§ 2201, 2202, appellee city's zoning ordinance that regulated sexually oriented businesses. The federal court ruled that the zoning ordinance was constitutional. Appellant then sought relief in state trial court. The trial court held that appellant's federal cause of action and state cause of action were the same and barred by collateral estoppel and res judicata. The trial court found that the ordinance did not violate Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 3a, 19. Appellant sought review. The court agreed that the issues and claims adjudicated by the federal court in appellant's action were the same as those brought to the trial court. The court held that enactment of the zoning ordinance fell within appellee's police power and did not constitute a taking under art. I, § 19. Appellant failed to show that the ordinance discriminated against females solely on the basis of gender in violation of art. I, § 3a. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because res judicata and collateral estoppel barred appellant's claims, and there was no violation of the Texas Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee city because appellant corporation's claims of the unconstitutionality of appellee's zoning ordinance, that regulated sexually oriented businesses, had been previously litigated in federal court and res judicata and collateral estoppel barred appellant's claims in state court, and the zoning ordinance was a proper exercise of appellee's police power and did not violate the Texas Constitution.

Burleson v. State


No. 3-86-285-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


791 S.W.2d 334; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1470



June 20, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:  [**1] Released for Publication July 24, 1990.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted October 31, 1990. Appellant's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied December 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the District Court of Caldwell County, 22nd Judicial District No. 9622, Honorable Fred A. Moore, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the constitutionality, under U.S. Const. amends. VI, XIV and Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 10, 19, of the verdict from the District Court of Caldwell County, 22nd Judicial District (Texas), that convicted him of aggravated sexual assault in violation of Tex. Pen. Code Ann. § 22.021(a)(5) (1985), and admitted the minor victim's videotaped and in-court testimony pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, §§ 2, 3 (1985).


OVERVIEW: At appellant's trial for aggravated sexual assault in violation of Tex. Pen. Code Ann. § 22.021 (a)(5) (1985), the trial court allowed the state to introduce, over appellant's objections, the minor victim's videotaped testimony under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 2 (1985), and ordered that the victim's in-court testimony be taken in a room other than the courtroom and transmitted in compliance with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.071, § 3 (1985). After the jury convicted appellant, he sought review and argued that art. 38.071, §§ 2, 3 violated his right of confrontation and due process under U.S. Const. amends. OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault because appellant's admission to the offense and other testimony constituted such overwhelming evidence that admission of the minor victim's videotaped testimony and the trial court order that the minor victim testify outside of appellant's presence did not contribute to appellant's conviction and any constitutional infringement was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt.

State v. Garcia


No. 08-89-00397-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


794 S.W.2d 472; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1494



June 20, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 327th District Court of El Paso County, Texas; TC No. 55430-327.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the decision of the 327th District Court of El Paso County, Texas, that granted appellee's motion to suppress the fruits of a search resulting from an alleged pretext arrest of appellee.


OVERVIEW: The state sought review of the decision to suppress the fruits of its search of appellee's vehicle after stopping him for a traffic violation. The appellate court reversed, concluding that given the actual occurrence of the stop sign violation, the officers' actions leading to the arrest, search, and seizure were proper, regardless of their preexisting suspicions and desire for an opportunity to stop the appellee's vehicle. Appellee failed to exit the vehicle when an officer approached him, attempted to run the officer over, and took off in his vehicle. Appellee was apprehended, arrested for aggravated assault of a police officer, and his vehicle was searched. Cocaine was found. The officers had observed the vehicle in front of a house known to be a drug house and had wanted to investigate, but did not do so because they did not have probable cause. The court reviewed the origins of the pretext arrest doctrine and concluded that it has been misinterpreted and misapplied in a multitude of other cases. It found that the doctrine, as applied by current courts, was without any authoritative support.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision to suppress evidence found in a search of appellee's vehicle, finding that there was no pretext arrest because appellee had violated a traffic ordinance by failing to stop at a stop sign. As a result of that violation, it was proper for the arresting officers to search his vehicle and seize the contraband that was discovered.

Stotter v. Wingo

The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in imposing monetary sanctions and striking defendant's answers where defendant, in bad faith, failed to comply with discovery orders to produce relevant documents setting forth its policies.

State v. Wagner


No. 05-89-00675-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


791 S.W.2d 573; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1789



May 29, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 2; Dallas County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. MB89-32717-B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state, filed an appeal from a judgment of the County Criminal Court No. 2, Dallas County (Texas), which acquitted appellee on a charge of driving while intoxicated, after the trial court granted appellee's motion to suppress the evidence obtained in a roadblock.


OVERVIEW: Police set up a roadblock near a high concentration of bars and nightclubs. Every vehicle was stopped and all drivers were asked about their drinking or drug use. Appellee was arrested at the roadblock and charged with driving while intoxicated (DWI). The trial court granted appellee's motion to suppress the evidence obtained in the roadblock. Appellant, the state, filed an appeal. Appellant alleged that the sole purpose of the roadblock was a sobriety check, and that as long as it did not engage in any form of subterfuge in conducting the roadblock, no U.S. Const. amend. IV violation took place. The court affirmed. The court concluded that the roadblock was not based on reasonable suspicion but was designed to be preemptive in nature and premised on nothing more than inarticulable facts; hunches that criminal conduct would occur. As such, the court said, the roadblock was an infringement of individual freedom of privacy and travel. The court said that a DWI roadblock differed from the usual administrative or regulatory inspection because there was no regulatory agency to enforce the drunk driving prohibition other than the police and the criminal courts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that acquitted appellee on a charge of driving while intoxicated, after the trial court granted appellee's motion to suppress the evidence obtained in a roadblock, because the roadblock was not based on reasonable suspicion but was designed to be preemptive in nature and premised on nothing more than inarticulable facts and hunches that criminal conduct would occur.

Appeal from District, Court; 314th County; Robert Baum, Judge.

Original Proceeding on Motion for Leave to File Petition for Writ of Mandamus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relators, parent and minor child, requested a writ of mandamus against an order of respondent district court judge of the District Court, 314th County (Texas), that appointed the Harris County Child Protective Services to be relator minor child's temporary managing conservator under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 17.04(c), 11.11(a)(1) (1986), which included the authority to consent to a blood transfusion for the minor despite his religious conviction.


OVERVIEW: The Harris County Child Protective Service (CPS) filed a complaint under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 11.03(a)(5)-(6) (Supp. 1990) that sought appointment as temporary managing conservator of relator parent's minor child. The court overruled the motion of relators, parent and minor child, that requested leave to file a petition for writ of mandamus to order respondent district court judge not to appoint CPS to give consent to a blood transfusion for the minor. The court held that respondent's order was authorized by Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 17.04(c ), 11.11(a)(1) (1986). OUTCOME: The court overruled the request of relators, parent and minor child, for a writ of mandamus against respondent district court judge's order that appointed Harris County Child Protective Services as relator minor child's temporary managing conservator. The court held that the order was not an abuse of discretion because relator parent failed to show an infringement of his constitutional rights to the free exercise of religion or to privacy.

Elam v. State


No. 01-89-00048-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1234



May 24, 1990, Delivered


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 8834198.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Criminal Court of Harris County (Texas) which convicted her of cruelty to animals under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.11(a)(2) following a finding that appellant failed to provide an animal with necessary food, shelter, and medical care.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of cruelty to animals under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.11(a)(2) for failing to provide the necessary food, shelter, and medical care to sustain the life of a dog in her custody. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in overruling her objection to the state's peremptory challenges, alleging that the state discriminated on the basis of race. Appellant also alleged error in the denial of her motion to quash the information for failure to provide adequate notice of the charges against her. The court affirmed, holding that given the presence of one black person on the jury and the concededly neutral explanation for the peremptory strike of another black venireperson, there was sufficient evidence to support the trial court's conclusion that the state did not peremptorily strike a juror solely on the basis of his race. Further, § 42.11(a)(2) sufficiently informed appellant of the nature of the cause against her. There was no error in the trial court's jury instructions, and a rational jury could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant intentionally or knowingly failed unreasonably to provide necessary care for the dog in her custody.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for committing cruelty to animals because the jury's finding that appellant intentionally or knowingly failed unreasonably to provide necessary care for a dog in her custody was well-supported, the applicable statute provided sufficient notice of the nature and cause against appellant, and there was evidence that the prosecution did not strike a juror solely on the basis of race.

Chavez v. State


No. 01-89-00402-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1267



May 24, 1990, Delivered


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 174th District Court; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 519941.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 174th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which held that his sentence for conviction of aggravated robbery would be cumulated with the sentence imposed in another case, for which he was also convicted of aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: A jury found appellant guilty of aggravated robbery; the jury also assessed punishment at confinement. Before the trial court could pronounce that sentence, the state filed a motion to cumulate it with a sentence rendered in another case, also resulting from an aggravated robbery conviction. Appellant challenged the order, arguing that the record was devoid of any evidence of the prior conviction and sentence. The court found it relevant that both convictions occurred in the same trial court, as a trial court could judicially take notice of its own records in a criminal case, including all judgments and convictions entered by it. As appellee called the trial court's attention to appellant's prior conviction, and because that conviction occurred in that same court, the trial court judicially recognized that fact as true and any proof was unnecessary. The court also noted that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.08(a) (Supp. 1990), which allowed for cumulation of sentences, did not deprive a party of his constitutional right to due process; moreover, the statute had been held to be constitutional. The order below was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Order cumulating appellant's sentence for an aggravated robbery conviction with another sentence, also for a prior aggravated robbery conviction occurring in the same trial court, was affirmed. The trial court took judicial notice of the fact of appellant's prior conviction as true, making any proof unnecessary, and the statutory article allowing for such cumulation did not deprive appellant of due process, nor was it unconstitutional.

 

1741 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Shaw v. State


No. B14-88-00905-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1134



May 17, 1990, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 13; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 8812635. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 13, Harris County, Texas, which convicted her of resisting arrest and which assessed a fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for resisting arrest after being stopped for a traffic violation and behaving belligerently. She was convicted and ordered to pay a fine. The court affirmed the trial court's conviction. The court held that defendant was not denied a court-appointed lawyer because it had indeed appointed one, just not one who would put forward the arguments she wanted. Because a lawyer had been appointed for defendant, there was no reason to admonish her about the dangers and disadvantages of proceeding pro se as required in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Art. 1.051(g) (1990). There was no error in not giving her an opportunity to object to the amended information because she had been given notice of the amendment, had ample time to respond, and did not do so. There was also no error in not allowing the jury to recommend probation because defendant failed to offer evidence that she was eligible for probation. Defendant's mere filing of her affidavit, as set out in Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12 § 4(b) (1990), was not sufficient to establish her eligibility for probation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for resisting arrest. The court held that defendant was not denied her right to appointed counsel, that the trial court was not required to admonish her of the dangers and disadvantages of proceeding pro se, that she was not prejudiced by not receiving a copy of the amended information, and that the trial court did not err in not allowing the jury to recommend probation.

 

1742 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Ochs v. Martinez


Appeal No. 04-89-00007-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


789 S.W.2d 949; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1652



May 16, 1990, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

Appeal from the 57th District Court of Bexar County; Trial Court No. 85CI-20194; Honorable Carol R. Haberman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants mother and grandparents challenge an order by the 57th District Court of Bexar County(Texas), claiming that an order changing the conservatorship of two young girls from their mother to their father was error. Appellants also claimed that the testimony by appellee father's witnesses that the mother's new husband had sexually abused the younger of the two girls was improperly admitted.


OVERVIEW: Appellants mother and grandparents claimed that a jury's verdict which changed custody from appellant mother to appellee father based on allegations of sexual abuse by appellant mother's new husband was reversible error. The court agreed, and in reversing it held that the videotaped testimony of the child was improper because the questioner used leading questions throughout her questioning. The court also held that appellee had elicited improper testimony when he asked witnesses to act as human lie detectors telling jury whether the child was telling the truth. The court held that it was completely improper because the witnesses invaded the province of the jury; only they could determine the truth or veracity of a witness. Additionally, the court held that the trial court erred in admitting expert opinion testimony as to the child's truthfulness. Again the court held that the expert invaded the province of the jury regarding the truthfulness of the child. In conclusion, the court refused to relax the law of evidence to allow hearsay testimony in a case involving allegations of sexual abuse of a child. It reversed holding that the trial court erred in admitting the testimony.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment transferring custody to appellee father and remanded for a new trial, holding that appellee had elicited improper testimony and that the trial court erred in admitting expert opinion testimony as to the child's truthfulness.

Conklin v. Broach Oil Co.


No. B14-88-00965-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1073



May 10, 1990, Rendered and Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 272nd District Court; Brazos County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 29,577-272.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant debtor sought review of a decision by the 272nd District Court of Brazos County (Texas), which entered a turnover order requiring appellant to endorse one paycheck each month and place it with the court clerk, beginning in August 1988, to enable appellee company to obtain satisfaction of a judgment against appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant debtor challenged an order requiring him to endorse one paycheck each month and place it with the court clerk, beginning in August, 1988, to enable appellee company to obtain satisfaction of a judgment against appellant for damages, plus attorneys fees, court costs, and interest. The appellate court affirmed the turnover order because the order was not violative of Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 28 (1983), Tex. Prop. Code Ann. § 42.002(8) (1984), and Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 63.004 (1986), which exempted current wages for personal services from garnishment or seizure, other than for court-ordered child support payments. The court held further that appellant had not established an abuse of discretion by the trial court. The appellate court stated that once appellant came into possession of the paycheck, it no longer constituted exempt current wages for personal services. Furthermore, the case did not involve a third party in possession of appellant's property or owing money to appellant. The appellate court also stated that it was unconvinced that the trial judge acted arbitrarily or unreasonably in ordering appellant to turn over $ 750.00 from his monthly paycheck.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the turnover order because the order was not violative of constitutional and statutory provisions that exempted current wages for personal services from garnishment or seizure, other than for court-ordered child support payments, and appellant had not established an abuse of discretion by the trial court where it did not act arbitrarily or unreasonably in ordering appellant to turn over money from his paycheck.

State v. Muller


No. 01-89-00306-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1089



May 10, 1990, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn August 23, 1990. Substituted Opinion Reported at 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 2158. Rehearing Granted August 23, 1990. State's Motion for Rehearing on Petition for Discretionary Review Denied May 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6; Harris County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 8832565; Hon. J. R. Musslewhite, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6, Harris County (Texas), striking a paragraph in the information that charged defendant with operating a motor vehicle in a public place while intoxicated. The struck paragraph alleged a .10 alcohol concentration using Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-5, § 3(a), (b) (1990) and breath alcohol testing regulations which the trial court found to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The state charged defendant with operating a motor vehicle in a public place while intoxicated. Defendant's motion to strike the paragraph of the information that alleged a .10 alcohol concentration, and to suppress intoxilyzer evidence was granted by the trial court finding Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-5, § 3(a), (b) (1990) and Texas Department of Public Safety's Breath Alcohol Testing Regulations unconstitutional. The court reversed the judgment which reinstated the information and remanded the cause. Nothing prohibited an assistant prosecuting attorney from signing a notice of appeal and the defect was cured. Breath alcohol test regulations and statutes were found to be constitutional where they were not unreasonable or arbitrary when enacted. There was no violation of the separation of powers doctrine, due process regarding reasonable terms, vagueness, and unbridled discretion by a scientific director, due process where intoxilyzer evidence's accuracy or reliability was not ensured, due process because multiple breath tests immediately at and after the time of driving were not required, and due process where preservation of a breath specimen was not required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment that granted defendant's motion to strike a paragraph of the information and to suppress intoxilyzer evidence, reinstated the information, and remanded the cause. Breath alcohol testing regulations and statutes were constitutional in an operating a motor vehicle in a public place while intoxicated charge, favoring the state. The notice of appeal, claiming ineffective signature, was cured by an amendment.

In re S.C.


Nos. 3-88-144-CV, 3-89-087-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


790 S.W.2d 766; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1061



May 9, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of March 21, 1990, Reported at 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 646. Motion for Rehearing of Cause Overruled May 9, 1990. Application for Writ of Error Denied November 7, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY 126TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT; NO. J-9470, HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JR., JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged a judgment of the District Court of Travis County 126th Judicial District (Texas), which found that he engaged in delinquent conduct by committing murder. The juvenile court held a release hearing and ordered appellant transferred to the penitentiary at age 18 to serve the remainder of his determinate sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile was adjudicated delinquent for murder and transferred to the penitentiary to finish his 30-year sentence. The court found that appellant was incarcerated for the commission of a Penal Code offense, was adjudicated pursuant to a petition that was procedurally and substantively equivalent to a criminal indictment, and was tried in a quasi-criminal proceeding that provided him with fundamental criminal constitutional protections. The court concluded that appellant could become eligible for parole and did not suffer unequal protection of the laws. The court found that appellant was not criminally prosecuted, because juvenile proceedings are civil proceedings, which are quasi-criminal in nature. The court concluded that the work requirement imposed on appellant was an appropriate punishment and held that the determinate sentencing statute did not impose involuntary servitude or peonage on him in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIII or 42 U.S.C.S. § 1994 (1981). The court affirmed and concluded appellant waived error regarding a prosecutor that previously represented him, because he did not object to her participation either before or during the adjudication process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of appellant juvenile's adjudication and disposition for murder. The court affirmed the order transferring appellant to the penitentiary. The court found that appellant did not suffer unequal protection of the laws.

1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1026

Alvarado v. State


No. B14-89-00122-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 959



April 26, 1990 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 477,684.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 176th District Court, Harris County, Texas, convicting appellant for aggravated robbery. The trial court instructed the jury that they were not to consider how long appellant would be required to serve the sentence they imposed, but did not otherwise instruct the jury on parole law under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated robbery and sentenced to 36 years in prison, after assisting two others in robbing a victim of $ 20,000 and killing her spouse. Appellant challenged his conviction, claiming that the trial court erred in charging the jury on parole law. The court affirmed, finding that the trial court did not improperly instruct the jury on parole law under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07, § 4(a), but only gave a cautionary instruction not to consider how long appellant would be required to serve. Appellant's two statements were given voluntarily, after proper Miranda warnings, and appellant was not under arrest at the time, under either U.S. Const. amend. IV or Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 14.03. Additionally, the evidence did not raise a question of diminished capacity, but the threats to appellant constituted duress, on which the jury was properly instructed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. Appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery was upheld, because the trial court's cautionary instruction to the jury that they not consider how long appellant would serve did not constitute an unlawful charge on parole law.

Matagorda County Appraisal Dist. v. Conquest Exploration Co.


No. 13-89-346-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


788 S.W.2d 687; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 930; 108 Oil & Gas Rep. 402



April 19, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

On appeal from the 130th District Court of Matagorda County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county appraisal district and appraisal review board, sought review of a judgment from the 130th District Court of Matagorda County, Texas, which granted summary judgment granted in favor of appellee mineral exploration company on the grounds that appellants incorrectly appraised and taxed appellee for exempt mineral interests owned by the State of Texas, that the error was clerical, and that appellee should have received a refund.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, county appraisal district and county appraisal review board, sought review of a summary granted in favor of appellee company. The trial court found that appellants incorrectly appraised and taxed Conquest for exempt mineral interests owned by the State of Texas, that the error was clerical, and that appellee should have received a refund. The court reversed the judgment. The court found that appellant review board did not err when it approved that portion of appraisal roll affecting appellee as the state did not have a working interest in any of the gas wells in controversy, and appellee was not taxed for any property interest owned by the state. Further, no clerical error existed in the appraisal roll. Appellee received a correct tax bill based upon the appraisal roll determination. Although appellee was taxed for a greater percent working interest that it owned, such error, if any existed, was judicial rather than clerical in nature because appellant district prepared an accurate appraisal and gave appellee timely notice of those values and appellant review board, in good faith, approved the appraisal records when it did not discover any errors contained therein.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment granting summary judgment in favor of appellee mineral exploration company holding that the trial court erred when it granted appellee a refund because the ownership interests of the pertinent gas wells reflected on the appraisal roll did not constitute a clerical error as a matter of law.

Lauderback v. State


No. 2-88-056-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


789 S.W.2d 343; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1344



April 18, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled June 5, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the County Court of Cooke County; Jim A. Robertson, Trial Court Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the County Court of Cooke County (Texas), which found her guilty of obstructing a highway in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.03(a)(2)(A). Appellant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to show that she was not a handicapped person, and that her rights to free speech were violated because the statute was overly broad and no overriding public interest was shown by enforcing it.


OVERVIEW: In protest of her treatment by an area bank, appellant put a wheelchair with signage in a lane of traffic in the busiest road in town. After being convicted of obstructing a highway in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42,03(a)(2)(A) she sought review, arguing that the evidence was insufficient to show that she was not entitled to additional protections because of a handicap, and that enforcement of the statute denied her freedom of speech in violation of the state and federal constitutions. The court affirmed her conviction, finding that she did not have a legitimate need for the wheelchair, and that even if she had such a right, she would have no legal privilege to be in the highway obstructing traffic because of that handicap. The court held that there was sufficient evidence to show that appellant created an obstruction by making the passage unreasonably inconvenient and hazardous, and that it was necessary to prevent that conduct. The purpose of the statute was to prevent obstructions in the road, not to inhibit speech, and the restriction on appellant's free speech rights was no greater than was essential to prevent appellant from hurting herself or others.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for obstructing a highway, finding that she did not prove she was entitled to the benefits of a handicapped person, but that even if she were, that did not entitle her to obstruct a roadway. Additionally, her freedom of speech was not violated because preventing harm to appellant and others was an overriding public interest and the statutory restriction was no greater than necessary to prevent that harm.

Courtney v. Sherman


No. 05-89-00901-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


792 S.W.2d 135; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1862



April 16, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied March 20, 1991. Motion for Rehearing of Application for Writ of Error Overruled April 16, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 15th Judicial District Court; Grayson County, Texas; Trial Court Cause No. 88-1535.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and Reversed and Rendered in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant club owner challenged a ruling of the 15th Judicial District Court, Grayson County (Texas), which upheld a local ordinance that applied additional restrictions upon the operation of private clubs in appellee city.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city adopted zoning ordinances which, among other things, required that all private clubs granted a permit by the state of Texas must obtain a specific use permit to operate in the city. The ordinances also required that the operation of such clubs be conducted such that revenues from the sale of food was equal to or greater than the revenue produced through the sale of alcohol. Appellant club owner refused to comply with the ordinances at issue and filed an action which claimed that the ordinances were unconstitutional because they conflicted with state law. The trial court deemed two of the three ordinances at issue unconstitutional and appellant challenged that ruling. Appellee filed a cross-appeal and claimed that none of the ordinances were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed in part and affirmed in part the trial court ruling, and deemed all three ordinances unconstitutional. The court held that the state preempted the regulation of private clubs, and the ordinances at issue attempted to make operating a club more onerous than state statutory requirements. For that reason, the ordinances were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part and affirmed in part the trial court ruling, which upheld one of three local ordinances that applied additional restrictions upon the operation of private clubs. The court held that all three ordinances at issue were unconstitutional because the state had preempted the area of private club regulation and the ordinances at issue conflicted directly with state law.

Garza Garza v. State


Nos. 13-89-127-CR, 13-89-128-CR, 13-89-129-CR

The court also found that no ineffective assistance of counsel occurred.

Rezapour v. State


Case No. 06-89-00073-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Sixth District, Texarkana


788 S.W.2d 642; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 803



April 10, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appealed from the 232nd Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for illegal investment by the 232nd Judicial District Court of Harris County, Texas. Defendant alleged his conviction was based on insufficient evidence and an improper charge to the jury.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and co-defendant made an agreement with undercover agents to purchase cocaine. At the planned meeting site, co-defendant went to approve the cocaine while defendant waited in the car with the money. Defendant and co-defendant were arrested before money changed hands. Defendant was convicted of illegal investment. Defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction and that the jury charge was improper. The court affirmed, holding that although the funds did not change hands, the money had been raised and committed by agreement with the agents for the purpose of gaining unlawful possession of the cocaine; therefore, the evidence was sufficient to support the jury's verdict. The court held that it was not necessary that the cocaine actually be received as long as defendant believed the funds would further the delivery of the cocaine. Where the trial court instructed the jury that it should find defendant guilty if they found that he committed the charged offense either individually or as a party, the court found the trial court did not err in submitting the law of the parties to the jury in addition to the question of individual culpability.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for illegal investment because the evidence of defendant's agreement with the under cover agents and defendant's belief that the money would further the delivery of the cocaine, among other things, was sufficient to support the jury's verdict. The court also determined the trial court did not err in its charge to the jury.

Haney v. Texas Real Estate Com.


No. A14-88-01087-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


789 S.W.2d 304; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 745



April 5, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled May 17, 1990. Motion for Rehearing of Application for Writ of Error Overruled November 21, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 56th District Court, Galveston County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 123,978, I. A. Lerner, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant real estate broker sought review of an order of the 56th District Court, Galveston County (Texas), directing appellee, Texas Real Estate Commission to pay appellee individuals sums from the Real Estate Recovery Fund.


OVERVIEW: Appellant real estate broker and a company were found jointly and severally liable to appellee individuals. Appellees settled with the company and then applied to the trial court for an order directing payment from the Real Estate Recovery Fund (Fund) because they were unable to collect the remainder of the judgment from appellant. The court held that appellees were not required to attempt recovery of the entire judgment from the co-debtor prior to seeking reimbursement from the Fund and noted that to so hold would enable appellant to evade both payment of the judgment and disciplinary action from the Texas Real Estate Commission. The court found that appellees were entitled to recover attorney fees incurred in applying for reimbursement from the Fund and those incurred in the underlying suit. Noting that the company paid more than half of the total damages awarded, the court held that the company's failure to pay the entire judgment, for which appellant was jointly and severally liable, did not result in an unconstitutional sate subsidy of a private corporation's debt. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order directing appellee, Texas Real Estate commission to pay appellee individuals sums from the Real Estate Recovery Fund (Fund) because appellee individuals were not required to attempt recovery of the entire judgment from the co-debtor, attorney fees incurred in the underlying suit were recoverable from the Fund, and the order did not result in an unconstitutional state subsidy of a private corporation's debt.

Video News, Inc. v. State


No. 01-88-00824-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


790 S.W.2d 340; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 762



April 5, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 88-16209, Hon. J.R. Musselwhite, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Criminal County Court at Law Number Six, Harris County (Texas) that convicted him of possession with the intent to promote obscene material after the jury found appellant guilty and the court assessed punishment at a $ 5,000 fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's magazine shop was under investigation for selling obscene magazines in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 43.23 (Supp. 1989). Officers secured, on two separate occasions, a search warrant that stated they had probable cause to believe appellant's business was engaged in the sale of obscene materials. Officers seized magazines, which the officers concluded after inspection were obscene. Appellant was convicted of possession with the intent to promote obscene material, and the court assessed punishment at $ 5000. Appellant challenged the conviction, alleging that the trial court erred when it denied appellant's motion to quash the information because the Texas obscenity law was unconstitutionally overbroad; when it denied his motion to suppress for no probable cause; and, when it failed to give jury instruction regarding purient interest and the average person. The court found that the Texas constitution did not extend freedom to obscene material, that the magazines were seized for preservation of evidence, and that the jury instruction requested was substantially the same as the one given, which caused no harm. The case was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the case finding that the obscene magazines were not constitutionally protected, that seizure of them was for the purpose of preserving evidence, and that the jury instruction was very similar to appellant's requested instruction and was not harmful.

Pend Oreille Oil & Gas Co. v. Railroad Com. of Texas


No. 13-88-581-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


788 S.W.2d 878; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 771; 113 Oil & Gas Rep. 557



April 5, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted by Court on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of February 28, 1990, Reported at 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 454. Application for Writ of Error Granted November 21, 1990. Motion for Rehearing of Cause Overruled September 11, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 156th District Court of Live Oak County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, royalty interest owners and gas companies, sought review of a judgment from the 156th District Court of Live Oak County (Texas), which affirmed appellee commission's order that granted appellee lessee's application to force pool his tracts with those containing appellee royalty interest owners' existing gas well pursuant to the Mineral Interest Pooling Act, Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. § 102 et. seq. (1978).


OVERVIEW: On review, the court determined that appellee commission lacked authority to enter an order granting the application to force pool both the main sand and the stray sand because the authority to pool under the Mineral Interest Pooling Act (MIPA), Tex. Nat. Res. Code Ann. § 102 et. seq. (1978), was limited to pooling tracts that were embraced in a reservoir whose deposits, if separated, were in natural communication. The court further held that the granting of a 16 Tex. Admin. Code § 3.10 commingling exception did not alter appellee commission's authority to pool. The court directed that to the extent appellee commission exceeded its authority by pooling two separate reservoirs, the order was to be reformed by vacating the portion pooling the stray sand and affirming the portion that pooled the main sand because substantial evidence showed that the offer was fair and reasonable from the standpoint of the party being force pooled. The court concluded by reversing, in part, the retroactive applicability of the final order as applied to the period between the final field order and the final MIPA order because it interfered with appellants' vested property rights.


OUTCOME: Although the court affirmed appellee commission's order granting appellee lessee's application to force pool, reforming the order to vacate the portion that pooled the stray sand, the court partially reversed the order to the extent that it applied retroactively to the period between the final field order and the final Mineral Interest Pooling Act order because it interfered with vested property rights.

 

1759 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


McLean v. State


No. 13-89-214-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


787 S.W.2d 196; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 680



March 29, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Overruled April 19, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 347th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the 347th District Court of Nueces County (Texas), which entered a conviction for voluntary manslaughter. The jury answered a special issue, which found that defendant had used a deadly weapon to commit the offense. Defendant claimed lack of notice as to the special issue, insufficiency of the evidence, and challenged the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.18, § 8(b)(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with murder and found guilty of voluntary manslaughter by the jury. The jury also answered a special issue finding that defendant had used a deadly weapon to commit the offense. The court affirmed in all respects. Defendant claimed that he lacked notice that the state intended to seek a finding on the special issue. The court held that any allegation that averred that a death was caused by a named weapon or instrument necessarily included sufficient notice that the nature of the weapon would be at issue in the trial. The court found that evidence that defendant threatened the victim, retrieved a knife, and then stabbed him was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to conclude that defendant used the knife as a deadly weapon. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.18, § 8(b)(1) (Supp. 1990) was not unconstitutional because there was nothing unreasonable in a legislative scheme which required persons who use deadly weapons to serve a minimum prison term before being eligible for parole.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the special issue finding by the jury that defendant had used a deadly weapon to commit the offense of voluntary manslaughter. The court held that defendant was on notice that the nature of the weapon was at issue. There was sufficient evidence to support the jury's finding. The court held that a minimum prison term for people who use deadly weapons was constitutional.

Minton v. Ft. Worth Planning Com


No. 2-87-125-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Second District, Fort Worth


786 S.W.2d 563; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 873



March 28, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

FROM THE 236TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY, ALBERT L. WHITE, JR., JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sought review of a decision from the 236th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which declared a property re-platting consent statute, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 974a, § 5(c)(2) (1987), as constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant property owner proposed to the local planning commission his plan to re-plat his lot of property into three separate lots. At the time, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 974a, § 5(c)(2) (1987), required that the owners of lots within 500 feet of the proposed re-plat be notified. If 20 percent of such owners objected to the proposed re-plat, then written approval of 66 2/3 percent of such owners was required for approval. The commission denied the re-plat because more than 20 percent of the owners objected. Appellant then filed a declaratory judgment action, contending that the consent statute was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority. The reviewing court agreed with appellant that the statute delegated the legislative power given by the people to the legislative body, to a narrow segment of the community. The court held that such delegation of authority was contrary to the constitution and reversed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment finding the consent statute at issue to be constitutional was reversed based on the court's holding that the statute delegated the legislative power given by the people to the legislative body to a narrow segment of the community and was therefore contrary to the constitution.

Jannise v. State


No. 09-88-089 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


789 S.W.2d 623; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1422



March 28, 1990, Delivered  
March 28, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 11, 1990, Discretionary Review Denied May 10, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appealed from the 75th District Court of Liberty County, Texas. This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of February 14, 1990.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a jury verdict of guilt in the 75th District Court of Liberty County, Texas, of aggravated sexual assault of a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault of a child and sought review, based on his contention that the admission of evidence of sexual assaults on another child at the same time as the victim was prejudicial and that the jury was not properly charged relative to his right not to testify. The court affirmed the verdict and remanded for a new trial on the punishment phase. The court held that appellant had made several voluntary statements which corroborated the complainant's testimony as well as the other child victim's testimony. The court held that the extraneous offenses were relevant and their probative value was not substantially outweighed by unfair prejudice. The court further held that failure to include a limiting instruction with regard to the extraneous offenses was not reversible error because the evidence in the case and the confessions were so overwhelming that it would not have effected the outcome. The court did hold that it was error for the trial court not to have instructed the jury regarding appellant's choice not to testify at the punishment stage.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jury verdict as to the guilt/innocence phase and remanded for a new trial as to the punishment phase only because the jury was not properly charged as to appellant's right not to testify.

Laws 238, known as House Bill 170, was unconstitutional in rendering summary judgment for appellees, corporation and others, on their declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, state board of insurance and others, challenged the trial court's ruling that 1987 Tex. Gen. Laws 238, known as House Bill 170, was unconstitutional as the bill by which the law was enacted contained two subjects and, therefore, violated Tex. Const. art. III, § 35(a), when it rendered summary judgment for appellees, corporation and others, on their declaratory judgment action. The court found that as the bill contained two separate subjects, it violated the one-subject rule and was, therefore, unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court that ruled bill was unconstitutional in rendering summary judgment for appellees, corporation and others, on their declaratory judgment action, was affirmed, as the bill contained more than one subject and was unconstitutional.

In re S. C.


Nos. 3-88-144-CV, 3-89-087-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 646



March 21, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn May 9, 1990; Substituted Opinion Reported at 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1061 


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 126TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT, NO. J-9470, HONORABLE PAUL R. DAVIS, JR., JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his delinquency adjudication by the District Court of Travis County, 126th Judicial District (Texas), for committing murder at age 16. Appellant was sentenced to a determinate sentence of 30 years under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 54.03 and 54.04 (1990), and was transferred to the penitentiary at age 18 to complete his sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant committed murder at the age of 16 and a jury found that he engaged in delinquent conduct and committed him to the Texas Youth Commission subject to transfer to the penitentiary for a total of 30 years under Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 54.03 and 54.04 (1990). At the age of 18, appellant was transferred to the penitentiary and then challenged his judgment of adjudication and disposition, and the order of transfer. The court affirmed, however, finding that appellant had not been transferred without possibility of parole, because the legislature, under Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 498.053(c) (1990), granted parole eligibility to persons transferred from the Texas Youth Commission. Therefore, the court found that appellant's sentence did not violate his equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Tex. Const. art. I, § 3. The court further found that appellant's sentence did not constitute involuntary servitude under U.S. Const. amend. XIII or the Anti-Peonage Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1994. Finally, the court found that appellant was not improperly prosecuted for a criminal offense because delinquency proceedings are primarily civil in nature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's adjudication, disposition, and transfer to complete a 30-year determinate sentence for committing murder at age 16, finding that appellant's equal protection rights were not violated because he became eligible for parole in the same manner as adult offenders.

Oliver v. State


Nos. 09-89-002 CR, 09-89-003 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


787 S.W.2d 170; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 1000



March 21, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEALED FROM THE 1-A DISTRICT COURT OF TYLER COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of controlled substances possession convictions in favor of appellee state in the District Court of Tyler County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of convictions for controlled substance possession in favor of appellee state based on the argument the lower court never acquired jurisdiction when the indictments failed to allege the essential elements of the offenses. The court reversed and remanded for dismissal of the indictments, concluding the charging instruments failed to allege the required mental states. The court rejected appellee's argument that appellant waived the error by not complaining of the defect before the date of trial. The court explained that in order to invoke the jurisdiction of the court, the charging instrument had to allege an offense. The court determined the culpable mental state was an element of the offense that had to be pled. As a result, the court found the lower court never acquired jurisdiction, and a jurisdictional defect was able to be raised at any time. The court further noted in the indictments an essential element was simply absent from the face of the instrument and no words were alleged which could reasonably substitute for such elements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for dismissal of indictments for possession of controlled substances in favor of appellant because appellee state's failure to allege essential element of offense mental state rendered the indictments fundamentally defective, so the lower court never acquired jurisdiction.

Maderazo v. Archem Co.


No. B14-88-00737-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


788 S.W.2d 395; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 547



March 15, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

On Appeal from the 164th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 88-8038, Peter S. Solito, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, parents of an deceased employee, sought review of an order of the 164th District Court, Harris County (Texas), granting appellee employer summary judgment. Appellants brought suit seeking actual and exemplary damages. Appellee filed a motion for summary judgment on the ground that appellants' exclusive remedy was a claim under the Workers' Compensation Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 71.003.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, parents of a deceased employee, brought suit under the Wrongful Death Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8306, against appellee employer for the wrongful death of their son in an explosion on appellee's premises. Appellee was a subscriber of the Workers' Compensation Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 71.003. The trial court granted summary judgment and ruled that appellants' exclusive remedy was a claim against the compensation carrier. The court found that under the Wrongful Death Act, parents of a deceased were designated as beneficiaries entitled to recover. That act, however, limits recovery to actions in which the injured would have been entitled to bring suit if he had lived. In affirming the award of summary judgment, the court ruled that because appellants' son was covered by workers' compensation insurance, he was deemed to have waived his common-law cause of action against his employer. Appellants were therefore precluded from bringing suit because their son would not have been entitled to sue had he lived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting summary judgment to appellee employer in the wrongful death action brought by appellants, parents of an deceased employee. The court ruled that appellants' exclusive remedy was a suit against the workers' compensation carrier.

State v. Taylor


No. 13-89-299-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


787 S.W.2d 120; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 491



March 8, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 105th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State challenged the order from the 105th District Court of Nueces County, Texas, which dismissed the indictment filed against appellee for "Keeping A Gambling Place" in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 47.04(a) (1989).


OVERVIEW: In passing on the vagueness challenge, the court noted that it should not consider hypothetical situations but should scrutinize the statute only to determine whether it was impermissibly vague as applied to appellant. Assuming that appellant acted as alleged in the indictment, the court looked to see if the statute provided appellant with notice so that he could ascertain to what extent his conduct was criminal, and that law enforcement authorities were given sufficient standards to prevent arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement. The court found that under the statute's present form, the state could obtain a conviction of appellee for "Keeping A Gambling Place" on evidence which merely showed that he "received bets" at a certain building. The statute does not require that the receipt of bets at the location constituted bookmaking. As the indictment only alleged that appellant controlled a place that "received bets," without specifying that he controlled a place where the act of bookmaking occurred, the court found that the trial court did not err in dismissing the indictment. Thus, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order as the statute failed for vagueness in that had not given notice to appellant so that he could ascertain to what extent his conduct was criminal, and had not given law enforcement authorities sufficient standards to prevent arbitrary and discriminatory enforcement.

Defendant also contended that his sentence violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. The court rejected defendant's contention, finding that the punishment assessed was within statutory limits.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

ORIGINAL PROCEEDING, WRIT OF MANDAMUS.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator judge sought a writ of mandamus to order respondent party chairman to remove a rival's name from the ballot for judge, claiming that rival failed to gather the required number of voter signatures under Tex. Elec. Code Ann. Art. 172.021 (e) (1990).

Elec. Code Ann. Art. 172.021 (e) (1990). A would-be candidate for the office sought had to pay either a filing fee and tender a petition with 250 signatures or tender a petition with 750 signatures under the statute. The petition lacked the required number of signatures after duplicate signatures were eliminated. It was inconceivable that the state constitution forbade requiring a limited number of signatures to be drawn from a county of millions of citizens.
