Pend Oreille Oil & Gas Co. v. Railroad Com. of Texas


No. 13-88-581-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 454



February 28, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn by Order of the Court on Denial of Rehearing April 5, 1990; Substituted Opinion Reported at 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 771 


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 156th District Court of Live Oak County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, landowners and a company, challenged a judgment from the District Court of Live Oak County (Texas), which affirmed appellee railroad commission's order granting appellee landowner's application to force pool his tracts with those containing appellant landowners' gas well.


OVERVIEW: Appellants owned interests in tracts of land located within a gas field. Appellee landowner (landowner) held an oil and gas lease on land adjacent to appellants. Appellee commission (commission) granted landowner's application to force pool his tracts with appellants' tracts. The trial court affirmed the commission's order. On appeal, the court held that the commission did not have authority to force pooling of stray sand and main sand as a common reservoir because there was no natural communication. However, the court held that the commission only exceeded its jurisdiction that it pooled both sands in one proceeding. The court also held that landowner met the jurisdiction requirements of Tex. Nat. Res. Code § 102.013 when he filed his application. The court found that appellee made a fair and reasonable offer for voluntary pooling before seeking forced pooling. Appellee also demonstrated standing by showing that pooling would prevent the drilling of an unnecessary well. The court also modified the order to the extent that retroactive application affected appellants' property rights and was unconstitutional. Judgment was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and partially vacated.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that affirmed appellee commission's order was affirmed in part because the commission had the authority to force pool main sand and the landowner met jurisdictional requirement and had standing. Judgment was reversed in part and partially vacated because the commission lacked authority to force pool stray sand and portions of its order could not be applied retroactively.

Flood v. State


No. C14-89-00179-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 382



February 22, 1990 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 522,804.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal appellant challenged his conviction in the 185th District Court of Harris County (Texas) for misdemeanor theft which was upgraded to felony theft by two prior thefts pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(e)(4)(C) and his sentence of 25 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's misdemeanor conviction was upgraded to felony theft by two prior thefts pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.03(e)(4)(C). Appellant was sentenced to the minimum for a habitual criminal, 25 years. On appeal, appellant argued that the enhancement statute was unconstitutional; that his punishment was improperly enhanced under the repeat and habitual felony statute; and that his punishment was cruel and excessive. The court held that the challenged statute, which provided for the enhancement of theft offenses was not unconstitutional in general and was particularly not unconstitutional as to appellant. His argument was purely theoretical and did not reflect his situation. The court further held that, even if appellant had been pardoned on the prior felony conviction, it would still be available for enhancement purposes. On appellant's cruel and unusual punishment claim, the court held that under the habitual criminal statute, appellant's 25 year sentence was the minimum punishment allowed and that Texas courts have consistently held that punishment assessed by a judge or jury within the statutory limit was not cruel or unusual.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment on the basis that the enhancement statute was not unconstitutional, appellant's habitual felony enhancement was proper, and because his sentence did not constitute cruel or unusual punishment.

 

1774 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Travelers Indem. Co. v. Montelongo


No. 13-89-191-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


785 S.W.2d 436; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 365



February 21, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled March 8, 1990


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 24th District Court of Refugio County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurance carrier challenged the order of the 24th District Court of Refugio County (Texas), which granted appellee claimant's motion to dismiss appellant's suit because it lacked subject matter jurisdiction to hear an appeal of a completely favorable ruling from the Industrial Accident Board.


OVERVIEW: Appellee claimant filed a claim with the Industrial Accident Board (IAB) for benefits after the death of her husband. The IAB entered a completely favorable ruling for appellant insurance carrier. The day after the ruling, appellant filed a suit in Refugio County, where the accident occurred. Minutes later, appellee filed suit in Duval County, where the husband had resided. Appellee filed a motion to dismiss appellant's suit. The court granted the motion, finding that it lacked subject matter jurisdiction. Appellant contended that the appeal from the IAB award was not a true appeal because the filing of the suit vacated the IAB ruling. On appeal the court affirmed the dismissal, because subject matter jurisdiction over a case depended on the facts at the time the suit was initiated. At the time appellant filed its petition, the totally favorable IAB ruling was in force. Therefore, the court did not have subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The grant of appellee claimant's motion to dismiss appellant insurance carrier's suit concerning benefits after appellee's husband died was affirmed, because the trial court did not have subject matter jurisdiction to hear an appeal of the Industrial Accident Board's completely favorable ruling.

Batiste v. State


No. 13-89-335-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Thirteenth District, Corpus Christi


785 S.W.2d 432; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 386



February 21, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 8, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 230th District Court of Harris County, Texas.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for aggravated sexual assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code. Ann. § 22.021 (1989), entered in the 230th District Court of Harris County (Texas). Appellant contended that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.10 (1989) was unconstitutional because it allowed an indictment to be amended without further presentation to the grand jury.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was tried and convicted for aggravated sexual assault in violation of Tex. Penal Code. Ann. § 22.021 (1989). The indictment as originally presented included two enhancement allegations. Before trial, the state moved to substitute one felony conviction for another. Appellant did not challenge the sufficiency of the evidence pertaining to the offense for which he was tried. Rather, he asserted that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.10 (1989) was unconstitutional because it allowed an indictment to be amended without further presentation to the grand jury. The court affirmed the conviction and noted that the requirement that amendment of indictments be presented to the grand jury dealt with the substantive offense for which appellant was being accused. The amendment of an indictment that was related to enhancement allegations had nothing to do with the substance of the original indictment and did not charge appellant with an additional or different offense.


OUTCOME: The trial court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault and found that, although appellant had a right to notice of a prior conviction on which the state would rely to enhance appellant's punishment, appellant had no right to a grand jury probable cause determination regarding that prior conviction.

 

1776 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. Comeaux


No. 3-88-091-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Third District, Austin


786 S.W.2d 480; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 644



February 21, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 5 OF TRAVIS COUNTY, NO 287-664, HONORABLE WILFRED AGUILAR, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a decision of the County Court at Law No. 5 for Travis County (Texas) that suppressed evidence of appellee accused's blood-alcohol test results. The state contended that the results were admissible because appellee had consented to the search and also because no state agent had conducted the search.


OVERVIEW: The state charged appellee accused with driving while intoxicated in violation of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. § 67011-1 (1990). The arrest grew out of an accident that occurred while appellee was returning from a party. The accident was not appellee's fault. While at the hospital, medical personnel ordered a blood sample to assist in diagnosis and treatment of appellee's injuries. The state requested and obtained a portion of this sample for analysis. Neither the state nor the medical personnel had noted any signs of intoxication by appellee prior to the test. The trial court suppressed the blood test results. The court affirmed and noted that appellee had not consented to the search by the state and there was no warrant obtained by the search. Thus, the state had to prove that the search was justified by an exception to the warrant requirement. The court found that appellee's simple acquiescence to a claim of lawful authority was not sufficient to establish an exception to the warrant requirement. The court also noted that the seizure of the blood sample by the police officer from the nurse constituted state involvement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's suppression of the results form appellee's blood alcohol test, taken after appellee was in an accident, because the search was per se unreasonable where the state conducted the search without a warrant. The court also rejected the state's arguments that the search was a private search and was therefore not subject to the warrant requirement.

McFadden v. State


No. 01-88-00933-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 320



February 15, 1990 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 509333, Mary Bacon, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal sought review from a judgment of the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted her of injury to a child by omission or failure to act under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.04 (1989) and assessed punishment at 70 years confinement in a case brought by appellee, the state of Texas.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal challenged her conviction of injury to a child by omission or failure to act under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.04 (1989). Appellant contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the definition of bodily injury in § 1.07(a)(7) was not so vague that it violated due process. Appellant alleged insufficient proof to show that she possessed the requisite mental state. The court held that appellant knew of circumstances that would have endangered her child's safety. Appellant argued that expert testimony of a psychologist was improperly excluded. Appellant did not raise the defense of insanity and was not entitled to such testimony. Appellant questioned the denial of her motion for directed verdict. Any possible error was waived because appellant put on a defense after her motion. Appellant questioned the admitting of letters seized from her residence and certain photographs. The court held that the letters were in plain view and that the exhibits were not preserved for review. Appellant finally complained that she was denied a fair and impartial trial. The court found that no complaint was preserved for review. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of appellant criminal for injury to a child by omission or failure to act in a case brought by appellee, the state of Texas. The court held that the definition of bodily injury was not so vague that it violated due process, that appellant possessed the requisite mental state, that appellant was not entitled to testimony on insanity, and that the evidence admitted was in plain view or not preserved for review.

Fogo v. State


No. C14-89-00492-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


786 S.W.2d 777; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 321



February 15, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Reversed and Cause Remanded April 15, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court At Law No. 3, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 8,903,942, Robert Moen, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the County Criminal Court At Law No. 3, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of the misdemeanor offense of making a political contribution that exceeded $ 100 in cash in aggregate amount in a single reporting period.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for the misdemeanor offense of making a political contribution that exceeded $ 100 in cash in aggregate amount in a single reporting period. Appellant contended that the election statute, which criminalized his contribution, was unconstitutionally vague and that he was unaware that his actions were against the law. Appellant further contended that Texas legislative history indicated an intent to remove criminal penalties for the making of political contributions. The court stated that the election statute clearly criminalized the making of a political contribution such as appellant's and that although the statute was inartfully worded, the legislative intent was clear and its directive was to be upheld. The court found no merit to appellant's contention that he was unaware of the election statute prior to his violation because the evidence showed that appellant was an attorney, a frequent political contributor, and a former political candidate. Therefore, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted appellant of making an illegal campaign contribution.


OUTCOME: The conviction of appellant for the misdemeanor offense of making a political contribution that exceeded $ 100 in cash in aggregate amount in a single reporting period was affirmed. As an attorney, frequent political contributor, and former political candidate, appellant could not argue ignorance of the election statute, which was clear in its intent to criminalize his conduct.

Thomas v. State


No. C14-89-00564-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 322



February 15, 1990 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 12, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 8,841,596.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 12, Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of criminal trespass under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.05(a)(2)(A) (1989).


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of criminal trespass under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.05(a)(2)(A) (1989). The court affirmed that conviction on appeal. The court noted that appellant waived any possible error as to the denial of his motion for instructed verdict of acquittal by presenting evidence in his defense after his motion was denied. The court also found that appellant's conviction did not implicate his free speech rights under U.S. Const. amend. I and Tex. Const. art. I, § 8 because the private club where he was arrested was not a public forum. The court also found that appellant's uncontrolled outburst after being escorted to the club's office to await the police was admissible as a spontaneous and voluntary oral outburst that did not result from interrogation or a response to a police inquiry. The court additionally held that appellant failed to preserve the issue of the trial court's denial of his oral motion to quash the information against him because all motions to set aside an information had to be in writing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's criminal trespass conviction, noting that his presentation of evidence after his instructed verdict motion was denied waived any error as to that denial. The court also found that appellant's outburst after being detained in a club's office was an admissible spontaneous voluntary statement, and that he did not preserve the issue of a denial of his oral motion to quash his information because it was not written.

Shell Pipeline Corp. v. Coastal States Trading, Inc.


No. 01-89-00452-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


788 S.W.2d 837; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 343



February 15, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Writ of Error Denied January 9, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 333rd District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 83-09503, Hon. Davie L. Wilson, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pipeline company sought review of a judgment by the 333rd District Court, Harris County, Texas, which awarded appellee trading company damages and prejudgment interest in its action against appellant for negligence and breach of contract after it mis-delivered crude oil to a nominee other than the one to whom appellee had contracted to sell the oil.


OVERVIEW: The court reformed the judgment against appellant pipeline company, for negligently delivering oil to a company different from the one to which appellee trading company had sold it, to account for appellee's recovery from the receiving entity and affirmed it as reformed. The Federal Energy Regulatory Commission did not have exclusive or primary jurisdiction over the case and appellant did not rebut the presumption that the trial court had jurisdiction. The parties had an enforceable contract and appellant's failure to discover the mismatch of nominations breached appellant's duty to appellee. There was sufficient evidence to support the findings that appellant's breach of contractual and common-law duties was the proximate cause of appellee's damage and to support the trial court's apportionment of fault. Appellant failed to present the trial court with controverting evidence of market prices and thus could not show that the trial court used an erroneous measure in calculating the market value of the oil. The trial court properly assessed 10 percent prejudgment interest because the case involved both tort and contract issues and because the damages were not ascertainable.


OUTCOME: The court reformed the judgment to account for appellee trading company's pre-trial recovery from the receiving nominee and affirmed the judgment as reformed. Appellant pipeline company was negligent and also breached its contract with appellee when it mis-delivered oil to the wrong nominee. The trial court properly exercised jurisdiction over the case and properly based the prejudgment interest calculation on contract and tort grounds.

Ex parte Williams


No. 01-89-00651-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


786 S.W.2d 781; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 345



February 15, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 339th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 526,351, Norman Lanford, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the 339th District Court of Harris County (Texas), which denied defendant's relief requested in his writ of habeas corpus. Defendant requested the trial court dismiss the information issued against him by the county criminal court at law for unlawfully carrying a weapon under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02 (1974).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by information in a county criminal court at law for unlawfully carrying a weapon under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02 (1974). Defendant filed in the district court a writ of habeas corpus. The district court denied defendant's relief. Upon appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 11.05 (1965), the district court had power and jurisdiction to issue defendant's writ of habeas corpus even though defendant was charged by information in the county criminal court. The court found that Tex. Penal Code § 46.02 (1974) was not unconstitutional because the statute did not impinge upon a person's right to keep and bear arms under Tex. Const. art. I, § 23. The court reasoned that a person only had the right to keep and bear arms if there was evidence that the possession of weapons had some reasonable relationship to the preservation or efficiency of a well regulated militia. The court held that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 46.02 was not unconstitutionally vague where the statute set a standard that was sufficiently clear and definite so that an ordinary person would know the proscribed conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that denied the relief requested by defendant in his writ of habeas corpus. The court held that the statute that defendant was charged under for unlawful possession of a weapon was not unconstitutional because it did not impinge upon a person's right to keep and bear arms.

Flowers v. State


No. 08-88-00352-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


785 S.W.2d 890; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 288



February 14, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Discretionary Review Granted September 18, 1991, Reported at 1991 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 181.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from 161st District Court of Ector County, Texas, Tryon D. Lewis, (TC# B-19, 123).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction in the 161st District Court of Ector County, Texas for second degree felony theft of oil field equipment under Tex. Penal Code Ann. 31.03(a)(3), (e)(5)(A)(ii) (1988) and his sentence to four years imprisonment. Appellant argued points of error in the state's amendment of essential elements of the grand jury indictments over his trial objections.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested in a sting operation regarding the theft of oil field equipment. After indictment, he was convicted for second degree felony theft under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 31.03(a)(3), (e)(5)(A)(ii) (1988) and sentenced to four years imprisonment. Appellant raised points of error and argued that the state improperly amended the grand jury indictment despite his trial objections. The court reversed the conviction, vacated the amended indictment, and remanded to the trial court. The court found that changing the indictment to reflect a different property owner and adding a new statutory element alleging that appellant believed he received stolen property were violations of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 28.10 (1988) which allowed amendments under certain conditions not found in this case. The violations confronted appellant with a different offense, prejudiced his substantive rights by failing to provide adequate notice to prepare a defense, and rendered appellant's subsequent trial and conviction void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for second degree felony theft of oil field equipment, vacated the grand jury amended indictment and remanded to the trial court. The court found that amendments to the indictment that changed the property owner and that added a statutory element alleging appellant's belief he received stolen property were improper and violated the statute allowing amendments, rendering appellant's subsequent trial void.

Morris v. State


No. 05-88-01205-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fifth District, Dallas


786 S.W.2d 451; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 798



February 14, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Criminal Court, Dallas County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. MB88-330-30-A. Opinion of January 2, 1990 Withdrawn and Substituted on Grant of Rehearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged her jury conviction in the County Criminal Court, Dallas County, Texas, for the offense of failure to leave information following an automobile collision under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, § 39 (1964).


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for the offense of failure to leave information following an automobile collision under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, § 39 (1964). The court found that the applicable statutes gave sufficient notice of what conduct was required because Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 6701d, §§ 39 and 40 (1964) read in conjunction with Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. arts. 6675a-2 and 6675a-3e, made it sufficiently clear that the term vehicle registration number as used in § 40 meant license plate number. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support her conviction and show that she knowingly failed to provide the required information after the accident, and that it was not the complainant's duty to obtain the information. Proof of noncompliance with any one of the five § 40 requirements constituted an offense under § 39 and it was unnecessary for the trial court to charge her on all requirements. Failure to give her name, address, and vehicle registration number were three separate means of committing an offense under §§ 39 and 40 and therefore it was proper for the trial court to charge only on the two means supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for failure to leave information following an automobile collision because the statutes gave ample notice of the required conduct, the evidence was sufficient to convict her, the violation of each component of the statute could be charged separately, and the controlling statute could be violated by failing to do any one of the three distinct required actions addressed therein.

Graham v. State


Nos. 01-89-00625-CR, 01-89-00626-CR, 01-89-00627-CR, 01-89-00628-CR, 01-89-00629-CR, 01-89-00630-CR, 01-89-00631-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, First District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 200



February 1, 1990 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 2, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 4441.

On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 3, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 4425.

On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 5, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 4491.

On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 11, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 4511.

On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 4546.

On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 4510.

On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 3, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 4377.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A municipal court (Texas), convicted appellants of having operated an adult arcade without a permit. Upon appellants' plea of nolo contendere, the court found appellants guilty and assessed them each a fine of $ 750.00. On appeal, the County Criminal Courts, Harris County (Texas), affirmed the convictions.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were convicted of having operated an adult arcade without a permit. Upon their pleas of nolo contendere, the court found them guilty. On appeal, the convictions were affirmed. Appellants asserted that Houston, Tex., Code 85-1337 ("the ordinance") violated U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV in that it was void for vagueness, overbroad, and was an impermissible prior restraint on free speech. The court had recently rejected these contentions, and similar provisions in a California ordinance had been upheld as constitutional. Appellants also asserted that the ordinance was void under Tex. Const. art. 11 § 5, and under the doctrine of preemption, because of its inconsistency with Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8814, 8817, and 2372w (1989). Under Tex. Const. art. 11, § 5, city charters may not have contained provisions inconsistent with the state constitution or with the general laws passed by the state legislature. The statutes dealt with the regulation of coin-operated machines, and the regulation of the locations of sexually oriented commercial activities. As the court had already held that the ordinance was not inconsistent with these statutes, the ordinance was not void.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and appellants' points of error were overruled. Houston City Code had not violated the First or the Fourteenth amendments, and it was, therefore, not void for vagueness, overbreadth, or as an impermissible prior restraint on free speech. The ordinance was void under the doctrine of preemption, as its provisions were not inconsistent with the state constitution or with general laws passed by the state legislature.

State v. Hanson


Nos. 10-89-018-CR, 10-89-019-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Tenth District, Waco


793 S.W.2d 270; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 311



January 25, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From 220th Judicial District Court Bosque County, Texas, Trial Court Nos. 11,277, 11,278.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of the decision of the 220th Judicial District Court, Bosque County, Texas, that quashed and dismissed two misdemeanor indictments that charged appellee county judge with attempting to coerce a public servant in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 36.03(a) (1) (1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellee county judge was the budget officer and the presiding officer over the commissioner's court. Indictments were returned against appellee for alleged coercive influence over public servants when appellee threatened to terminate funding of the salaries of two county officials in an attempt to coerce them into action within the scope of their duties. The court held that the trial court acted correctly when it quashed and dismissed the indictments. The court held that appellee's indictments under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 36.03(a)(1) and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 36.01(1) (F), which were handed down before the statutes were amended effective September 1, 1989, violated appellee's rights under U.S. Const. amend. I (the First Amendment). The court held that threats that portended lawful action were afforded First Amendment protection and the application of section 36.01(1)(F) to appellee's alleged conduct was unconstitutionally vague because of the definition of "coercion." The court held that appellee did not have fair notice of what type of threat was prohibited, and there was not a clear objective standard so that those charged with enforcement could assess conduct for legality.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trial court acted correctly when it quashed and dismissed the indictments handed down against appellee county judge. The court held that the coercion statutes as they were applied to appellee were unconstitutionally vague because they potentially punished political speech and threats that were legal and constitutionally protected.

Osborn v. Kinnington


No. 08-89-00212-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Eighth District, El Paso


787 S.W.2d 417; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 181



January 24, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 358th District Court of Ector County, Texas, Bill McCoy, Judge, (TC# D-75,265-A).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The appellant sought review of a decision by the 358th District Court of Ector County (Texas), which dismissed his action against the appellee, for injuries sustained in a vehicle accident in Texas, on the basis that the appellant and the appellee, who were co-workers, were covered by workers' compensation.


OVERVIEW: The appellant and the appellee, co-workers, drove a truck for their employer. Both individuals were residents of Alabama. The truck overturned in Texas and the appellant filed an action against the appellee in the Texas trial court in an effort to recover for his personal injuries. Thus, the court remanded the case to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the appellant's action and held that the appellant could maintain his action against the appellee in a Texas court, even though he could not maintain it in an Alabama court.

State v. Eaves


No. 07-89-0304-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


786 S.W.2d 396; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 136



January 18, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 1 OF POTTER COUNTY; NO. 52490; HONORABLE MORRIS L. OVERSTREET, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of the order of the County Court at Law No. 1 of Potter County (Texas), which granted defendant's motion to quash an information that charged him with the offense of being intoxicated on premises licensed to sell beer while he was the holder of the license in violation of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 104.01(5) (1989). The county court granted the motion on the ground that the statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by information with the offense of being intoxicated on premises licensed to sell beer while he was the holder of the license in violation of Tex. Alco. Bev. Code Ann. § 104.01(5) (1989). The trial court set aside the information on the ground that the statute creating the offense was unconstitutionally vague in violation of U.S. Const. amend. V, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19. The state filed a notice of appeal under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.01(a)(1) (1989). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the appeal on the basis that the trial court's order was not appealable because it allowed the state to amend the information. The court overruled defendant's motion, holding that the legal effect of the trial court's order setting the information aside based upon a perceived unconstitutionality of the statute was equivalent to dismissal. The court reversed the order setting aside the information, holding that the term intoxication in § 105.01(5) was not unconstitutionally vague and was sufficient to afford defendant notice of the proscribed conduct, and the court remanded the case for reinstatement of the information.


OUTCOME: The court overruled defendant's motion to dismiss the state's appeal from the trial court's order that set aside the information, holding that the order was a dismissal of the information. The court reversed the trial court's holding that the statute under which defendant was charged was unconstitutionally vague, and the court ruled that the statute provided sufficient notice of the proscribed conduct.

May v. State


No. C14-89-0243-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 68



January 11, 1990 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law No. 2, Brazos County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 1524-87.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the County Court at Law No. 2, Brazos County, Texas, which convicted him, after a jury trial, of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction, after a jury trial, for driving while intoxicated. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The trial court did not err in not declaring Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-5, §§ 3(a) and 3(b) unconstitutional. Defendant failed to show that under any circumstance could the statutes be construed as unconstitutional. The trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury on which manner of proving intoxication under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 67011-1(a)(2)(A)(B) the jury was to use. The trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury regarding consent to take a breath test and the destruction of evidence by the prosecution because the given instructions were adequate and fully protected defendant. The trial court did not err in admitting a videotape into evidence. The videotape was admissible because a police officer that participated in its recording testified to the authenticity and accuracy of the tape. There was sufficient evidence to support defendant's conviction. Based on the evidence, a rational trier of fact could have found the essential elements of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's driving while intoxicated conviction (DWI). Defendant failed to show that DWI statutes were unconstitutional. The trial court did not err in refusing to give certain jury instruction defendant requested because the given instructions were adequate and fully protected defendant. There was sufficient evidence to support defendant's DWI conviction beyond reasonable doubt.

 

1790 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Tabor v. Joe A. McDermott, Inc.


No. B14-88-00986-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourteenth District, Houston


1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 72



January 11, 1990 


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO RULE 90(i) OF THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 190th District Court, Harris County, Texas, Trial Court Cause No. 85-02403.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of a 190th District Court, Harris County (Texas), decision that granted appellee corporation's motion to strike pleadings that led to the dismissal of appellant's petition for a bill of review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant individual challenged a trial court decision that dismissed appellant's petition for a bill of review after the trial court granted appellee corporation's motion to strike the pleadings. The court affirmed the trial court decision. Appellant failed to prove the requisites of a bill of review, specifically that he had standing to bring such an action. Neither the petition nor the final judgment in the challenged original lawsuit named appellant in his individual capacity. As such, appellant had no standing to file a bill of review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a trial court decision that dismissed appellant's petition for bill of review. Appellant lacked standing to file a bill of review because he was not named in his individual capacity in the challenged original petition or lawsuit.

 

1791 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Boetscher v. State


No. 07-88-0288-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Seventh District, Amarillo


782 S.W.2d 954; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 82



January 11, 1990 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 9, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; 72nd JUDICIAL DISTRICT; NO. 88-408371; HONORABLE WILLIAM R. SHAVER, JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant ex-husband appealed from the denial of his petition for writ of habeas corpus by the District Court of Lubbock County, 72d Judicial District (Texas), wherein he sought the dismissal of a criminal nonsupport charge under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.05 (1989) and release from custody after extradition. His ex-wife had filed suit under the Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act, Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 21.01 et seq. (1986).


OVERVIEW: Ex-wife and children moved, and ex-wife filed suit against defendant ex-husband under the Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act, Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 21.01 et seq. (1986) for failure to pay child support. Defendant was indicted for criminal nonsupport and put into custody in Texas after extradition from Michigan. Defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied, and he appealed, claiming a lack of jurisdiction and claiming Tex. Penal Code § 25.05(g)(2) was unconstitutional. The appellate court affirmed. The statutory criminal nonsupport conduct had the necessary consequence, detrimental effect, and result of denying a child who was a Texas resident the support to which he was entitled to receive by a court order. The interest in protecting the viability of a child support judgment and the rights of Texas residents to have received court awarded support gave Texas jurisdiction. Moreover, extradition was proper, and the indictment sufficiently alleged all the elements of § 25.05(g)(2) to support personal jurisdiction. Section 25.05(g)(2) was not unconstitutional as applied to nonresidents under equal protection or cruel and unusual punishment analysis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant ex-husband's petition for writ of habeas corpus after he was indicted for criminal nonsupport for child support arrearages and was put into custody after extradition from Michigan. Texas had proper jurisdiction under the criminal nonsupport statute and properly protected interests of residents and support orders, and the criminal nonsupport statute was constitutional.

 

1792 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez v. State


Appeal No. 04-89-00411-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Fourth District, San Antonio


783 S.W.2d 764; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 348



January 10, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from County Court at Law No. 5 of Bexar County, Trial Court No. 412397, Honorable Timothy Johnson, Judge Presiding, Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the County Court at Law No. 5 of Bexar County (Texas), which entered his conviction for criminal trespass of a habitation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal trespass of a habitation under Texas Penal Code Ann. § 30.05 (1989) in that he entered the habitation with notice that entry was forbidden and remained without effective consent. On appeal, defendant argued that the statutory term "remain" rendered the criminal trespass statute void for vagueness because the statute did not specify how long one must "remain" to be subjected to criminal prosecution. The court applied rules of statutory construction, including Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 311.011(a) which required that the challenged term be construed according to common usage, and affirmed. The court held that the dictionary definition of "remain" made no reference to a time requirement; consequently, because a stay of any length of time after entry would satisfy the statutory "remain" requirement, the wording of the statute was sufficient in describing the conduct which it declared to be criminal. The court also held that given the wording of the criminal trespass statute, the state could present evidence of either or both "enter or remain;" and thus, even if "remain" was vague, proof of "entry" would suffice to sustain defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for criminal trespass because the statutory term "remain" was not so indefinite as to render the criminal trespass statute void for vagueness.

 

1793 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Gass v. State


Nos. 09-88-314 CR, 09-88-315 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, Ninth District, Beaumont


785 S.W.2d 834; 1990 Tex. App. LEXIS 789



January 10, 1990 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]

APPEAL FROM THE 75TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF LIBERTY COUNTY, TEXAS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from his convictions for child indecency and aggravated sexual assault, entered in the 75th Judicial District Court for Liberty County (Texas). Appellant alleged that his convictions violated due process because the statute under which he was convicted was unconstitutional and further that the trial court erred in allowing evidence of extraneous offenses and character evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant committed two sexual incidents on his granddaughter. In one incident, he exposed himself and touched her genitals and penetrated her with his genitals, while in the other incident he exposed himself and asked her to place her hand on his penis. Two days later, he admitted his transgressions to an aunt of the granddaughter. Appellant was convicted of aggravated sexual assault and child indecency. Appellant claimed that error occurred when the trial court allowed testimony about other incidents of sexual abuse both at the guilt/innocence stage and at the punishment stage. He also complained that the case should have been dismissed because the statute was unconstitutional and, additionally, he was denied due process of law. The court reviewed the record and found no error as to any of the claims made by appellant. The court noted that the extraneous offense issue was not meritorious because of an exception in cases pertaining to young children. The court also noted that there was no violation of appellant's equal protection rights or his due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellants' convictions for child indecency and aggravated sexual assault because the assertions of error did not have merit. The court further found that appellant was not denied his equal protection or due process rights.
